Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Introduction to Hanafi Fatwa Methodology: Overview of 'Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den?'
Table of contents listing chapter headings and page numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major principles and sources that govern Hanafi fatwa practice as outlined in the book's table of contents.

Core Idea
A fatwa must be based on explicit texts, not mere analogy or general maxims; custom and context matter.

This lesson provides an orientation to the structure and key topics of the book 'Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den?', which is a systematic guide to the methodology of issuing fatwas in the Hanafi school. The table of contents reveals the foundational rules, preferred sources, and practical considerations a mufti must know.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the primacy of explicit textual cases
The fihrist begins by stating that a fatwa should not be given without finding an explicit case. This establishes that the default source is clear textual evidence (nass).
2
Identify prohibited methods: analogy and general qawaid
The fihrist explicitly prohibits giving fatwa from mere analogy (nazir) and from general legal maxims (qawaid kulliya) alone. This highlights the need for direct textual support.
3
Note the hierarchy of preferred opinions
The fihrist mentions that in worship, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is mufta bih, and that a saying supported by evidence is preponderant. Also, intermediate opinions are not automatically preferred.
4
Understand the role of istihsan, mafhum, and urf
The list includes that istihsan takes precedence over qiyas, mafhum mukhalif is valid under conditions, and custom (urf) is considered and can change rulings.
5
Appreciate the practical considerations for a mufti
The fihrist emphasizes caution in matters of disbelief, the need for the mufti to understand people's circumstances, and that weak sayings can be used in necessity.

خاتمہ
How do you give a fatwa? Reason for not finding an explicit case. Do not give a fatwa from analogy. It is also not permissible to give a fatwa from general principles. Sharh Rasm al-Mufti. The method of Badaya, Bada'i, Shuruh Hidayah and Shuruh Kanz. The intermediate opinion is not the preponderant opinion. Where is it permissible to give a fatwa from analogy? Verses numbers 40 to 43. Verses numbers 44 to 52. In acts of worship, the saying of Imam A'zam is the mufta bih. The saying that is supported by evidence is the preponderant one. Verses numbers 57 to 60. Terminologies for correction of issues and their ranks. In judiciary issues, which is more confirmed between Imam Abu Yusuf's sahih and asbah? The mufta bih saying. Verses numbers 61 to 67. In issues of dhawi al-arham, ten reasons by Kutr for preferring Imam Muhammad's correction. Verse 68. The mufta bih saying is that istihsan has preference over qiyas. Regarding mafhum and its rulings, it is necessary to give fatwa according to zahir al-riwaya. The ruling of mafhum. At the time of conflicting narrations, consideration of dirayah in transactions and rational matters. Meaning of dirayah. Caution is necessary in fatwas of disbelief. The abandoned saying is like the abrogated saying. Mafhum mukhalif is valid. In fiqh expressions and sayings of the Companions, mafhum mukhalif is also valid. In shariah texts, mafhum mukhalif and the clarification of Allamah Shami. The presence of a saying in the texts is an implicit correction by Imam Muhammad. Classification of mutun, shuruh and fatawa. Khulasat al-Maram. Reliable mutun. Verses numbers 53 to 56. Mafhum mukhalif is a proof only when it does not oppose an explicit statement. Method of Fatawa Qadi Khan and Muntqa al-Abhur. Verse 69. Definitions of urf and custom. Sharbat [؟]. The discussion of urf is still incomplete. Consideration of urf and custom. Verses numbers 70 to 73. Acting upon a weak saying and fatwa. Only general custom and predominant habit are considered. Verse 74. The status of a ruling established by custom. Rulings change by change of custom and objection upon Allamah Shurunbulali. Twenty-two examples of it. Meaning of bil-wafa (footnote). What is a bathhouse? (footnote). A question and answer. Objection upon Allamah [؟]. Answer. In times of necessity, acting upon a weak saying is also permissible according to Hanafis. Matters appended to necessity. It is necessary for the mufti to be insightful and familiar with custom. Interpretation of Allamah Bir's saying. Consideration of maslahah in fatwa is necessary. A severe contradiction: the objection and its detailed answer. It is necessary for the mufti to know the conditions of people. When is it necessary to judge by a weak saying or by another madhhab? A question and answer. If custom is not against shariah, its consideration in fatwa is necessary. Rulings of general custom, specific custom, and both. Is it permissible? Conclusion.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the fihrist (table of contents) of the book 'Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den?'. It provides an overview of the topics covered, which are central to the discipline of ifta according to the Hanafi madhhab. The list begins with foundational rules such as not giving fatwa from mere analogy or general qawaid (legal maxims) without an explicit textual case. It then references commentaries like Sharh Rasm al-Mufti and other major works. Important principles are highlighted: in matters of worship, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is the mufta bih; a saying supported by evidence is preponderant; istihsan takes precedence over qiyas; fatwa must be based on zahir al-riwaya; and changes in custom (urf) can change rulings. The author also addresses topics like mafhum mukhalif, the hierarchy of texts, acting on weak sayings in necessity, and the necessity for a mufti to understand custom and circumstances. This fihrist serves as a roadmap for the systematic study of ifta rules.

Key Terms
مفہوم مخالف (Mafhum Mukhalif): A method of interpretation where the opposite meaning of a statement is considered legally valid evidence.
عرف (Urf): Customary practice that is prevalent among people and not contrary to shariah, which is considered in fatwa and legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fihrist, which of the following is explicitly prohibited as a basis for giving a fatwa?
A) Using explicit texts from the Quran and Sunnah
B) Relying on general legal maxims (qawaid kulliya)
C) Following the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa in worship
D) Considering custom (urf) in transactions

Key Takeaway
A fatwa must be grounded in explicit textual cases, avoiding reliance on general maxims or mere analogy, while incorporating custom and necessity within the Hanafi methodology.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Obligation to Follow the Rajih Opinion
Author states the rule and supports with ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rule that a mufti must follow the rajih opinion and apply it to determine permissible fatwa practice.

Core Idea
It is obligatory to follow the preferred opinion or Zahir al-Riwayah; the marjuh is impermissible in fatwa except in specific exceptions.

This passage establishes a foundational rule for muftis: it is wajib (obligatory) to follow the opinion that has been given tarjih (preferred) by the scholars of the madhhab, or if that opinion is from Zahir al-Riwayah and no alternative has been preferred. The author emphasizes that violating this rule – by issuing a fatwa based on a marjuh opinion – is generally impermissible, and he supports this with a claim of consensus (ijma). Understanding this hierarchy is critical for any mufti or student of iftaa.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the central dictum: it is wajib to follow the rajih or Zahir al-Riwayah when no tarjih has been made to the contrary.
The rule is presented in the first line: 'اعلم بأن الواجب اتباع ما ترجيحه عن أهله قد علما أو كان ظاهر الرواية ولم يرجحوا خلاف ذاك'.
2
Define key terms
Explain tarjih (preference), rajih (preferred opinion), marjuh (un-preferred opinion), and Zahir al-Riwayah (core transmitted corpus). Understand their roles in the Hanafi hierarchy.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest authority; tarjih is a scholarly process.
3
Recognize the prohibition
Understand that following a marjuh opinion is impermissible for both acting and giving fatwa, as stated: 'مرجوح قول پر نہ فتویٰ دینا جائز ہے نہ عمل کرنا'.
The prohibition is general but exceptions exist (to be covered later).
4
Note the exception
Acknowledge that the passage mentions specific circumstances where acting upon a marjuh opinion may be permissible, referenced to verse 7.
The exception is not elaborated here; it is a caveat.
5
Validate the authority
Recognize that this rule is established by ijma (consensus) reported by Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji, Ibn Hajar al-Makki, and others, making it a binding principle.
Ijma gives the rule a strong epistemological basis.

اعلم بأن الواجب اتباع ما ترجيحه عن أهله قد علما أو كان ظاهر الرواية ولم يرجحوا خلاف ذاك فاعلم ترجمہ (۹) جان لیجئے کہ اس کی پیروی واجب ہے۔ جس کی ترجیح اصحاب ترجیح کی طرف سے جانی گئی ہو۔ (۱۰) یا وہ قول ظاہر روایت ہو اور نہیں ترجیح دی ہو اصحاب ترجیح نے اس کے علاوہ قول کو پس یہ بات اچھی طرح جان لیجئے ! مرجوح قول پر نہ فتویٰ دینا جائز ہے نہ عمل کرنا: مذکورہ اشعار کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جو شخص خود عمل کرنا چا ہے یا دوسرے کو فتویٰ دینا چاہے اس کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ قول اختیار کرے جس کو علمائے مذہب نے ترجیح دی ہے۔ کیونکہ مرجوح قول پر نہ تو عمل کرنا جائز ہے نہ فتویٰ دینا۔ البتہ بعض مخصوص حالات میں مرجوح قول پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے جیسا کہ شعر نمبر ۷ والے میں آرہا ہے۔ یہ مسئلہ اجماعی ہے: اور متعدد علماء نے اس سلسلہ میں اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔ علامہ ابن حجر مکی رحمہ اللہ (۵) فتاویٰ کبری میں تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ: " زوائد الروضہ (1) میں ہے کہ مفتی کے لیے اور عمل کرنے والے کے لیے جائز نہیں ہے کہ غور و فکر کئے بغیر دو قولوں میں سے کسی بھی قول پر یا دو وجہوں میں سے کسی بھی وجہ پر فتوی دے دے یا عمل کرے اور زوائد کی بیان کردہ اس بات میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحب زوائد سے پہلے ان دونوں مسئلوں میں علامہ ابن الصلاح ( ۷ ) نے اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔ اور مالکیہ میں سے علامہ باجی (۸) نے مفتی کے بارے میں اجماع نقل کیا ہے اور علامہ قرانی (۹) کے کلام سے تو یہ مفہوم ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی اور مفتی کے لیئے خواہ وہ مجتہد فی المذہب ہوں یا مقلد محض جائز نہیں ہے کہ غیر راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ یہ فقہ شافعی کی مخصوص اصطلاح ہے۔ شوافع امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے اقوال کو روایات کہتے ہیں اور بعد کے مشائخ کے اقوال کو وجوہ" کہتے ہیں اور احناف کے یہاں ائمہ ثلاثہ کے اقوال کو روایات اور بعد کے علماء کی آراء کو اقوال کہا جاتا ہے۔ (معارف السنن ج ۱ ص ۳۳)
Know that it is obligatory to follow what whose tarjih has been known from its people; or it is Zahir al-Riwayah and they have not preferred the opposite of that, so know. Translation (9): Know that following that which is known to have been given tarjih by the people of tarjih is obligatory. (10) Or it is a statement from Zahir al-Riwayah and the people of tarjih have not preferred another statement over it, so know well! It is not permissible to give fatwa or act upon the marjuh statement. The summary of the verses is that the one who wants to act himself or give fatwa to others must choose the statement that the scholars of the madhhab have preferred. Because it is not permissible to act or give fatwa on the marjuh statement. However, in some specific circumstances there is leeway to act upon the marjuh statement, as will come in verse number 7. This issue is a matter of ijma', and many scholars have transmitted consensus on this. Allamah Ibn Hajar al-Makki (5) writes in al-Fatawa al-Kubra: 'Zawaid al-Rawdah (1) states that it is not permissible for the mufti or the practitioner to give fatwa or act upon any of two statements or any of two aspects without reflection, and there is no disagreement in what Zawaid mentioned. Before the author of Zawaid, Allamah Ibn al-Salah (7) transmitted consensus on both issues. And among the Malikis, Allamah al-Baji (8) transmitted consensus regarding the mufti. And from the words of Allamah al-Qarani (9), it is understood that it is not permissible for the judge and the mufti, whether he is a mujtahid within the madhhab or a mere muqallid, to make a decision according to an un-preferred statement. This is a specific Shafi'i terminology: Shafi'is call the statements of Imam al-Shafi'i 'riwayat' and the statements of later shaykhs 'wujuh', while in the Hanafi school, the statements of the three imams are called 'riwayat' and the views of later scholars are called 'aqwal'. (Ma'arif al-Sunan, vol. 1, p. 33)
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage presents a core methodological rule for muftis: it is obligatory (wajib) to follow an opinion that has been clearly preferred (tarjih) by the scholars of the madhhab, or if it is from Zahir al-Riwayah (the well-known transmitted corpus of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) and no alternative has been given tarjih. The author emphasizes that it is impermissible to act upon or give fatwa according to a marjuh (deemed weak) opinion. However, he notes an exception: in specific circumstances, acting upon a marjuh opinion may be permissible, a point to be elaborated later (presumably verse 7). The commentary then cites multiple authorities to establish that this ruling is a matter of consensus (ijma). Ibn Hajar al-Makki, Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji, and al-Qarani all affirmed the impermissibility of choosing any opinion without due consideration. The passage also includes a terminological clarification: in the Hanafi school, the statements of the three founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) are called 'riwayat', while later scholars' opinions are called 'aqwal'—this is contrasted with Shafi'i terminology where 'riwayat' refers to Imam al-Shafi'i's statements and 'wujuh' to later shaykhs. This rule establishes the mufti's duty to adhere to the established hierarchy of authority within the madhhab.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of weighing evidence to determine which opinion is stronger or preferred.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted corpus of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the six books).
مرجوح (marjuh): The opinion that is considered weaker or not preferred after tarjih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on giving a fatwa according to a marjuh opinion?
A) Permissible in all cases
B) Impermissible generally, with exceptions
C) Always wajib
D) Only permissible for a mujtahid

Key Takeaway
A mufti must identify and follow the preferred opinion (rajih) or Zahir al-Riwayah; acting on marjuh is impermissible unless an exception applies.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Obligation to Follow the Preponderant Opinion in the Madhhab
Establishing the rule that only the rājiḥ is followed in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the preponderant (rājiḥ) opinion in a given case and apply the rule that only the rājiḥ may be used in fatwa and action.

Core Idea
Only the preponderant (rājiḥ) opinion may be followed; acting on a marjūḥ is forbidden except in specific cases.

This lesson establishes a foundational rule for any mufti or Muslim acting upon the Hanafi madhhab: it is obligatory (wājib) to follow the preponderant opinion (rājiḥ). The passage, taken from a work on Rasm al-Mufti, cites a near-consensus among leading scholars of all schools. Understanding this rule protects the mufti from following personal desire and ensures that fatwas are based on the strongest evidence within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the core principle
Read the opening lines: the mufti or acting person must follow the saying that has been given tarjīḥ (preponderance) by the scholars of the madhhab, or that is Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and has not been outweighed.
This principle is stated as a verse in Rasm al-Mufti.
2
Understand the consensus (ijmā’)
The author lists multiple scholars (Ibn Ḥajar Makkī, Ibn al-Ṣalāḥ, al-Bājī, al-Qarāfī, etc.) who transmitted ijmā‘ that it is impermissible to give fatwa or act upon a non-rājiḥ opinion without proper consideration.
Consensus is a strong evidence in uṣūl al-fiqh.
3
Distinguish rājiḥ from marjūḥ
A rājiḥ opinion is the preponderant one; its opposite is marjūḥ (weak). The passage equates following a marjūḥ without tarjīḥ with following one's desires, which is unanimously prohibited.
Marjūḥ is treated as 'non-existent' compared to the rājiḥ.
4
Note the exception
An exception is given: when proofs are so conflicting that tarjīḥ is impossible, a mujtahid muqallid may act on any of the conflicting opinions, by consensus.
This is a limited escape for genuine cases of ta‘āruḍ (conflict).
5
Apply to fatwa practice
In practice, a mufti must research which opinion is rājiḥ (e.g., by referring to later fatwa collections or clear Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah) and base his fatwa on that. He may not pick an opinion arbitrarily.
The story of al-Bājī illustrates the importance of correcting errors in fatwa.

شروع رسم المسلحی
(فض ) الشيءُ: دینا عطا کرتا ۔ المنحه: عطیہ ۔
- اعلَمُ بِأَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ اتَّبَاعُ مَا تَرْجِيْحُهُ عَنْ أَهْلِهِ قَدْ عُلِمَا -١٠ أو كَانَ ظَاهِرَ الرّوَايَةِ وَلَمْ يُرَجَحُوا خِلافَ ذَاكَ فَاعْلَمُ - ترجمہ (۹) جان لیجئے کہ اس کی پیروی واجب ہے۔ جس کی ترجیح اصحاب ترجیح کی طرف سے جانی گئی ہو۔
(۱۰) یا وہ قول ظاہر روایت ہو اور نہیں ترجیح دی ہو اصحاب ترجیح نے اس کے علاوہ قول کو پس یہ بات اچھی طرح جان لیجئے ! مرجوح قول پر نہ فتویٰ دینا جائز ہے نہ عمل کرنا۔
مذکورہ اشعار کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جو شخص خود عمل کرنا چا ہے یا دوسرے کو فتویٰ دینا چاہے اس کے لیے ضروری ہے کہ وہ قول اختیار کرے جس کو علمائے مذہب نے ترجیح دی ہے۔ کیونکہ مرجوح قول پر نہ تو عمل کرنا جائز ہے نہ فتویٰ دینا۔ البتہ بعض مخصوص حالات میں مرجوح قول پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہے جیسا کہ شعر نمبر ۷ والے میں آرہا ہے۔
یہ مسئلہ اجماعی ہے: اور متعدد علماء نے اس سلسلہ میں اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔ علامہ ابن حجر مکی رحمہ اللہ (۵) فتاویٰ کبری میں تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ: " زوائد الروضہ (1) میں ہے کہ مفتی کے لیے اور عمل کرنے والے کے لیے جائز نہیں ہے کہ غور و فکر کئے بغیر دو قولوں میں سے کسی بھی قول پر یا دو وجہوں میں سے کسی بھی وجہ پر فتوی دے دے یا عمل کرے اور زوائد کی بیان کردہ اس بات میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحب زوائد سے پہلے ان دونوں مسئلوں میں علامہ ابن الصلاح ( ۷ ) نے اجماع نقل کیا ہے۔ اور مالکیہ میں سے علامہ باجی (۸) نے مفتی کے بارے میں اجماع نقل کیا ہے اور علامہ قرانی (۹) کے کلام سے تو یہ مفہوم ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی اور مفتی کے لیئے خواہ وہ مجتہد فی المذہب ہوں یا مقلد محض جائز نہیں ہے کہ غیر راجح قول کے مطابق فیصلہ یہ فقہ شافعی کی مخصوص اصطلاح ہے۔ شوافع امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے اقوال کو روایات کہتے ہیں اور بعد کے مشائخ کے اقوال کو وجوہ" کہتے ہیں اور احناف کے یہاں ائمہ ثلاثہ کے اقوال کو روایات اور بعد کے علماء کی آراء کو اقوال کہا جاتا ہے۔ (معارف السنن ج ۱ ص ۳۳)

شرح رسم الملتی
کریں یا فتویٰ دیں۔ کیونکہ ایسا کرنا خواہش کی پیروی کرتا ہے جو بالا جماع حرام ہے۔ اور مجتہد فی المذہب کے بارے میں علامہ قرانی کی بات کا مصداق وہ صورت ہے جب وائل میں تعارض نہ ہویا تعارض ہو مگر ترجیح ممکن ہو۔ اور اگر کسی مسئلہ میں دلائل ایسے متعارض ہوں کہ کسی طرح ترجیح ممکن نہ ہو تو اس وقت مجتہد مقلد کے لیے دوقولوں میں سے کسی بھی قول پر بالا جماع فیصلہ کرنا اور فتویٰ دینا درست ہے (فتاوی کبری کی عبارت پوری ہوئی ) اور امام محقق علامہ قاسم بن قُطلُوبُغا (۱۰) اپنی کتاب صحیح القدوری کے شروع میں تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے اپنے ائمہ ثلاثہ کے قبعین میں ایسے لوگ اپنی آنکھوں سے دیکھتے ہیں جو خواہشات پر عمل پیرا تھے۔ یہاں تک کہ میں نے بعض قاضیوں کے منھ سے یہ بات سنی ہے کہ اس میں۔ یعنی کسی بھی قول کو لے لینے میں کیا حرج ہے؟ میں نے جواب دیا کہ ہاں ! خواہش کی پیروی حرام ہے اور راج کے مقابلہ میں مرجوح کالعدم ہے اور کسی مرجح کے بغیر متعارض اقوال میں ترجیح نا جائز ہے۔" اور ابن سید الناس معمری (۱۱) نے کتاب الاصول میں لکھا ہے کہ: " جسے معلوم نہیں کہ دوقولوں میں سے اور دو وجہوں میں سے کون سا قول اور کون کی وجہ مشہور ہے تو اس کے لیے خواہش کی پیروی کرنا اور ترجیح میں غور کئے بغیر کسی بھی قول یا وجہ پر فیصلہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔"
اور امام ابو عمرو بن الصلاح آداب المفتی (۷) میں تحریر فرماتے ہیں کہ: یہ بات جان لیجئے کہ جو شخص ترجیح میں غور نہیں کرتا اور محض اتنی بات پر اکتفا کرتا ہے کہ اس کا فتویٰ یا عمل کسی بھی قول یا کسی بھی وجہ کے مطابق ہو جائے اور وہ مختلف اقوال و وجوہ میں سے جس پر چاہتا ہے عمل کرتا ہے تو وہ نادان ہے اور خرق اجماع کرتا ہے۔" اور علامہ باجی رحمہ اللہ (۸) نے یہ قصہ بیان کیا ہے کہ ان کے ساتھ ایک واقعہ پیش آیا مفتیوں نے اس سلسلہ میں جو فتونی دیا وہ باجی کے خلاف تھا۔ پھر جب باجی نے خود مسئلہ دریافت کیا تو مفتیوں نے معذرت کی کہ ہمیں معلوم نہیں تھا کہ یہ آپ کا واقعہ ہے۔ اور انہوں نے دوسری روایت پر فتوی دیا جو باجی کے موافق تھا۔ باجی کہتے ہیں کہ تمام قابل لحاظ مسلمانوں کے اجماع سے ایسا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
Begin Rasm al-Mufti. (Fadd) al-shay’: giving, granting. Al-Minhah: gift. - Know that it is obligatory to follow that whose preponderance from its people is known (9) Or it is Zahir al-Riwayah and they have not given preference to other than that, so know (10). Translation (9): Know that following it is obligatory: that whose preponderance is known from the people of preponderance. (10) Or that saying is Zahir al-Riwayah and the people of preponderance have not given preference to the other saying; so know this well! It is not permissible to give a fatwa or act upon a marjuh saying. The gist of the above verses is that a person who wants to act himself or give fatwa to another must adopt the saying that the scholars of the madhhab have given preponderance (tarjih) to. Because it is neither permissible to act upon nor give fatwa upon a marjuh saying. However, in certain specific circumstances there is scope for acting upon a marjuh saying, as will come in verse number 7. This issue is a matter of consensus (ijma’): and many scholars have transmitted consensus regarding this. Ibn Hajar Makki (5) writes in Fatawa Kubra: “In Zawaid al-Rawdah (1) it is stated that it is not permissible for a mufti or a person acting to give a fatwa or act upon any one of two sayings or any one of two wajh without consideration and reflection, and there is no difference of opinion in what Zawaid has stated. And before the author of Zawaid, Ibn al-Salah (7) transmitted consensus on both these issues. And among the Malikiyyah, al-Baji (8) transmitted consensus regarding the mufti. And from the words of al-Qarafi (9) it is understood that it is not permissible for a judge and mufti, whether they be mujtahid fil-madhhab or pure muqallid, to adjudicate or give fatwa according to a non-rajih saying. This is a specific term of Shafi’i fiqh: the Shafi’is call the sayings of Imam Shafi’i 'riwayat' and the sayings of later shaykhs 'wujuh', while the Hanafis call the sayings of the three Imams 'riwayat' and the views of later scholars 'aqwal'. (Ma’arif al-Sunan vol. 1 p. 33) … Sharh Rasm al-Mufti: … to adjudicate or give fatwa, because doing so is following desires, which is unanimously prohibited. And regarding the mujtahid fil-madhhab, the application of al-Qarafi’s words is when there is no conflict, or there is conflict but tarjih is possible. And if in a matter the proofs are so conflicting that tarjih is not possible by any means, then for the mujtahid muqallid it is valid to adjudicate and give fatwa upon any of the two sayings, by consensus. (The quote from Fatawa Kubra ends.) And Imam Muhaqqiq Allamah Qasim bin Qutlubugha (10) writes at the beginning of his book Sahih al-Quduri: “I have seen with my own eyes among those who follow the three Imams people who act according to their desires. So much so that I heard some judges saying: ‘What harm is there in this?’ – i.e., adopting any saying. I replied: ‘Yes! Following desires is forbidden, and the marjuh compared to the rajih is as if non-existent, and it is not permissible to give preference (tarjih) between conflicting sayings without a preponderance.’” And Ibn Sayyid al-Nas al-Ma’mari (11) wrote in al-Usool: “The one who does not know which of the two sayings or which of the two wujuh is well-known – it is not permissible for him to follow desires or to decide upon any saying or wajh without considering tarjih.” And Imam Abu ‘Amr bin al-Salah in Adab al-Mufti (7) writes: “Know that the one who does not reflect upon tarjih and is satisfied merely that his fatwa or action conforms to any saying or any wajh, and acts upon whichever of the different sayings and wujuh he wishes, then he is ignorant and breaches consensus.” And Allamah al-Baji (8) narrated this story: An incident occurred concerning him. The muftis gave a fatwa that was against al-Baji. Then when al-Baji himself asked about the issue, the muftis apologized, saying they did not know it was his case. And they gave a fatwa according to the other riwayah, which was in agreement with al-Baji. Al-Baji said: “Doing so is not permissible by the consensus of all Muslims whose opinion is to be considered.”
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling establishing the obligation to follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion in the madhhab. The author begins by quoting a verse from the Rasm al-Mufti poem: it is obligatory to follow what has been given tarjih by the people of tarjih, or what is Zahir al-Riwayah without the people of tarjih preferring something else. The Urdu commentary then explains that a mufti or one acting for himself must adopt the rajih saying; acting on a marjuh saying is impermissible except in specific exceptions (to be detailed later). This ruling is asserted as a matter of consensus (ijma’), supported by numerous scholars: Ibn Hajar Makki, Ibn al-Salah, al-Baji, al-Qarafi, Qasim bin Qutlubugha, Ibn Sayyid al-Nas, and Abu ‘Amr bin al-Salah. The passage also clarifies technical terms: in the Shafi’i school, ‘riwayat’ refer to Imam Shafi’i’s own sayings and ‘wujuh’ to later scholars; in the Hanafi school, ‘riwayat’ refer to the sayings of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and ‘aqwal’ to later scholars. The consensus evidence is strong: it is prohibited to follow one’s desires by picking any opinion without tarjih. However, an exception is noted: if proof texts are conflicting to such an extent that tarjih is impossible, then a mujtahid muqallid may legitimately act on any one of the conflicting sayings, by consensus. The story of al-Baji illustrates that even eminent scholars should follow the preponderant opinion; the muftis’ initial mistake of issuing a fatwa contrary to al-Baji’s own case was corrected when they became aware. Overall, the lesson is that the mufti must not be casual; he must know which opinion is rajih and base his fatwa on that.

Key Terms
مرجوح (marjūḥ): An opinion or ruling that is considered weaker, less preponderant, and is not to be followed in fatwa or action except under specific exceptions.
راجح (rājiḥ): The preponderant or stronger opinion in the madhhab, which it is wajib to follow.
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): The act of determining which opinion is preponderant over another, using established criteria of usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on giving a fatwa based on a marjuh (non-preponderant) opinion without any consideration of tarjih?
A) It is permissible, as all opinions in the madhhab are equally valid.
B) It is impermissible and constitutes following one's desires, which is haram by consensus.
C) It is permissible only for a mujtahid mutlaq.
D) It is permissible as long as the fatwa is supported by some text.

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory (wājib) to follow only the preponderant (rājiḥ) opinion in fatwa and action; the marjūḥ is not to be followed except when tarjīḥ is impossible.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Mufti vs the Qadi: Authority and the Prohibition of Weak Fatwa
Rasm al-mufti rules: mufti-qadi distinction and prohibition of marjuh fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the difference between a mufti and a qadi, and apply the rule that giving fatwa on a marjuh narration is against ijma.

Core Idea
A mufti informs; a qadi enforces. Never give fatwa from a marjuh view.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition establishes two critical principles for any mufti. First, you must understand that your role is advisory, not coercive—the qadi holds enforcement power. Second, when issuing a fatwa, you are bound to the strongest (mufta bihi) position within the school; relying on a marjuh narration is a violation of scholarly consensus. These are foundational to rasm al-mufti.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the roles
Identify the core difference between mufti and qadi as given in the text: the mufti informs of the ruling, the qadi makes it binding.
The Arabic verb 'اطلاع' (informs) vs 'لازم' (makes binding) is key.
2
Note the shared function
Both communicate the ruling, but authority differs; the mufti's opinion is not enforceable.
3
Understand 'marjuh'
A marjuh narration is one outweighed by stronger evidence within the school.
Marjuh is the opposite of raajih (preponderant).
4
Apply the rule
Issuing fatwa on a marjuh view is against ijma; explain why that is a serious transgression.
Ijma is a binding source; violating it is a major breach.
5
Note the exception
When there is no preponderance among opinions, the ruling is deferred to later explanation.
The text indicates this will be covered later (verse 66).

Source Text

اور اصول اقضیہ میں ہے کہ: ۱۶ شروع رسم السلطنتی " مفتی اور قاضی کے درمیان فرق صرف یہ ہے کہ مفتی حکم کی اطلاع دیتا ہے اور قاضی اس کو لازم کرتا ہے۔ ( یہاں علامہ قاسم بن قطلوبغا کی عبارت پوری ہوئی)۔ اس کے بعد علامہ قاسم (۱۰) نے نقل کیا ہے کہ: " مرجوح روایت کے مطابق فیصلہ کرنا یا فتویٰ دینا اجماع کے خلاف ہے۔ نوٹ: اگر مختلف اقوال میں سے کسی قول کی ترجیح موجود نہ ہو تو اس کا حکم آگے شعر نمبر ۶۶ کی شرح میں آ رہا ہے۔
And in 'Usool al-Aqdiyah' it is said: 16 Beginning of Rasm al-Sultani: 'The only difference between a mufti and a qadi is that the mufti informs of the ruling and the qadi makes it binding.' (Here ends the quote of Allamah Qasim bin Qutlubugha). After that, Allamah Qasim (10) narrated: 'Passing a judgment or giving a fatwa according to a marjuh (preponderated) narration is against consensus.' Note: If there is no preponderance among different statements, its ruling will come in the commentary of verse number 66 ahead.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a rule from the discipline of ifta. It first clarifies a foundational distinction: the mufti and qadi share the role of communicating divine rulings, but the qadi possesses the authority to enforce his ruling, a power the mufti lacks. The mufti merely informs the questioner of the law without making it binding. Then the text transmits a crucial caution from Allamah Qasim bin Qutlubugha: issuing a fatwa or judgment based on a marjuh (weaker) view is contrary to scholarly consensus (ijma). This underscores the responsibility of the mufti to rely only on the strongest positions within his school. However, an exception is noted: if no clear preponderance exists among differing opinions, the matter is deferred to later explanation. This teaches that a mufti must not arbitrarily select weak opinions; he must adhere to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.

Key Terms
مفتی (mufti): One who informs of a legal ruling without making it binding.
قاضی (qadi): One who passes binding verdicts in disputes.
مرجوح روایت (marjuh riwayah): A transmission of a ruling that has been outweighed by stronger evidence within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between a mufti and a qadi?
A) The mufti gives binding verdicts, the qadi only informs.
B) The mufti informs of the ruling, the qadi makes it binding.
C) There is no difference; both have the same function.
D) The mufti can judge and enforce, the qadi only advises.

Key Takeaway
A mufti is a non-binding legal informant; he must only give fatwa according to the preponderant (mufta bihi) view, as relying on a marjuh narration violates scholarly consensus.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Seven Levels of Hanafi Jurists (Tabaqat)
Classification of seven levels of jurists for fatwa authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the seven levels of Hanafi jurists and determine the qualifications required for each level in the context of issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy has seven levels, from absolute mujtahid to pure muqallid — only qualified jurists may issue reliable fatwas.

This lesson presents the classical Hanafi classification of jurists into seven hierarchical levels (tabaqat), which is foundational for understanding who is qualified to issue fatwas. The passage, from a work on the rules of the mufti, defines each level's authority and warns against the lowest level of pure imitation. By the end, you will be able to place any Hanafi scholar within this hierarchy and assess the reliability of their legal opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall structure
Read the passage and list the seven levels in order: from level 1 (mujtahid mutlaq) to level 7 (muqallid mahd). Note the Arabic names and their translations.
The levels progress from highest ijtihad to pure taqlid.
2
Examine each level's role and examples
For each level, extract: (a) the designation, (b) the degree of ijtihad/taqlid, (c) the key scholars given as examples, and (d) their function in fatwa (e.g., deriving rulings, preferring narrations, distinguishing strengths).
Focus on the specific wording: 'مجتہد مطلق', 'مجتہد فی المذہب', etc.
3
Understand the progression of authority
Observe how authority decreases from level 1 to level 7. Level 1 can derive directly from sources; level 2 follows the imam's principles but may differ in particulars; level 3 deduces for new issues; level 4 extracts from ambiguous statements; level 5 prefers among existing narrations; level 6 distinguishes strong from weak; level 7 merely collects.
This hierarchy determines who may issue a fatwa and how it is weighted.
4
Analyze the warning about level 7
Read the description of the muqallid mahd (pure imitator) and the warning: they cannot distinguish between sound and unsound rulings, and their fatwas are unreliable. Understand why the author compares them to 'gathering sticks at night'.
This is a caution against unqualified fatwa-giving.
5
Apply the hierarchy to hypothetical scholars
Given a description of a scholar's method (e.g., 'always prefers the easier ruling without checking sources'), determine their level. Use the definitions to justify your answer.
Practice placing contemporary or historical figures within this framework.

مجتہدین فی المذہب کا ہے جیسے امام ابو یوسف (۱۴) امام محمد (۱۵) اور امام اعظم کے دوسرے تلامذہ جو اپنے استاذ کے مقرر کردہ اصول و ضوابط کی روشنی میں ادلہ اربعہ سے احکام مستنبط کرنے پر پوری طرح قادر ہیں۔ ان حضرات نے اگر چہ بعض جزئیات میں اپنے استاذ کی مخالفت کی ہے مگر اصول میں وہ اپنے استاذ کی پیروی کرتے ہیں۔

اصحاب تخریج کا ہے۔ یہ حضرات مقلد ہوتے ہیں ۔ مثلاً جصاص رازی (۲۳) اور ان کے ہم رتبہ حضرات ۔ ان حضرات میں اجتہاد کی صلاحیت مطلق نہیں ہوتی مگر چونکہ یہ حضرات اصول کو اچھی طرح محفوظ کئے ہوئے ہوتے ہیں اور ان اصول کے مآخذ سے بھی

ان مسائل کی تفصیل کی ہے۔
پانچواں طبقہ:
اصحاب ترجیح کا ہے۔ یہ حضرات بھی مقلد ہوتے ہیں ۔ ان میں بھی اجتہاد کی مطلق صلاحیت نہیں ہوتی ۔ جیسے قدوری (۲۴) صاحب ہدایہ (۱) اور انہی جیسے دوسرے حضرات ان فقہاء کا کام مختلف روایتوں میں سے کسی ایک روایت کو ترجیح دیتا ہے۔ جس کے لیے عام طور پر یہ تعبیرات اختیار کی جاتی ہیں ۔ (۱) ہذا اولی ( یہ بہتر ہے ) (۲) ہذا اصبح روایہ (اس کی روایت زیادہ صحیح ہے ) (۳) ہذا اوضح ( یہ دلائل کے اعتبار سے زیادہ واضح ہے ) (۴) ہذا اوفق للقياس ( یہ قیاس سے زیادہ ہم آہنگ ہے ) (۵) ہذا ارفق للناس ( اس میں لوگوں کے لیے
زیادہ سہولت ہے )
چھٹا طبقہ:
اصحاب تمییز کا ہے۔ یہ حضرات بھی مقلد ہوتے ہیں۔ مگر اقویٰ قومی اور ضعیف کے درمیان امتیاز کر سکتے ہیں۔ نیز ظاہر روایت ظاہر مذہب اور روایت نادرہ کے درمیان فرق کر سکتے ہیں مثلاً متون معتبرہ کنز مختار وقایہ اور مجمع کے مصنفین (۲۵) ان حضرات کا کام یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنی کتابوں میں مردود اقوال اور ضعیف روایتیں نقل نہ کریں۔
ساتواں طبقہ:
ان فقہاء کا ہے جو مقلد محض ہوتے ہیں اور جو مختلف اقوال میں تمیز بھی نہیں کر سکتے ۔ نہ کار آمد اور نکمے کے درمیان امتیاز کر سکتے ہیں۔ نہ دائیں بائیں میں فرق کر سکتے ہیں بلکہ جو کچھ مل جاتا ہے سب اپنی کتابوں میں جمع کر لیتے ہیں۔ ان کا حال رات میں لکڑیاں چننے والے جیسا ہے اور ان لوگوں کے لیے بڑی خرابی ہے جو ان کی تقلید کرتے ہیں ( ابن کمال
How do you give a fatwa? There are seven levels (grades). First level: It is for absolute mujtahideen, who have performed ijtihad in the Shariah, for example the four Imams (13) and those mujtahideen who followed their path. They established the foundations of the principles of fiqh and deduced legal rulings from the four evidences: Quran, Hadith, Ijma, and Qiyas, without taqlid of anyone. Second level: ...... It is for mujtahideen within the madhhab, like Imam Abu Yusuf (14), Imam Muhammad (15), and other students of the Great Imam, who are fully capable of deducing rulings from the four evidences in light of the principles and rules set by their teacher. Although they opposed their teacher in some subsidiary matters, in principles they follow their teacher. Third level: It is for mujtahideen in specific issues. For issues where no narration is transmitted from the Great Imam and his students, they state rulings through their own ijtihad. For example, Khassaf (16), Tahawi (17), Karakhi (18), Tawani (19), Sarkhasi (20), Bazdawi (21), Qadi Khan (22), etc. They cannot oppose the Great Imam in principles nor in subsidiary matters. However, keeping in view the principles and rules established by the Great Imam, they can deduce rulings for those issues about which no saying is transmitted from the Great Imam. Fourth level: It is for the people of takhrij (extraction). These are muqallids. For example, Jassas al-Razi (23) and those of his rank. They do not have absolute capacity for ijtihad, but because they have thoroughly preserved the principles and are acquainted with their sources, they can detail and specify an ambiguous (?) statement transmitted from the master of the madhhab or one of his mujtahid students, or a ruling with two possibilities, using their innate ability, keeping the principles of their imam in view, and analogizing from parallels and similar cases. What occasionally appears in al-Hidayah such as 'thus in the takhrij of al-Karakhi' and 'thus in the takhrij of al-Razi' means this: Imam al-Karakhi and Imam al-Jassas al-Razi detailed these issues. Fifth level: It is for the people of tarjih (preference). These are also muqallids. They also do not have absolute capacity for ijtihad. For example, al-Quduri (24), the author of al-Hidayah (1), and others like them. The work of these jurists is to prefer one narration over others. For this, generally these expressions are used: (1) Hadha awla (This is better), (2) Hadha asbah riwayah (This narration is more correct), (3) Hadha awdah (This is clearer in terms of evidence), (4) Hadha awfaq li'l-qiyas (This is more consistent with analogy), (5) Hadha arfaq li'l-nas (This is more convenient for people). Sixth level: It is for the people of tamyiz (distinction). These are also muqallids. But they can distinguish between the stronger and the weaker statement. Also they can differentiate between the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), the apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab), and the rare narration (riwayah nadirah). For example, the authors of the reliable texts Kanz, Mukhtar, Wiqayah, and Majma' (25). Their work is to not transmit rejected statements and weak narrations in their books. Seventh level: It is for those jurists who are pure muqallids and cannot distinguish between different statements, nor differentiate between useful and useless, nor tell right from left. Rather, they collect whatever they find into their books. Their state is like that of a person gathering sticks at night. Great harm awaits those who imitate them (Ibn Kamal).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents the seven levels (tabaqat) of jurists in the Hanafi madhhab, a fundamental classification for determining who is qualified to issue fatwas. The first level is the absolute mujtahid (mujtahid mutlaq), who derives rulings directly from the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas without following any particular madhhab. Examples include the four founders of the major schools. The second level is the mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi'l-madhhab), such as Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. They follow the principles of their imam but may differ in subsidiary issues. The third level is the mujtahid in specific issues (mujtahid fi'l-masa'il), who, using the principles of the madhhab, deduces rulings for issues not explicitly addressed by the founding imams. Scholars like Karakhi and Qadi Khan belong here. The fourth level (ashab al-takhrij) are muqallids who can extract and detail rulings by extending principles to ambiguous texts. The fifth level (ashab al-tarjih) prefer one existing narration over another using criteria such as textual strength or ease for the people. The sixth level (ashab al-tamyiz) distinguish between strong and weak narrations, and ensure they only transmit reliable material. Finally, the seventh level consists of pure imitators who indiscriminately compile everything and are warned against; their fatwas are unreliable. This hierarchy underscores the importance of authority and qualification in ifta.

Key Terms
مجتہد مطلق (mujtahid mutlaq): A jurist who derives rulings directly from the primary sources (Quran, Hadith, Ijma, Qiyas) without following any specific madhhab.
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi'l-madhhab): A jurist who follows the principles of a specific imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) but may differ in subsidiary issues.
مجتہد فی المسائل (mujtahid fi'l-masa'il): A jurist who deduces rulings for new issues not directly addressed by the founding imam, using the madhhab's principles.
اصحاب تخریج (ashab al-takhrij): Jurists who extract and detail rulings by applying the madhhab's principles to ambiguous or unresolved statements.
اصحاب ترجیح (ashab al-tarjih): Jurists who prefer one narration or ruling over others within the madhhab based on certain criteria.
اصحاب تمییز (ashab al-tamyiz): Jurists who distinguish between strong (qawi) and weak (da'if) narrations, and between apparent and rare transmissions.
مقلد محض (muqallid mahd): A pure imitator who has no ability to distinguish between sound and unsound rulings, merely collecting whatever he finds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which level of Hanafi jurists are permitted to deduce rulings for issues not directly mentioned by the founding imam, as long as they follow his principles?
A) Mujtahid mutlaq (absolute mujtahid)
B) Mujtahid fi'l-madhhab (mujtahid within the madhhab)
C) Mujtahid fi'l-masa'il (mujtahid in specific issues)
D) Ashab al-tarjih (people of preference)

Key Takeaway
The seven-level hierarchy of Hanafi jurists determines who is qualified to issue fatwas, with only levels 1-6 being reliable and level 7 (muqallid mahd) warned against.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
The Fifth to Seventh Tabaqat: Ashab al-Tarjih, Ashab al-Tamyiz, and Pure Muqallids
Describes the classification of jurists from preference-givers to pure imitators, with scholarly critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of the fifth, sixth, and seventh tabaqat of Hanafi jurists and evaluate the later critiques of Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification.

Core Idea
Hanafi jurists are hierarchically ranked; not all muqallids are equal—some can prefer, some can distinguish, some merely collect.

The Hanafi school has a structured hierarchy of jurists. This lesson covers the last three levels described by Ibn Kamal Pasha: those who give preference (Ashab al-Tarjih), those who distinguish (Ashab al-Tamyiz), and pure muqallids. We also examine scholarly critiques of specific placements, revealing the nuance of these categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels and their key abilities
Read the descriptions of the fifth, sixth, and seventh tabaqat. Note what each level can do: the fifth (Ashab al-Tarjih) can prefer between narrations; the sixth (Ashab al-Tamyiz) can distinguish stronger from weaker; the seventh (pure muqallids) cannot distinguish anything.
These are all muqallids, but their capacities vary.
2
Map the standard expressions used by Ashab al-Tarjih
List the five expressions given in the text: هٰذا أولى، هٰذا أصح رواية، هٰذا أوضح، هٰذا أوفق للقياس، هٰذا أرفق للناس. Understand when each might be used.
These expressions formalize the act of tarjih within the madhhab.
3
Distinguish between Zahir al-Riwaya, Zahir al-Madhhab, and Riwayah Nadira
The sixth level can differentiate these three. Define each: Zahir al-Riwaya is the transmitted corpus of Imam Muhammad; Zahir al-Madhhab is the relied-upon view; Riwayah Nadira are rare/rejected narrations.
This distinction is critical for fatwa reliability.
4
Analyze the critiques of Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification
Read the 'Benefit' (fa'idah) section. Identify the three objections: (1) Sahibayn placed too low, (2) Khasaf/Tahawi/Karakhi placed too low, (3) Jassas placed too low. Understand the Hanafi responses, especially al-Lakhnawi's explanation for Sahibayn.
The critique shows that classification is not absolute; actual scholarly merit may exceed the assigned level.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a practical scenario
Given a fatwa situation with conflicting narrations, determine which level of jurist would be competent to resolve it: e.g., if a mufti needs to prefer one riwayah over another, he must be at least of the fifth level.
This reinforces the practical importance of the hierarchy.

لیے علامہ ابن کمال پاشا کی یہ عبارت قدرے اختصار کے ساتھ علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے رد المختار ج 1۔ ص ۵۷ - مطلب فی طبقات الفقہاء میں بھی نقل کی ہے۔
یعنی ترجیح اور اصحاب ترجیح کے سلسلہ میں ۱۲ سے علامہ کفوی نے پانچ طبقے کئے ہیں دیکھیے مقدمہ عمدۃ الرعایہ۔ انہوں نے پہلی اور آخری قسمیں چھوڑ دی ہیں اور علاقی رحمہ اللہ نے در مختار میں مجتہد مطلق کے علاوہ سات طبقات کئے ہیں ۱۲۔
Fifth level: Ashab al-Tarjih. These persons are also muqallids. They also do not have absolute capability of ijtihad. Like al-Quduri (24) and the author of al-Hidayah (1) and other such scholars. The work of these jurists is to give preference to one of the various narrations. For this, generally these expressions are adopted: (1) Hādha awlā (this is better), (2) Hādha asahh riwāyah (this narration is more correct), (3) Hādha awdah (this is clearer in terms of proofs), (4) Hādha awfaqu lil-qiyās (this is more in harmony with analogy), (5) Hādha arfaqu li-l-nās (this has more ease for the people).
Sixth level: Ashab al-Tamyiz. These persons are also muqallids, but they can distinguish between stronger and weaker. Also they can differentiate between zahir al-riwaya, zahir al-madhhab, and riwayah nadira. For example, the authors of the reliable texts Kanz, Mukhtar, Wiqayah, and Majma (25). The work of these persons is that they do not transmit rejected statements and weak narrations in their books.
Seventh level: Those jurists who are pure muqallids and cannot distinguish between various statements. They cannot differentiate between useful and useless. They cannot tell left from right. Rather, whatever they find, they collect all in their books. Their condition is like one who gathers sticks in the night. And great harm is for those who follow them (Ibn Kamal Pasha).
[Page 20]
(Allamah Ibn Kamal Pasha's statement is complete; some text in between has been omitted, and further discussion will come later.)
Benefit: The classification of jurists that Allamah Ibn Kamal Pasha (12) made has been viewed with approval by scholars, but they have criticized the examples given for each level. For example: (1) He counted the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the second level, while these two possessed capabilities of the level of absolute mujtahid. Maulana Abdul Hayy al-Lakhnawi (26) answered this objection in the introduction to his Hashiyah 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on Sharh al-Wiqayah: 'The truth is that these two were absolute mujtahids. Both had attained the rank of absolute ijtihad, but out of respect for their teacher and extreme politeness, they adopted the principles of their teacher and followed his path. They engaged in the dissemination, support, and reinforcement of his madhhab and ascribed themselves to him. Therefore, they were counted as mujtahid fi al-madhhab instead of absolute mujtahid.' (2) He counted Imam Khasaf, Imam Tahawi, and Imam Karakhi in the third level, while their rank is higher than that, because they have differed from Imam al-A'zam in many issues, as is seen from fiqh and ikhtilaf books. (3) He diminished the rank of Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi, placing him in the fourth level, while he was superior to those of the third level—like al-Halwani and Qadi Khan—in both time and knowledge. (Quoting H. al-Hazrat Mufti Sayyid Mahdi Hasan Shahjahanpuri) ... For this reason, Allamah Ibn Kamal Pasha's statement has been quoted with some brevity by Allamah al-Shami in Radd al-Muhtar, vol. 1, p. 57 (Matalib fi Tabaqat al-Fuqaha). Also, Allamah al-Kafwi has made five levels regarding tarjih and Ashab al-Tarjih; see Muqaddimah 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. He omitted the first and last categories. And Allaqi in Durr al-Mukhtar made seven levels besides the absolute mujtahid.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a classification of jurists (fuqaha) into hierarchical levels (tabaqat), specifically the fifth, sixth, and seventh levels, followed by a benefit discussing critiques of Ibn Kamal Pasha's allocation of scholars to those levels. The passage proceeds as follows:

First, the author describes the fifth level: Ashab al-Tarjih (those who give preference). These jurists are muqallids (followers of an imam) but do not have absolute ijtihad. However, they can prefer one narration over another using standard expressions like 'this is better' or 'this narration is more correct.' The examples given include al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani).

Second, the sixth level: Ashab al-Tamyiz (those who distinguish). These jurists can differentiate between stronger and weaker narrations, and between the authoritative transmission (zahir al-riwaya and the madhhab's preferred view) and rare narrations (riwayah nadira). They are careful to avoid transmitting weak or rejected statements. Examples include authors of reliable texts like Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah, and Majma'.

Third, the seventh level: pure muqallids who indiscriminately collect everything without judgment. Ibn Kamal Pasha compares them to someone gathering sticks at night, emphasizing the danger of following them.

Then the passage presents a 'benefit' (fa'idah) that critiques Ibn Kamal Pasha's examples. While his general classification is accepted, scholars objected to his placement of specific scholars: (1) The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan) were placed in the second level, but they were capable of absolute ijtihad; the response by Maulana Abdul Hayy al-Lakhnawi explains that they voluntarily restricted themselves to their teacher's fiqh out of respect. (2) Imam al-Khasaf, Tahawi, and Karakhi were placed in the third level, whereas they often differed from Abu Hanifa, indicating a higher rank. (3) Abu Bakr al-Jassas al-Razi was placed in the fourth level, though he was superior to al-Halwani and Qadi Khan.

The passage concludes by noting that Allamah al-Shami reproduced Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification in Radd al-Muhtar, and that other scholars like al-Kafwi and Allaqi have different numbers of levels.

Key Terms
اصحاب ترجیح (Aṣḥāb al-Tarjīḥ): Those who can prefer between conflicting narrations using standard expressions; they are muqallids without absolute ijtihad.
اصحاب تمییز (Aṣḥāb al-Tamyīz): Those who can distinguish between stronger and weaker narrations, and between Zahir al-Riwaya, Zahir al-Madhhab, and Riwayah Nadira.
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The transmitted corpus of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani in six books, forming the relied-upon position of the madhhab.
روایت نادرہ (Riwāyah Nādirah): Rare or weak narrations that are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah; generally not relied upon for fatwa.
مقلد محض (Muqallid Mahḍ): A pure follower who cannot distinguish between different statements or narrations; indiscriminately collects whatever he finds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which level of jurists (fuqaha) are able to distinguish between stronger and weaker narrations but still remain muqallids?
A) Ashab al-Tarjih
B) Ashab al-Tamyiz
C) Pure muqallids (seventh level)
D) Mujtahid mutlaq

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's hierarchy of jurists ensures that fatwa is given by appropriately qualified scholars; understanding these ranks is essential for proper ifta.

Weak Books for Fatwa: The Rasm al-Mufti Rule
Lists unreliable fatwa sources and the condition for their use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the books listed as weak for fatwa and apply the condition that a fatwa from them is permissible only after verifying the original source (manqul 'anhu).

Core Idea
A mufti must verify the original source before using a weak book; abridged works are unreliable without consulting commentaries.

In the Hanafi tradition, not every book has the same authority for issuing fatwas. This passage from the Rasm al-Mufti identifies specific works whose authors or contents are unreliable, or which are too abridged to be used directly. Understanding this rule protects a mufti from making errors based on incomplete or transmitted weak statements. The key is the condition: a weak book may be used only if the original source (manqul 'anhu) is known and the ruling can be traced back to a reliable text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the List of Weak Books
Read the passage and note each book's title and author. They include commentaries on Kanz and Nuqaya, all books of Quniya's author, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Nabr al-Fa'iq, Ramz al-Haqa'iq, and later additions like al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Memorize these titles to avoid reliance on them without verification.
2
Extract the Condition for Use
The passage states that giving fatwa from these books is not permissible unless the original source (manqul 'anhu) is known. This means the statement must be traceable back to a reliable Zahir al-Riwayah text or its authoritative commentary.
The condition is derived from the quote of Sheikh Salih al-Jeneini.
3
Understand the Rationale
Books are considered weak due to unknown author, transmission of weak statements, or excessive abridgment. Abridgments risk misunderstanding without consulting full commentaries. The rule ensures the fatwa is based on sound, complete evidence.
This rationale applies even to famous works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرع رسم الملتی
ضعیف کتابیں:
علامہ محمد ہستہ اللہ علی الاشباہ کی شرح کے شروع میں لکھتے ہیں کہ: فتوئی کے تعلق سے ضعیف کتابیں یہ ہیں۔ کنز کی شرح ملا سکین، نقایہ کی شرح قہستانی کیونکہ ان دونوں کتابوں کے مصنفین کا حال معلوم نہیں۔ قنیہ کے مصنف کی تمام کتابیں کیونکہ وہ اپنی کتابوں میں ضعیف اقوال نقل کرتے ہیں، علامہ حصکفی کی در مختار، علامہ عمر بن نجیم کی کنز کی شرح النبر الفائق، بخاری کے شارح علامہ عینی کی کنز کی شرح رمز الحقائق۔ مؤخر الذکر تینوں کتابیں مختصر ہونے کی وجہ سے مفتی بہ کتابوں میں شامل کرنے کے قابل نہیں ہیں۔" شیخ صالح جینینی فرماتے ہیں کہ: مذکورہ کتابوں سے فتوی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ الا یہ کہ منقول عنہ کا علم ہو جائے یعنی ان کے مآخذ کا پتہ چل جائے۔" بعلی کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے ان سے اسی طرح سنا ہے اور وہ علم فقہ کے مشہور علامہ تھے اور جو کچھ انہوں نے فرمایا ہے اس کی ذمہ داری انہیں پر ہے ( شرح اشباہ کی عبارت پوری ہوئی )
فائدہ
علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے رد الختمار (ص۵۲ - ج۱) میں فتویٰ کے لیے ناقابل کتابوں میں علامہ ابن نجیم مصری رحمہ اللہ کی الاشباہ والنظائر کو بھی شامل کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی عبارتیں بے حد مختصر ہیں اس لیے شروح یا مآخذ سے رجوع کیے بغیر ان کا مطلب سمجھنے میں غلطی ہو سکتی ہے اور مولی برکلی نے قدوری کی شرح السراج الوہاج کو بھی ضعیف اور غیر معتبر کتابوں میں شمار کیا ہے؟ ( کشف الظنون ج ۲ ص ۱۶۳۱)
Chapter on the Custom of the Mufti
Weak books: Allama Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, writes at the beginning of his commentary on al-Ashbah: 'The weak books regarding fatwa are these: the commentary on Kanz by Mulla Sakin, the commentary on Nuqaya by Qahistani, because the condition of the authors of these two books is unknown; all the books of the author of Quniya, because he transmits weak statements in his books; al-Durr al-Mukhtar by Allama Hasakfi; al-Nabr al-Fa'iq, the commentary on Kanz by Allama Umar ibn Nujaym; Ramz al-Haqa'iq, the commentary on Kanz by Allama Ayni, the commentator of Bukhari. The last three books, due to being abridged, are not worthy of being included among the relied-upon books for fatwa.' Sheikh Salih al-Jeneini says: 'It is not permissible to give fatwa from the mentioned books, unless the source of transmission is known, i.e., their reference is found.' Ba'li says: 'I heard from him likewise, and he was a famous scholar of fiqh, and whatever he said, the responsibility is upon him.' (The statement from the commentary on al-Ashbah is complete).
Benefit: Allama Shami, may Allah have mercy on him, in Radd al-Mukhtar (vol. 1, p. 52) included among the books not suitable for fatwa also al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Allama ibn Nujaym al-Misri, because its expressions are extremely abridged, so without referring to commentaries or sources, misunderstanding its meaning is possible. And Mawla Barkali also counted al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the commentary on al-Quduri, among weak and unreliable books? (Kashf al-Zunun vol. 2, p. 1631)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) identifying which books a mufti should avoid when issuing fatwas. It begins by stating that weak books are those whose authors' reliability is unknown, or the authors themselves transmit weak opinions. Specifically mentioned are the commentaries on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Mulla Sakin and on Nuqaya by Qahistani. All works of the author of al-Quniya (a Hanafi text) are also considered weak because he includes weak narrations. Three well-known later works—al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Nabr al-Fa'iq, and Ramz al-Haqa'iq—are deemed unreliable for fatwa due to their abridged nature. The rule is that giving fatwa from these books is not permissible unless one verifies the original source (manqul 'anhu). This condition is emphasized by Sheikh Salih al-Jeneini and confirmed by Ba'li. The fiqh principle here is that a fatwa must be based on texts that are both authentic and properly understood; abridged works can lead to error. The 'Benefit' (fa'ida) adds that even the famous work al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym is included in this category for its brevity, and similarly al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is considered unreliable. This teaches the mufti to prioritize original, comprehensive references and to avoid relying solely on convenient but insufficient abridgments.

Key Terms
ضعیف کتاب (da'if kitab): A book that is not reliable for issuing fatwas due to the unknown status of its author, transmission of weak statements, or excessive abridgment.
مفتی بہ (mufta bihi): The relied-upon position in the madhhab that is used for giving fatwas.
منقول عنہ (manqul 'anhu): The original source from which a statement or ruling is transmitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is never allowed.

C) It is allowed only if the original source (manqul 'anhu) is known.
D) It is allowed if the book is widely used.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only use weak books after verifying the original source; abridged works are not reliable for direct fatwa.

Warning Against Copying Errors from Books
First example of a common textual error in fiqh works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a common textual error in fiqh works and apply the mufti's duty to verify original sources before issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
A copy of a copy is not a proof; always verify the original source.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq draws attention to a dangerous practice: when later scholars copy mistakes from earlier works without checking. For a mufti, this is a critical methodological rule: never rely on secondary citations alone. The source itself must be inspected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Read the passage and identify the problem described: an author makes an error, and later scholars copy it without correction.
2
Locate the Warning
Find the warning by Ibn Nujaym al-Misri in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Understand that this is a well-known principle among later Hanafi jurists.
Ibn Nujaym is a major authority in the later Hanafi school.
3
Understand the Consequence
Recognize the consequence: the error propagates widely, and many people may act upon a mistaken ruling.
This violates the duty of the mufti to ensure correctness.
4
Apply the Rule
Formulate the rule: a mufti must verify the original source before relying on a citation. Do not assume later works are always accurate.
This is part of rasm al-mufti (the mufti's method).
5
Reflect on the Example
Consider the specific example from Kanz al-Daqa'iq about suspending contracts on conditions. Use it as a cautionary tale.
Apply the rule to your own study habits.

The beginning of the name of the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq... in the book of sales, chapter on miscellaneous topics, where the discussion is about what things can be suspended on a condition and what cannot. Ibn Nujaym al-Misri (31) warned about such an error: 'It often happens that an author mentions something erroneously in his book, then later scholars come and copy that exact phrase without change or warning, so many people copy it while its single source is mistaken, as happened in this topic.' (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 2, p. 185) It often happens that an author mistakenly mentions something in his book, then later scholars copy that phrase exactly, neither correcting it nor alerting to the error, then many others copy it, while the first writer had committed an error, as happened in the topic under discussion.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage presents an example of a common error in fiqh literature. The author points out that when a mistake appears in a foundational book, later scholars often copy it without verification, leading to widespread propagation of error. He cites Ibn Nujaym's warning from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The lesson for a mufti is to always verify original sources and not rely solely on later copies or citations. This is a methodological rule in the science of ifta.

Key Terms
المؤلف (al-mu'allif): The author of a book, who may inadvertently introduce an error.
الناقل (al-naqil): The transmitter or copyist, who may propagate an error if he does not verify.
الغلط / الخطأ (al-ghalat / al-khata'): An error or mistake in the text.
التنبيه (al-tanbih): Alerting the reader to a potential error or correction.

Correcting a Mistaken Fatwa: Ijarah for Recitation vs. Teaching
Rasm al-Mufti: correcting an erroneous fatwa on ijarah for recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti principle to identify the correct mufta bih view in a disputed issue, specifically distinguishing between ijarah for teaching vs. mere recitation of the Qur'an.

Core Idea
A mufta bih for teaching Qur'an does not extend to recitation; generality in fatwa leads to error.

This passage illustrates a critical lesson for muftis: the danger of transmitting rulings without verifying their exact scope. The author corrects a common error where a mufta bih view on ijarah for teaching the Qur'an was incorrectly applied to mere recitation. This lesson will help you apply the principles of fatwa hierarchy to avoid similar mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed mufta bih
Read the passage and note the mistaken view: that hiring for any act related to the Qur'an is permissible. Identify the original source they claimed (al-Jawharah, Sharh al-Siraj).
The error is not in the source but in its interpretation.
2
Verify the exact wording from reliable texts
Check the actual text of al-Jawharah and Hidayah. The passage shows that the correct wording refers to teaching, not mere recitation. Note the difference between 'تعلیم' (teaching) and 'تلاوت' (recitation).
Al-Haddadi cited Hidayah which states the chosen view is impermissibility for recitation at graves.
3
Distinguish between general and specific rulings
Identify that the permissibility for teaching is a specific ruling (خصوصل) that cannot be generalized to all acts of worship. The principle that 'acts of worship are not subject to ijarah' is the general rule.
The Hanafi school has two principles: ijarah on acts of worship is invalid, except for teaching Qur'an due to necessity.
4
Apply the rasm al-mufti hierarchy
Rank the sources: Hidayah (mukhtar) over later generalizations. The mufta bih for recitation is the chosen view (مختار) of impermissibility as per al-Haddadi's transmission.
Later scholars who claimed permissibility for all acts of worship made a grave error in fatwa.
5
Conclude with the correct mufta bih
State the correct ruling: ijarah for teaching Qur'an is permissible (mufta bih); ijarah for mere recitation is not permissible (mukhtar). Avoid generalizing without explicit text.
This case shows why a mufti must verify the exact wording and scope of relied-upon opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسری مثال: محض تلاوت قرآن کے لیے کسی کو اجرت پر لینا درست ہے یا نہیں؟ قدروری کی شرح السراج الوہاج (۳۸) اور الجوہرۃ النیر (۳۸) میں ہے کہ : " مفتی بہ قول یہ ہے کہ اجرت پر لینا درست ہے۔ حالانکہ وہ النا سمجھ گئے ہیں اصل مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ "مفتی بہ قول یہ ہے کہ تعلیم قرآن کے لئے کسی کو اجرت پر لینا درست ہے محض تلاوت پر اجارہ درست نہیں ہے۔ سراج و باج تو ابھی تک غیر مطبوعہ ہے۔ اس کا قلمی نسخہ بھی ہمارے پاس نہیں ہے البتہ الجو ہر ہ مطبوعہ اور متداول ہے اس میں وہ بات مجھے نہیں ملی جو علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ اس کی طرف منسوب کر رہے ہیں بلکہ کتاب الا جارہ میں صراحت ہے کہ مفتی بہ قول تعلیم قرآن پر اجارہ کے جواز کا ہے۔ حدادی نے اس مسئلہ میں اپنی طرف سے کچھ کہنے کے بجائے ہدایہ جس ۲۸۷ ) کی عبارت نقل کی ہے اور بحث کے آخری میں لکھا ہے کہ واختلفوا في الاستيجار على قراءة القرآن على القبر مدة معلومة ، قال بعضهم: لا يجوز، وهو المختار ( جو بہ وج اص ۲۷۳ مجتبائی ) اس عبارت میں تصریح ہے کہ محض تلاوت کے بارے میں مختار قول عدم جواز کا ہے ۔ ۱۲
پھر حدادی کے بعد جو لوگ آئے انہوں نے حدادی کی پیروی کی اور ان کی بات نقل کرتے چلے گئے۔ حالانکہ وہ صریح غلطی تھی بلکہ بہت سے حضرات نے تو یہ کہدیا کہ فتوئی اس پر ہے کہ تمام عبادتوں پر اجارہ درست ہے . یہ سب حضرات مسئله عموم و اطلاق کے ساتھ لکھتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ یہ متاخرین کی رائے ہے اور بعض لوگ اس پر یہ مسئلہ بھی متفرع کرتے ہیں کہ حج کے لیے بھی اجارہ درست ہے یہ سب باتیں غلط ہیں اور پہلی غلطی سے بھی زیادہ سنگین ہیں ۔
Second example: Is it valid to hire someone solely for recitation of the Qur'an? In the commentary of Quduri on al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawharat al-Nayyira, it is stated: 'The mufta bih (relied-upon) view is that hiring is valid.' However, they misunderstood. The original issue is that the mufta bih view is that hiring for teaching the Qur'an is valid; hiring for mere recitation is not valid. Al-Siraj and al-Baj are still unpublished. We don't have the manuscript. However, al-Jawharah is published and available, and I did not find that statement in it which 'Allamah al-Shami attributed to it. Rather, in the book of ijarah there is explicit statement that the mufta bih view is the permissibility of ijarah for teaching the Qur'an. Al-Haddadi, instead of saying something himself, cited the text of Hidayah (vol. 2, p. 287) and wrote at the end of the discussion: 'They differed regarding hiring for recitation of the Qur'an at the grave for a specified period. Some said it is not permissible, and that is the chosen view.' (Jawhara?) This text clearly states that the chosen view regarding mere recitation is impermissibility. Then after Haddadi, those who came followed him and continued to transmit his statement, even though it was a clear error. Many people even said that the fatwa is that ijarah for all acts of worship is valid. These people write with generality and claim it is the view of the later scholars, and some even derive from it that ijarah for Hajj is also valid. All these statements are wrong, even more serious than the first error.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage illustrates a second example of how errors propagate in fatwa literature. It concerns the ruling on ijarah (hiring) for recitation of the Qur'an. The author clarifies that the correct mufta bih view is that hiring for teaching the Qur'an is permissible, but hiring for mere recitation is not permissible. He criticizes those who mistakenly attributed the permissibility to all acts of worship. He traces the error back to al-Haddadi and later scholars who followed him without verification. The lesson is that a mufti must ascertain the exact ruling from reliable sources and not accept a general claim without evidence.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): Hiring or leasing for a wage; here specifically hiring a person to perform an act.
مفتی بہ (mufta bih): The relied-upon view that is given in fatwa, as opposed to other opinions within the school.
تلاوت (tilawah): Recitation of the Qur'an, distinct from teaching.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bih (relied-upon) view regarding ijarah for mere recitation of the Qur'an?
A) Permissible
B) Not permissible
C) Permissible only if at a grave
D) Permissible only for teaching

Key Takeaway
The mufta bih for ijarah on teaching the Qur'an does not automatically apply to recitation; each case must be verified from authoritative texts and the distinction maintained.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
12 min
Ijarah on Acts of Worship: Necessity as a Basis for Fatwa
Clarifying the correct Hanafi ruling on ijarah for ta'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti principle that necessity (darurah) permits ijarah for acts of worship only in specific cases (teaching Qur'an, adhan, imamah) and distinguish this from the erroneous absolute permissibility.

Core Idea
Ijarah for acts of worship is invalid by default; necessity is a narrow gateway, not a blanket permission.

This passage from a Hanafi fatwa manual critiques a widespread error: that later scholars permitted hiring for all worship. In fact, the permission was strictly limited to preserving religious knowledge and symbols. The author emphasizes the need to verify citations and never blindly follow authority, and then lays out the correct hierarchy of fatwa: the consensus of the three Imams, the necessity-based exceptions, and the rejection of unwarranted generalization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling on ijarah for acts of worship
State the ruling of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on ijarah for ta'at. Note that it is invalid (batil) by consensus.
This is the baseline; any permission is an exception.
2
Recognize the necessity-based exceptions
List the specific cases where later mujtahids permitted ijarah: teaching the Quran, adhan, and imamah. Identify the common condition: darurah (necessity) to prevent loss of religious knowledge or symbols.
The necessity was historical: loss of government stipends for Quran teachers, risk of decline in religious practice.
3
Understand the limits of necessity (darurah)
Explain that necessity is measured by its extent (al-darurah tuqaddar bi qadariha). The permission does not extend to mere recitation for isal thawab because no such necessity exists.
The author argues that without necessity, ijarah leads to riya (ostentation) and nullifies reward.
4
Critique the argument of absolute permissibility
Analyze the opposing view (Ibn Nujaym, Allaqi) that ijarah for all acts of worship is permissible. Show how it ignores the condition of necessity and the fatwa hierarchy.
The author calls this a serious error, especially deriving ijarah for Hajj from it.
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy (mufta bihi)
Determine the mufta bihi position: ijarah for acts of worship is invalid except for the three specific cases of necessity. Provide the tarjih reasoning: the early consensus is binding; later exceptions are conditional and cannot be generalized.
The mufta bihi relies on Imam Qadikhan and Ibn al-Humam, who state that taking wages nullifies reward for worship.

Source Text
