پھر حدادی کے بعد جو لوگ آئے انہوں نے حدادی کی پیروی کی اور ان کی بات نقل کرتے چلے گئے۔ حالانکہ وہ صریح غلطی تھی بلکہ بہت سے حضرات نے تو یہ کہدیا کہ فتوئی اس پر ہے کہ تمام عبادتوں پر اجارہ درست ہے . یہ سب حضرات مسئله عموم و اطلاق کے ساتھ لکھتے ہیں اور کہتے ہیں کہ یہ متاخرین کی رائے ہے اور بعض لوگ اس پر یہ مسئلہ بھی متفرع کرتے ہیں کہ حج کے لیے بھی اجارہ درست ہے یہ سب باتیں غلط ہیں اور پہلی غلطی سے بھی زیادہ سنگین ہیں ۔
فائدہ
نقل وحوالہ پر آنکھ بند کر کے اعتماد نہیں کرنا چاہیے بلکہ حوالہ کو اصل سے ملا کر دیکھنا چاہئے ۔ ہم نے حضرت الاستاذ مفتی مہدی حسن صاحب قدس سره (۲۷) سے ایک بار عرض کیا تھا کہ ہمیں کوئی نصیحت فرمائیں۔ آپ نے ارشاد فرمایا کہ " کبھی کسی کے حوالہ پر اعتماد نہیں کرنا چاہیے۔ میں نے عرض کیا کہ : اگر حافظ ابن حجر عسقلانی رحمہ اللہ حوالہ دیں تو ؟" آپ نے برجستہ فرمایا کہ : اگر حافظ ابن جبل حوالہ دیں تب بھی ! میں نہیں بتا سکتا کہ حضرت الاستاذ کی اس نصیحت نے مجھے کس قدر فائدہ پہنچایا ہے۔ فَجَزَاهُ الله خَيْرًا. طاعات پر اجارہ اور ایصال ثواب کے لیے اجرت پر قرآن خوانی کرانے کا عدم جواز : ہمارے ائمہ ثلاثہ رحمہم اللہ سے بالا تفاق یہ مروی ہے کہ طاعات کا اجارہ باطل ہے ۔ لیکن بعد کے مجتہدین نے جو اصحاب تخریج و تصیح تھے۔ "ضرورت" کی وجہ سے تعلیم قرآن پر اجارہ کے جواز کا فتویٰ دیا۔ کیونکہ معلمین قرآن کو پہلے حکومت سے وظائف ملتے تھے جو بعد میں بند ہو گئے ۔ اس لیے اگر تعلیم قرآن پر اجارہ اور تنخواہ لینے کو ناجائز قرار دیا جائے گا تو قرآن ضائع ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اساتذہ قرآن کو بھی کسب معاش کی فکر دامن گیر ہوگی اور قرآن کا ضیاع دین کا ضیاع ہے۔ اسی طرح بعد کے حضرات نے جو اصحاب ترجیح و صحیح کے ہم رتبہ تھے۔ اذان و امامت پر بھی اجارہ کے جواز کا فتویٰ دیا کیونکہ یہ دونوں چیزیں بھی دینی شعائر ہیں اس لیے بر بنائے ضرورت تنخواہ لینے کو جائز قرار دیا گیا۔
مطلقا طاعات پر اجارہ کے جواز کا قول علامہ ابن نجیم اور علاقی (۳۰) کا ہے۔ دیکھیے رسائل ابن عابدین
بس یہ تھا متاخرین کا فتویٰ جو انہوں نے امام اعظم اور ان کے تلامذہ کی نمائندگی کرتے ہوئے دیا تھا کیونکہ آج اگر ائمہ ثلاثہ موجود ہوتے اور بدلی ہوئی صورت حال دیکھتے تو وہ بھی ضرور یہی فتویٰ دیتے اور اپنے سابق قول سے رجوع فرما لیتے ۔ غرض مذکورہ بالا صورتوں کے علاوہ دیگر طاعات پر اجارہ کے باطل ہونے پر متون شروح اور فتاوی متفق ہیں اور ان حضرات نے جواز کی بنیاد ضرورت کو یعنی دین کے ضیاع کا اندیشہ بیان کی ہے اور اس بنیاد کی انہوں نے صراحت بھی کر دی ہے۔ پھر یہ بات کیوں کر درست ہو سکتی ہے کہ متاخرین کے نزدیک محض تلاوت پر بھی اجارہ درست ہے؟ دراں حالیکہ ضرورت کا اس صورت میں تحقیق نہیں ہے۔ صدیاں بھی گزر جائیں اور کوئی کسی کو محض تلاوت کے لیے اجرت پر نہ لے تو بھی کسی قسم کا ضرر نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ضرر تو اس قسم کے اجارہ میں ہے۔ قرآن کریم کمائی کا ذریعہ اور پیشہ بن کر رہ گیا ہے کوئی قاری لوجہ اللہ قرآن پڑھتا ہی نہیں ۔ جو پڑھتا ہے اجرت کے لیے پڑھتا ہے جو خالص ریا ( نمود ) ہے کیونکہ ریا کی حقیقت غیر اللہ کے لیے عمل کرتا ہے۔ پس ثواب کہاں ملے گا؟ اور ایصال ثواب کس چیز کا کرے گا؟ امام قاضی خان رحمہ اللہ (۲۲) فرماتے ہیں کہ : " ذکر کے عوض میں اجرت لینا ثواب کے استحقاق کو ختم کر دیتا ہے ۔ " علامہ ابن الہمام رحمہ اللہ (۳۹) نے بھی فتح القدیر ج ا ص ۲۱۶) میں مؤذن کی اجرت کی بحث میں ایسا ہی لکھا ہے۔ اور اگر ایصال ثواب کے لیے قرآن پڑھوانے والے کو معلوم ہو جائے کہ ثواب نہیں ملے گا تو وہ دھیلا بھی نہ دے۔!
الغرض ایصال ثواب کے لیے اجرت پر قرآن پڑھوانے والے والے ذکر و قرآن کے ذریعہ جہنم کا ایندھن جمع کرتے ہیں، لوگ اس کو کار ثواب تصور کرتے ہیں حالانکہ یہ عظیم ترین برائی ہے اور یہ برائی صحت اجارہ کے قول پر مرتب ہوتی ہے نیز ایصال ثواب کے لیے قرآن خوانی کرانے میں اور بھی متعدد برائیاں ہیں مثلاً یتیموں کا مال کھانا ان کے مکان میں ان کے فرش کو استعمال کرنا، چلا چلا کر سونے والوں کی نیند کو حرام کر دینا ڈھول بجانا' گانا گانا عورتوں اور مردوں کا اکھٹا ہونا وغیرہ خطر ناک منکرات نہیں جن کی میں نے (علامہ شامی نے ) اپنے ایک رسالہ میں جس کا نام شفاء العلیل، دبل الغليل في بطلان الوصية بالختمات والتهاليل
Then those who came after Haddad followed him and continued to quote his statement, although it was a clear error. Indeed, many people even said that the fatwa is that ijarah is valid for all acts of worship. All these people write about the issue with generality and absoluteness and say that this is the opinion of the later scholars (mutakhkhirin). And some people further derive from this that ijarah is also valid for Hajj. All these statements are wrong and even more serious than the first mistake. Benefit: One should not blindly rely on citations and references; rather, one should check the reference against the original. We once asked Hadrat al-Ustadh Mufti Mahdi Hasan Sahib (may Allah sanctify his soul) for advice. He said: 'Never rely on anyone's citation.' I said: 'Even if Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (rah) cites?' He immediately said: 'Even if Hafiz Ibn Jabal cites!' I cannot tell how much this advice of Hadrat al-Ustadh has benefited me. May Allah reward him greatly. The prohibition of ijarah on acts of worship and hiring Quran recitation for conveying reward (isal thawab): It is narrated from our three Imams (rah) by consensus that ijarah on acts of worship is invalid. But later mujtahids who were experts in derivation and correction (ashab al-takhrij wa al-tashih) issued a fatwa permitting ijarah for teaching the Quran due to necessity. Because teachers of the Quran previously received stipends from the government, which later stopped. Therefore, if taking ijarah and salary for teaching the Quran were declared impermissible, the Quran would be lost. Because teachers of the Quran would be preoccupied with earning a livelihood, and loss of the Quran is loss of the religion. Similarly, later scholars, who were of the rank of those capable of weighing and correcting (ashab al-tarjih wa al-tashih), also issued fatwas permitting ijarah for adhan and imamah, because these are also religious symbols; hence they permitted taking salary based on necessity. The opinion permitting ijarah absolutely on all acts of worship is held by Allamah Ibn Nujaym and Allaqi. See Rasa'il Ibn Abidin. This was the fatwa of the later scholars given in representation of Imam A'zam and his students, because if the three Imams were alive today and saw the changed situation, they would certainly issue the same fatwa and retract their earlier statement. In short, apart from the mentioned cases, the texts, commentaries, and fatwas agree on the invalidity of ijarah for other acts of worship. These scholars based permission on necessity, i.e., the fear of loss of religion, and they explicitly stated this basis. So how can it be correct that in the view of the later scholars ijarah is valid even for mere recitation? While there is no actual necessity in that case. Even if centuries pass and no one hires someone for mere recitation, there would be no harm. Rather, harm lies in this type of ijarah. The Quran has become a means of earning and a profession; no reciter recites the Quran for the sake of Allah. Whoever recites, recites for wages, which is pure ostentation (riya), because the reality of riya is doing an act for other than Allah. So where will reward come from? And what will be conveyed? Imam Qadikhan (rah) says: 'Taking wages for dhikr nullifies entitlement to reward.' Allamah Ibn al-Humam (rah) also wrote similarly in Fath al-Qadir (vol. 1, p. 216) in the discussion of the mu'adhdhin's wages. And if the one who hires Quran recitation for conveying reward knew that no reward will be obtained, he would not give even a penny. In short, those who hire Quran recitation for conveying reward gather fuel for Hell through dhikr and Quran; people consider it a good deed, while it is the greatest evil, and this evil results from the opinion of the validity of ijarah. Moreover, hiring Quran recitation for conveying reward involves many other evils, such as consuming the wealth of orphans, using their houses and furnishings, disturbing the sleep of others by loud recitation, beating drums, singing, mixing of men and women, etc., which are dangerous evils that I (Allamah Shami) have discussed in my treatise named Shifa' al-'Alil wa Dubul al-Ghalil fi Butlan al-Wasiyyah bi al-Khatamat wa al-Tahlil.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage from 'Sharh Rasm al-Mufti' addresses a rasm al-mufti issue: the proper methodology for issuing fatwas concerning ijarah (hiring) for acts of worship (ta'at). The author begins by critiquing a common error among later scholars who blindly followed Haddad's opinion that ijarah is valid for all acts of worship. He emphasizes the gravity of this mistake, especially extending it to Hajj. He then inserts a crucial methodological benefit: never rely on citations without verifying the original source, recounting a personal anecdote with his teacher Mufti Mahdi Hasan, who insisted on checking even the most authoritative references. 

The core ruling is that the three founding Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) unanimously held that ijarah for acts of worship is invalid. However, later mujtahids (ashab al-takhrij wa al-tashih) permitted ijarah for teaching the Qur'an out of necessity (darurah): when government stipends ceased, the fear of Qur'anic knowledge being lost justified payment. Similarly, they permitted it for adhan and imamah, as these are religious symbols that might otherwise decline. This permission was strictly limited to these cases. 

The author strongly rejects the absolute permissibility of ijarah for all acts of worship (e.g., mere recitation for isal thawab), attributing that view to Ibn Nujaym and Allaqi. He argues that such permission lacks necessity, leads to riya (ostentation), nullifies reward, and involves numerous social evils (e.g., mixing of genders, wasting orphans' money). The passage thus clarifies the hierarchy of fatwa: the early consensus is the default, later exceptions are bounded by necessity, and any deviation beyond that is a grave error.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijārah): A contract of hiring or leasing, specifically payment for services. In this context, hiring someone to perform an act of worship.
طاعات (ṭāʿāt): Acts of obedience or worship, such as prayer, fasting, recitation, dhikr, etc.
ضرورت (ḍarūrah): Necessity, a legal concept that permits normally prohibited actions to prevent harm or loss, specifically here to prevent the loss of religious knowledge and symbols.
متاخرین (mutaʾakhkhirīn): Later Hanafi scholars who came after the formative period, often credited with issuing fatwas based on necessity and changed circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what specific condition did the later Hanafi scholars rely upon when permitting ijarah for teaching the Quran?
A) General permissibility of ijarah for all acts of worship
B) The consensus of all later scholars
C) Necessity (darurah) to prevent the loss of Quranic knowledge
D) The opinion of Ibn Nujaym and Allaqi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that ijarah for acts of worship is invalid except in cases of proven necessity to preserve religious knowledge or symbols (teaching Quran, adhan, imamah).

Verifying the Hanafi Ruling on Insulting the Prophet Then Embracing Islam
Critical refinement of a misattributed Hanafi ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct Hanafi ruling on the acceptance of repentance of a person who insults the Prophet (sabb al-rasul) and explain why the contrary view is a misattribution.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab accepts the repentance of one who insults the Prophet, contrary to a widespread misattribution.

In this lesson, we examine an important example of verifying a fatwa against original Hanafi sources. A ruling that later scholars attributed to Abu Hanifa—that the repentance of one who insults the Prophet is not accepted—is shown to be a mistake. The correct position is recorded in the earliest Hanafi works. As a mufti, you must learn to trace rulings back to their sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Find the claim made by later Hanafi scholars: that a person who insults the Prophet must be killed and his repentance is not accepted even if he embraces Islam.
This claim is found in al-Bazzaziyya and echoed by Ibn al-Humann and others.
2
Trace the attribution
Check where this ruling is attributed to. Al-Bazzaziyya cites al-Shifa (by Qadi Iyad, a Maliki) and al-Sarim al-Maslul (by Ibn Taymiyyah, a Hanbali). These are not Hanafi sources.
The passage explicitly says the attribution is to Shafi'i, Hanbali, and one narration from Malik.
3
Consult early Hanafi authorities
Look up the earliest Hanafi texts: Kitab al-Kharaj by Abu Yusuf, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Kafi al-Hasan by al-Saghdi. They unanimously state that repentance is accepted.
These are the foundational books of the madhhab.
4
Conclude the correct mufta bihi
Based on the early sources, the operative ruling for fatwa is that the person's repentance is accepted and he is not executed.
Ibn Abidin wrote a treatise on this to clarify the correct position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بزاز يه ( بر حاشية عالمگيرى ج۶ ص۳۲۲) میں منقول ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اس کا قتل واجب ہے تو یہ مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اگر چہ وہ اسلام قبول کر لے۔ صاحب بزاز يه (۴۱) نے یہ بات قاضي عياض مالکى (۴۲) کی الشفاء اور ابن تيميه خبيلى (۴۳) کی الصارم المسلول کی طرف منسوب کى ہے۔ پھر بعد کے اکثر فقہا نے اس کى پيروى کى ہے يہاں تک کہ خاتم محققين علامہ ابن الهام (۳۹) اور الدور والغرر کے مصنف (۲۵) نے بھى يہى بات لکھى ہے۔ حالانکہ شفاء اور صارم میں جو بات ہے وہ يہ ہے کہ يہ شوافع اور حنابلہ کا مذہب ہے اور امام مالک رحمہ اللہ کى دو روايتوں میں سے ایک روايت ہے۔ اور ہمارا مذہب قطعيت کے ساتھ يہ نقل کيا ہے کہ اس کى توبہ مقبول ہے۔ اور يہى بات قدماء احناف کى کتابوں میں مذکور ہے۔ امام ابو يوسف رحمہ الله (۱۴) کى کتاب الخراج امام طحاوى رحمہ اللہ ( ۱۷ ) کى مختصر کى شرح اور سغدى کى الحف الحسان (۴۴) و غيرہ فقہ حنفى کى کتابوں میں يہى بات مذکور ہے۔ میں نے (علامہ شامى نے ) اس کى خوب وضاحت کر دى ہے۔ اپنے ایک رسالہ میں جس کا نام ہے تنبيہ الولاة والحکام على احکام شاتم خير !! نام و احد اصحابہ الکرام عليه و عليهم الصلوۃ والسلام يہ رسالہ اپنے موضوع پر اتنا مفصل ہے کہ پہلے کسى نے اتنى تفصيل سے نہيں لکھا ہے۔
In al-Bazzaziyya (on the margin of Alamgiri vol. 6 p. 322) it is narrated that according to us his execution is obligatory, then this is not accepted, even if he accepts Islam. The author of al-Bazzaziyya attributed this statement to al-Shifa of Qadi Iyad al-Maliki and al-Sarim al-Maslul of Ibn Taymiyya al-Hanbali. Then most later jurists followed it, until the last of the verifiers, Allamah Ibn al-Humann, and the author of al-Durr wa al-Ghirar also wrote the same. However, what is in al-Shifa and al-Sarim is that this is the madhhab of the Shafi'is and Hanbalis, and one of two narrations from Imam Malik. And our madhhab has transmitted with certainty that his repentance is accepted. And this same thing is mentioned in the books of the early Hanafis. It is mentioned in Imam Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj, Imam al-Tahawi's Sharh Mukhtasar, al-Saghdi's al-Kafi al-Hasan, and other Hanafi books. I (Allamah Shami) have clarified this well in my treatise named Tanbih al-Wulah wa al-Hukkam 'ala Ahkam Shatim Khayr al-Anam wa Ahad Ashabihi al-Kiram, which is so detailed on its subject that no one before has written with such detail.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement, demonstrating a common error in later Hanafi fatwa literature. The author (Ibn Abidin) points out that some Hanafi scholars—including later luminaries like Ibn al-Humann—erroneously transmitted a ruling that a person who insults the Prophet (sabb al-rasul) must be killed and that his repentance is not accepted even if he embraces Islam. This, they claimed, was the Hanafi madhhab. However, Ibn Abidin shows that this ruling actually belongs to the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools, and is only one of two narrations from Imam Malik. The correct and certain Hanafi position, recorded in the earliest sources (Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj, Tahawi's sharh, etc.), is that the repentance of such a person is accepted. Ibn Abidin wrote a separate treatise on this. The lesson for the mufti is to verify fatwa transmissions against authoritative early Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
توبہ (tawbah): Repentance from apostasy; in this context, the act of returning to Islam after insulting the Prophet.
شاتم النبي (shatim al-nabi): One who insults the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on a person who insults the Prophet (sabb al-rasul) and then embraces Islam?
A) He is killed and his repentance is not accepted.
B) His repentance is accepted and he is not executed.
C) He is imprisoned for life.
D) He is given a discretionary punishment.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position is that the repentance of one who insults the Prophet is accepted; muftis must verify such rulings against early sources.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Correct Hanafi Position: Mortgagee's Liability for Destroyed Pawn
Correction of misattributed ruling in mortgage liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi ruling regarding the mortgagee's liability when the pawn is destroyed, and distinguish it from the Maliki position.

Core Idea
The mortgagee is liable only for the deficiency — not the full value — regardless of witnesses.

Some later Hanafi scholars, including Mulla Khusraw and Ibn Malik, wrote that if the mortgagee claims the pawn was destroyed without witnesses, he is liable for its full value. Ibn Abidin, in Radd al-Muhtar, corrects this: that view is actually Maliki. The true Hanafi position is that the mortgagee is liable only for the deficiency (the amount by which the pawn's value falls short of the debt), and this applies whether or not there are witnesses. This lesson will help you identify and apply the correct mufta bihi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The mortgagee (creditor holding the pawn) asserts that the pawn was destroyed. There may or may not be witnesses.
The claim is about destruction, not negligence.
2
Recall the school's principle
In Hanafi fiqh, a pawn is a trust (amanah). The mortgagee is not liable for destruction unless he is negligent or breaches the trust.
This principle leads to limited liability.
3
Contrast with the erroneous view
Mulla Khusraw and others wrote that without witnesses the mortgagee is liable for the full value. Ibn Abidin identifies this as the Maliki position, not Hanafi.
The erroneous view distinguishes apparent vs. hidden property.
4
Apply the correct Hanafi ruling
The mortgagee is liable only for the deficiency: the difference between the pawn's value at the time of destruction and the debt. This applies whether witnesses exist or not.
If the pawn's value equals or exceeds the debt, no liability; if less, the shortfall is due.
5
Confirm the fatwa hierarchy
The correct ruling is the mufta bihi, confirmed by Ibn Abidin citing Shurunbulaliyya and Haqa'iq al-Mandhumah. It derives from Zahir al-Riwayah.
A mufti must not follow the erroneous view even if found in later texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھی مثال : مرتبین رہن کی ہلاکت کا دعوی کرے تو ضمان کس طرح آئے گا؟ ملاخسرو نے دار الحکام (۲۵) میں اور ابن ملک (۴۵) نے علامہ ابن الساعاتی کی مجمع البحرین (۲۵) کی شرح میں یہ لکھا ہے کہ اگر مرتین گواہوں کے بغیر ہلاکت کا دعوی کرے تو ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ ملاخسر و لکھتے ہیں کہ: (وضمن) المرتهن بدعوى الهلاك بلابينة) يعني اذا ادعى المرتهن الهلاك ضمن ان لم يقم البينة عليه (مطلقاً) اى سواء كان من الاموال الظاهرة كالحيوان والعبيد والعقار او من الاموال الباطنة كالنقدين والحلى والعروض وقال مالك يضمن فی الاموال الباطنة فقط درر الحکام ۲ ص ۲۴۹ اگر مرتین گواہوں کے بغیر رہن کی ہلاکت کا دعوی کرے تو وہ ضامن ہو گا یعنی جب مرتہن رہن کی ہلاکت کا دعوی کرے تو وہ اس شرط کے ساتھ ضامن ہوگا کہ ہلاکت پر گواہ نہ ہوں یہ حکم مطلقا ہے یعنی رہن خواہ ایسی چیز ہو جو چھپائی نہ جاسکتی ہو جیسے جانور غلام اور جائداد یا چھپائی جاسکتی ہو جیسے دراہم و دنا نیر زیورات اور و سامان اور امام مالک رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صرف دوسری قسم کے اموال میں ضمان آئے گا۔ علامہ تمر تاشی (۲۵) نے بھی تنویر الا بصارت میں ان دونوں حضرات کی پیروی کی ہے۔ ان سب حضرات کی تحریروں کا مقتضی دو باتیں ہیں۔ (۱) رہن کی جو بھی قیمت ہو۔ خواہ دین سے کم ہو یا زیادہ یا مساوی... اس کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ علامہ خیر الدین رملی نے بھی یہی فتوئی تو دیا ہے: (۲) اگر رہن کی ہلاکت پر گواہ موجود ہوں تو کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ حالاں کہ یہ دونوں باتیں امام مالک کا مذہب تمہیں اور ہمارا مذ ہب یہ ہے کہ رہن کی قیمت اور قرض میں جو کم ہو گا اس کا ضمان واجب ہوگا خواہ رہن کی ہلاکت پر گواہ موجود ہوں یا گواہوں کے بغیر صرف مرتبین کی قسم سے ہلاکت ثابت ہوئی ہو۔ درالحکام کے حاشیہ شرنبلالیہ (۴۶) میں حقائق المنظومه (۴۷) کے حوالہ سے اس کی پوری وضاحت کر دی گئی ہے اور میں نے (علامہ شامی نے) بھی اپنے حاشیہ ردالمحتار میں اس پر تنبیہ کی ہے اور یہ بھی بیان کیا ہے کہ کس نے مذہب حنفی کے مطابق فتویٰ دیا ہے اور کس نے مخالف مذہب قول کی تردید کی ہے۔ اور بھی مثالیں: اور اس قسم کے تسامحات کی جن کا ہم نے تذکرہ کیا بہت نظائر ہیں جن میں صاحب بحر ا
Fourth example: If the mortgagee claims destruction of the pawn, how does liability arise? Mulla Khusraw wrote in Durar al-Hikam and Ibn Malik wrote in his commentary on Majma' al-Bahrayn of Allamah Ibn al-Sa'ati that if the mortgagee claims destruction without witnesses, then liability becomes obligatory. Mulla Khusraw writes: 'And the mortgagee is liable by claim of destruction without evidence; that is, when the mortgagee claims destruction, he is liable if he does not produce evidence over it, absolutely, whether it is from apparent property like animals, slaves, and real estate, or from hidden property like gold and silver, jewelry, and goods.' And Malik says he is liable only in hidden property. In Durar al-Hikam (2:249): If the mortgagee claims destruction of the pawn without witnesses, then he will be liable, meaning when the mortgagee claims destruction, he will be liable on condition that there are no witnesses to the destruction. This ruling is absolute, i.e., the pawn whether it is something that cannot be hidden, like animals, slaves, and property, or something that can be hidden, like dirhams, dinars, jewelry, and goods. And Imam Malik says that liability only applies to the second type of property. Allamah Tamurtashi also followed these two individuals in Tanwir al-Absar. The implication of all these writings is two things: (1) Whatever the value of the pawn, whether less than the debt, more, or equal, its liability is obligatory. Allamah Khayr al-Din al-Ramli also gave fatwa accordingly. (2) If there are witnesses to the destruction of the pawn, then no liability is obligatory. However, these two things are exactly the madhhab of Imam Malik, while our madhhab is that the deficiency between the pawn's value and the debt is liable whether there are witnesses to the destruction or without witnesses, merely by the mortgagee's oath establishing the destruction. In the Shurunbulaliyya commentary on Durar al-Hikam, this is fully clarified with reference to Haqa'iq al-Mandhumah. And I (Allamah Shami) have also alerted to this in my hashya Radd al-Muhtar, and have stated who gave fatwa according to the Hanafi madhhab and who refuted the contrary opinion. And there are more examples: there are many such instances of this kind of carelessness that we have mentioned, among which the author of Bahr...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement correcting an error in fatwa transmission regarding mortgage (rahn). Mulla Khusraw and Ibn Malik, followed by Tamurtashi and Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, transmitted that if the mortgagee claims the pawn was destroyed without producing witnesses, he is liable for the entire value of the pawn, and if witnesses exist, no liability. Ibn Abidin shows that this is actually the Maliki madhhab, not the Hanafi. The correct Hanafi position, as clarified in Shurunbulaliyya and Radd al-Muhtar, is that the mortgagee is only liable for the deficiency (the amount by which the pawn's value falls short of the debt)—and this liability applies regardless of whether witnesses are present or not. The reason is that the pawn is a trust (amanah) in the mortgagee's hands; he is not liable for destruction unless he is negligent. By claiming destruction, he is effectively asserting that he is not negligent. If his claim is accepted by oath, he is liable only for the deficit (if any) because the debt remains, and the pawn was meant to cover it. The mufti must ensure he attributes the correct ruling to the Hanafi school, not follow later scholars who inadvertently adopted a Maliki view.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Financial liability or guarantee; in this context, the mortgagee's obligation to compensate for the lost pawn.
مرتہن (murtahin): The mortgagee (creditor) who holds the pawn as security for a debt.
ہلاکت (halakat): Destruction or loss of the pawned item, claimed by the mortgagee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi madhhab, what is the mortgagee liable for if he claims the pawn was destroyed without witnesses?
A) The entire value of the pawn.
B) Only the deficiency (the difference between the pawn's value and the debt).
C) Nothing, because it is a trust.
D) Half of the debt.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's liability for a destroyed pawn is limited to the deficiency between the pawn's value and the debt, and this ruling applies regardless of the presence or absence of witnesses.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
beginner

The Obligation of Following Zahir al-Riwayah in Fatwa
Establishes the obligation to base fatwa on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and apply the rule that fatwa must be based on them unless overruled by tarjih.

Core Idea
Fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab rests on the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, unless later scholars give preference to another transmission.

This passage establishes a foundational rule of Hanafi fatwa: the mufti must primarily rely on the Zahir al-Riwayah books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. This principle ensures consistency and prevents reliance on rare or weak transmissions. The passage also explains that this obligation is lifted only when later authorities of tarjih explicitly prefer a different view from a non-Zahir al-Riwayah source.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Zahir al-Riwayah books
Memorize that Zahir al-Riwayah consists of six books authored by Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. These are called 'al-Usul' (the foundations).
These books contain the most widely transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
2
Understand the obligation to follow Zahir al-Riwayah
The rule states that fatwa must be given according to these books, even if no later scholar explicitly declares them sahih. Their mere belonging to Zahir al-Riwayah is proof of their correctness.
This gives Zahir al-Riwayah presumptive authority.
3
Recognize the exception for tarjih
If later scholars (arbab al-tarjih) prefer a ruling from a non-Zahir al-Riwayah source, that preferred opinion becomes the operative one for fatwa. The shadh (rare) narration is not to be followed without such explicit preference.
The exception applies only when scholars explicitly correct or prefer a shadh narration.
4
Note the authority hierarchy
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source; shadh riwaya is secondary and can only be used if the imams have explicitly stated that fatwa is on that shadh narration. Even a muqallid judge must follow this hierarchy.
This hierarchy prevents arbitrary use of weak opinions.
5
Apply the concept to a scenario
When asked about a transaction, first check if the ruling is in a Zahir al-Riwayah book. If yes, that is the default answer. If it is not present, search for tarjih by later scholars. Do not resort to a shadh transmission without explicit authority.
This ensures the fatwa is based on the most reliable evidence in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتویٰ ظاہر روایت پر دینا چاہئے: دسویں شعر میں کہا گیا تھا کہ ظاہر روایت کی پیروی واجب ہے بشرطیکہ ارباب ترجیح نے اس کے خلاف دوسرے قول کو ترجیح نہ دی ہو۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو مسائل امام محمد رحمہ الله (۱۵) کی مشہور کتابوں میں مروی ہیں ان پر فتوی دینا چاہیے۔ اگر چہ کسی امام نے صراحة ان کی تصحیح نہ کی ہو کیونکہ ان کا ظاہر روایت ہونا ہی ان کی صحت کی بڑی دلیل ہے۔ ہاں اگر ائمہ کسی ایسی روایت کی تصحیح کریں جو کتب ظاہر روایت کے علاوہ دوسری کتابوں میں ہے تو پھر ان کی تصحیح کی پیروی کی جائے گی ۔ علامہ طرسوی رحمہ اللہ (۵۰) انفع الوسائل میں یک مابہ کفالہ کے بیان میں لکھتے ہیں کہ: ا مقلد قاضی کے لیے ظاہر روایت کے مطابق ہی فیصلہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ شاذ روایت پر قاضی فیصلہ نہیں کر سکتا الا یہ کہ ائمہ نے صراحت کی ہو کہ فتویٰ شاز روایت پر ہے اھ ۔ وَكُتُبِ ظَاهِرِ الرّوَايَاتِ أَتَتْ سِرًّا وَبِالْأُصُولِ أَيْضاً سُمِّيَتْ ترجمہ: اور ظاہر روایت کی کتابیں آئی ہیں ( تعداد میں ) ۔ چھ اور وہ اصول" بھی کہلاتی ہیں ۔ تشریح دوسرا مصرع شامی ج ۱ ص ۳۸ میں اس طرح ہے سِرًّا لِكُلِّ ثَابِتٍ عَنْهُمْ حَوَتْ یعنی انکی تعداد چھ ہے اور وہ ہمارے ائمہ ثلاثہ کی تمام ثابت روایات کا احاطہ کر لیتی ہیں۔ ظاہر الروایۃ کی ترکیب: ظاہر الروایہ مرکب اضافی ہے مگر حقیقت میں مرکب توصیفی ہے اسی روایت ظاہراً یعنی ایسی
Fatwa should be given based on Zahir al-Riwayah. In the tenth verse it was said that following Zahir al-Riwayah is obligatory provided that the scholars of tarjih did not give preference to another statement against it. Its meaning is that fatwa should be given on issues that are narrated in the famous books of Imam Muhammad (15), even if no Imam explicitly declared them to be sahih, because their being Zahir al-Riwayah itself is a strong proof of their correctness. Yes, if the Imams correct a transmission that is in books other than the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, then their correction will be followed. Allamah Tarsusi (50) in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, in the discussion of kafalah, writes: 'For a muqallid judge, it is necessary to decide according to Zahir al-Riwayah. A judge cannot decide based on a shadh (rare) transmission unless the Imams explicitly state that the fatwa is on the shadh transmission.' End. And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came as 'sirr' (six) and they are also called 'al-Usul'. Translation: 'And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came, six in number, and they are also called al-Usul.' Explanation: The second hemistich is in Shami vol. 1 p. 38 as: 'sirra li kulli thabitin 'anhum hawat' meaning their number is six and they encompass all the established narrations from our three Imams. Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule stating the foundational principle for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab: fatwa must be based on Zahir al-Riwayah, which refers to the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat). This obligation holds unless later scholars of tarjih (like Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or later authorities) have given preference to a different transmission. The passage clarifies that the mere fact that a ruling is in Zahir al-Riwayah is sufficient proof of its correctness; explicit correction by later Imams is not needed. However, if later Imams correct a ruling from non-Zahir al-Riwayah sources, that correction is to be followed. Allamah Tarsusi's quote reinforces that even a muqallid judge must decide by Zahir al-Riwayah, not by shadh (rare) transmissions unless explicitly stated. The passage ends with a poetic verse about the six books, which are also called 'al-Usul' (the foundations), and they contain all established narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The composition of the term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' is explained as an idafah compound that is actually descriptive, meaning 'the transmission that is apparent/well-known'.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent/established transmissions from the Hanafi imams, specifically the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
شاذ روایت (shadh riwaya): A rare or weak transmission not from Zahir al-Riwayah, which cannot be used for fatwa unless scholars explicitly state otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many books comprise Zahir al-Riwayah according to the passage?
A) 4
B) 5
C) 6
D) 10

Key Takeaway
Fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab must be based on the Zahir al-Riwayah books unless later scholars have explicitly preferred a different transmission.

Fatwa Must Be Based on Zahir al-Riwayah
Ruling on obligation of fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah and punishment for unqualified mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that fatwa must be based on Zahir al-Riwayah and identify when a shadh narration may be used.

Core Idea
Fatwa is obligated upon Zahir al-Riwayah; shadh narrations require explicit authorization.

This passage from a Hanafi rasm al-mufti text establishes a foundational rule: a mufti or judge must base his fatwa or judgment on the well-known transmitted rulings of the school, known as Zahir al-Riwayah. The text also warns against unqualified individuals issuing fatwa and outlines the punishment for doing so. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for anyone who wishes to issue fatwa within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal rule
The passage states that fatwa must be based on Zahir al-Riwayah—the rulings transmitted in Imam Muhammad's six core books. This is the default source for fatwa.
This rule applies even if no later imam explicitly authenticated those rulings, because their widespread transmission (tawatur) itself indicates reliability.
2
Recognize the exception for tarjih
The rule holds 'unless the authorities of tarjih have preferred another statement contrary to it.' That is, later scholars may weigh and choose a different ruling within the madhhab, overriding the default Zahir al-Riwayah position.
Tarjih is a technical process; only qualified scholars can perform it.
3
Understand the use of shadh narrations
The passage allows fatwa on a shadh (rare) narration only if the imams have explicitly stated that fatwa should be on that shadh narration. Otherwise, the mufti must stick to Zahir al-Riwayah.
This prevents arbitrary use of isolated reports.
4
Apply to a muqallid judge
A judge who follows the Hanafi school (muqallid qadi) is bound to decide only according to Zahir al-Riwayah, as quoted from 'Allamah Tarsusi. He cannot use shadh narrations without explicit authorization.
This ensures consistency in judicial practice.
5
Consider the consequence of violation
An unqualified person who gives fatwa must be given a deterrent punishment to prevent harm to the community.
This underscores the seriousness of the mufti's role.

How to give fatwa? Commentary on Rasm al-Mufti: Only a person who is qualified to be an intermediary between people and Allah can give fatwa. This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling on the qualifications of a mufti and the source of fatwa. It begins by stating that only a qualified person can act as an intermediary between people and Allah by giving fatwa. However, if later imams authenticate a narration from outside these books, that may be followed. The passage concludes with a quote from 'Allamah Tarsusi confirming that a muqallid judge must decide by Zahir al-Riwayah, not by shadh narrations, unless the imams explicitly specify otherwise. شاذ روایت (Shadh Riwayah): A rare or isolated narration not in the six core books

Distinguishing Ashab and Mashayikh in Hanafi Authority
Definitions and temporal division of Hanafi scholarly categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi technical definitions of Ashab and Mashayikh, and apply the temporal division between Muttaqaddimin and Muta'akhkhirin when assessing the authority of a ruling.

Core Idea
Ashab are the direct students of Abu Hanifa; Mashayikh are later jurists who never met him.

A mufti must navigate a hierarchy of authorities when issuing verdicts. This lesson clarifies two key categories: the foundational Ashab (the three Imams and their immediate students) and the later Mashayikh (jurists who built upon their legacy). You will also learn the widely accepted chronological cutoff between the early and later scholars, a distinction essential for determining which opinion carries more weight.

Guided Path
1
Lexical and Technical Meanings
Begin by parsing the lexical origin of 'Ashab' (companion, teacher/student) and 'Mashayikh' (scholar of high rank). Then focus on their technical Hanafi usage: Ashab refers primarily to the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), and sometimes all direct students of Abu Hanifa. Mashayikh refers to early jurists who did not meet Abu Hanifa.
The term 'Ashab' can be broader (all direct students) or narrower (only the three Imams). The passage mentions both usages.
2
Identify the Two Scholarly Generations
The passage quotes Al-Dhahabi's demarcation: the end of the third century (300 AH) divides Muttaqaddimin (early scholars) and Muta'akhkhirin (later scholars). Note that both Ashab and Mashayikh belong to the Muttaqaddimin category, but Ashab are the earliest layer.
This timeline affects tarjih (preference): early opinions generally override later ones.
3
Apply the Hierarchy to Fatwa Practice
As a mufti, when conflicting opinions exist, prioritize the view of the Ashab (especially the three Imams) over the Mashayikh, and within the Mashayikh, prefer earlier scholars (Muttaqaddimin) over later ones (Muta'akhkhirin), unless a later consensus (ijma') or a stronger proof (dalil) dictates otherwise.
This hierarchy is a key principle in Rasm al-Mufti literature.

Difference between Ashab and Mashayikh: Ashab is the plural of Sahib, whose lexical meaning is companion, and customary meaning is teacher and student. Shaykh refers to a religious scholar who is great in knowledge, virtue, and rank in people's eyes; its plurals are Ashyakh, Shuyukh, and Mishyah, and the plural of plural is Mashayikh. In terminology, Ashab refers to the three Imams (Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn), and sometimes to Imam Abu Hanifa and all his direct students. Mashayikh refer to the early jurists who did not live in the time of Imam Abu Hanifa. The famous usage: 'our Ashab' is applied to our three Imams: Abu Hanifa and his two companions, as mentioned in Sharh al-Wahbaniyya. As for Mashayikh, it is stated in Waqf al-Nahr from Allama Qasim: 'What is meant by them in terminology is one who did not meet the Imam'. (Radd al-Muhtar, vol. 3, p. 497) Determination of Muttaqaddimin and Muta'akhkhirin: Allama Dhababi (d. 748 AH?) made the end of the third century the dividing line between early and later scholars. Shami writes in Shifa' al-'Alil: A benefit: al-Dhahabi said: The dividing line between early and later scholars is the beginning of the third century, i.e., 300 AH. So those before that are early, those after are later. (Rasa'il Ibn Abidin, vol. 1, p. 161) That is, scholars who passed away by the end of the third century are called Muttaqaddimin, and those after are Muta'akhkhirin.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage provides crucial terminological definitions for a mufti. It distinguishes between Ashab (the immediate students and companions of Imam Abu Hanifa, especially the three Imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Mashayikh (later jurists who did not meet Abu Hanifa personally). The term 'Ashab' can also include all direct students of Abu Hanifa. The Mashayikh are those who transmitted and expanded the school after the first generation. Additionally, the passage gives the famous demarcation between Muttaqaddimin (early scholars) and Muta'akhkhirin (later scholars) as the end of the third century (300 AH), quoting al-Dhahabi and Ibn Abidin. This classification is essential for determining the authority of a ruling: earlier scholars' opinions are generally given more weight.

Key Terms
اصحاب (Ashab): In Hanafi terminology, primarily the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and sometimes all direct students of Abu Hanifa.
مشائخ (Mashayikh): Later Hanafi jurists who did not meet Imam Abu Hanifa, responsible for transmitting and expanding the school.
متقدمین (Muttaqaddimin): Scholars who died up to the end of the 3rd century (300 AH), considered the early authorities.
متاخرین (Muta'akhkhirin): Scholars after the 3rd century who are later authorities in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must distinguish Ashab (direct students of Abu Hanifa) from Mashayikh (later jurists), and recognize the temporal cutoff of 300 AH between Muttaqaddimin and Muta'akhkhirin, to correctly prioritize competing opinions.

Definition and Status of Nawazil
Defining Nawazil and explaining their place after Nawadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish nawazil from nawadir and apply the Hanafi textual hierarchy when evaluating the authority of a ruling.

Core Idea
Nawazil are new issues derived by later scholars—authoritative only when no stronger transmission exists.

This lesson introduces the third category of Hanafi masail: Nawazil. Understanding where Nawazil sit in the hierarchy—after Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir—is essential for a mufti to correctly weigh the authority of rulings. The passage explains that Nawazil are new issues not transmitted from the founding imams, derived by later scholars using proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three tiers of Hanafi texts
Read the passage and note the implied three levels: Zahir al-Riwayah (six books), Nawadir (rare transmissions), and Nawazil (new issues).
The passage explicitly mentions Nawadir and Nawazil; Zahir al-Riwayah is the unmentioned first tier.
2
Define Nawazil linguistically and technically
The term Nawazil is plural of Nazila, meaning an incident. Technically, it is a new issue that arose after the mujtahidun period and is not found in their narrations.
Contrast with Nawadir: Nawadir are rare transmissions from the imams, while Nawazil are entirely new.
3
Understand the derivation method
Later scholars (mashayikh) extracted rulings for Nawazil using proofs (dalil), i.e., qiyas and istihsan, not direct transmission.
This is distinct from the earlier tiers which are based on transmitted texts.
4
Recognize the authority hierarchy
Zahir al-Riwayah is strongest, then Nawadir, then Nawazil. If a ruling is found in a higher tier, it takes precedence over a Nazila ruling.
The passage itself does not state this explicitly but the context (ranking after Nawadir) implies it.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a scenario
Given a new issue, classify it as a Nazila, derive a ruling using proofs, and acknowledge its lower authority compared to transmitted texts.
For example, a fatwa on cryptocurrency would be a Nazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-١٢- وَبَعْدَهَا مَسَائِلُ التَّوَازِلُ خَرَّجَهَا الْأَشْيَاحُ بالدَّلائِلُ ترجمہ: اور نوادر کے بعد "مسائل النوازل" کا درجہ ہے۔ جن کی مشائخ نے دلائل سے تخریج کی ہے۔

نوازل نازلہ کی جمع ہے جس کے معنی ہیں پیش آمدہ واقعہ اور اصطلاح میں نازلہ وہ نیا مسئلہ ہے جو مجتہدین کا زمانہ گزر جانے کے بعد پیش آیا ہے اور اس کا حکم مجتہدین سے مروی نہیں ہے۔ بعد کے اکابر نے دلائل سے اس کا حکم بیان کیا ہے فقیہ ابواللیث سمرقندی رحمہ اللہ (۵۱) کی کتاب النوازل غالباً اسی قسم کے مسائل کا مجموعہ ہے۔
12. And after them are the Nawazil issues, which the mashayikh extracted with proofs. Translation: After Nawadir, the rank of "Masail al-Nawazil" comes. They were derived by the mashayikh using proofs. Introduction to Nawazil books: Nawazil is the plural of Nazila, which means an incident that occurs. Technically, a Nazila is a new issue that arose after the era of the mujtahidun, and its ruling is not transmitted from the mujtahidun. Later senior scholars deduced its ruling from proofs. The book al-Nawazil by Faqih Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (d. 373 AH) is presumably a collection of such issues.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule defining the third category of masail in the Hanafi madhhab hierarchy — Nawazil (novel issues). The text first presents the Arabic statement: 'After them (i.e., after Nawadir) come the Nawazil issues, which the mashayikh extracted by way of proofs.' Then it expands in Urdu: Nawadir refers to rare transmissions not in the six core books. Nawazil are entirely new issues that arose after the period of the founding mujtahidun (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and their direct students). Since these issues are not found in the transmitted texts, later scholars (mashayikh) used qiyas and istihsan to derive rulings. The text gives an example: the book al-Nawazil of Imam Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. This classification is crucial as it determines the weight of a ruling: rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah are strongest, followed by Nawadir, then Nawazil. A mufti must know this hierarchy to issue correct fatwas.

Key Terms
نوازل (nawāzil): Plural of nāzilah; new issues that arose after the era of the mujtahidun, not found in earlier texts, and for which later scholars deduced rulings using proofs.
نازلہ (nāzilah): A single incident or issue that requires a ruling; the building block of nawazil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nawazil are new issues derived by later scholars; they occupy the third tier in the Hanafi textual hierarchy, after Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir.

Ghayr Zahir al-Riwayah: Sources and Evidentiary Weight
Classifying narrations outside the six core books of Imam Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sources of ghayr zahir al-riwayah and apply the hierarchy of evidence in fatwa, distinguishing it from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Ghayr zahir al-riwayah narrations are authoritative but hold secondary weight; a mufti must distinguish them from the primary Zahir al-Riwayah.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all transmitted rulings carry the same evidentiary weight. While Zahir al-Riwayah—the six core books of Imam Muhammad—form the primary foundation, many rulings come from other authentic sources. This lesson clarifies the category of ghayr zahir al-riwayah, its various forms, and its proper place in the mufti's hierarchy, ensuring that fatwa are based on the strongest available evidence.

Guided Path
1
Define ghayr zahir al-riwayah
Start by internalizing the definition: narrations not transmitted through Imam Muhammad's six well-known books (Zahir al-Riwayah) but from other recognized Hanafi sources. Identify the key terms: Kisaniyat, Haruniyat, Jurjaniyat, Ruqiyat, and others mentioned in the text.
These terms refer to collections attributed to various students of Abu Hanifa.
2
List the sources of ghayr zahir
From the passage, enumerate the three main types: (1) books of other students like Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad's al-Hajar, (2) Imla' (dictations) such as Imam Abu Yusuf's Amali, and (3) single-narrator transmissions like those of Ibn Sama'ah or Mu'alla ibn Mansur.
The Shafi'i equivalent of Amali is ta'liqah.
3
Understand the method of Imla'
Comprehend how Amali were produced: a scholar would dictate orally while students transcribed, later compiling the notebooks into a book. This was a standard method among early muhaddithun, fuqaha', and adab scholars.
The passage notes this method is now obsolete.
4
Apply the hierarchy in fatwa
Recognize that a mufti must prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah rulings. Ghayr zahir can be used when no clear ruling exists in the primary sources, but the mufti must note its lower evidentiary weight and exercise caution in tarjih.
This hierarchy prevents incorrect reliance on weaker transmissions.

شرح رسم الملاتی جیسے کیسانیات ہارونیات جرجانیات اور رقیات میں اور ان مسائل کو غیر ظاہر الروایہ اس لیے کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ مسائل مذکورہ بالا کتابوں کے مسائل کی طرح امام محمد سے صحیح ثابت اور مشہور روایت سے مروی نہیں ہیں ۔ (۲) یا وہ مسائل امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے علاوہ دیگر تلامذہ امام اعظم کی کتابوں میں مذکور ہیں مثله امام حسن بن زیادہ (۷۹) کی کتاب الحجر د میں اور اس کے علاوہ دوسری کتابوں میں امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کی امالی میں جو مسائل مذکور ہیں وہ بھی اسی قسم میں شامل ہیں ۔ فائدہ امالی جمع ہے املاء کی جس کے معنی ہیں لکھاتا۔ اس کا طریقہ یہ تھا کہ کوئی عالم بیٹھ جاتا اور اس کے گرد اس کے تلامذہ قلم دوات اور کاغذ لے کر بیٹھ جاتے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ اس عالم کے دل میں جو کچھ ڈالتا دہ زبانی لکھواتا۔ پھر وہ کا پیاں جمع کرلی جاتیں تو ایک مستقل کتاب بن جاتی۔ یہ طریقہ الماء یا امالی کہلاتا تھا۔ سلف میں محدثین، فقہاء اور ادباء وغیرہ سب ہی یہ طریقہ اختیار کرتے تھے اور اپنی اپنی لائن کے علوم لکھواتے تھے۔ اب نہ وہ علماء رہے اور نہ وہ علم ہی رہا اس لیے املاء کا یہ طریقہ بس قصہ پارینہ بن کر رہ گیا۔ شوافع کی اصطلاح میں اس کو تعلیقہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ (۳) یا ان مسائل کو امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کا کوئی ایک ہی شاگرد روایت کرتا ہے جیسے ابن سماعه (۵۸) اور معلی بن منصور (۸۰) وغیرہ کے روایت کردہ مخصوص مسائل ۔
Explanation of Rasm al-Mufti: Like Kisaniyat, Haruniyat, Jurjaniyat, and Ruqiyat, and these issues are called non-apparent (ghayr zahir al-riwayah) because these issues, like the issues of the above-mentioned books, are not transmitted from Imam Muhammad with authentic and well-known transmission. (2) Or those issues are mentioned in the books of other students of Imam al-A'zam besides Imam Muhammad, for example in the book al-Hajar by Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad (79) and in other books, and the issues mentioned in the Amali of Imam Abu Yusuf are also included in this category. Benefit: Amali is the plural of imla, meaning dictation. Its method was that a scholar would sit and around him his students would sit with pen, inkwell, and paper. Whatever Allah placed in the heart of the scholar, he would dictate orally. Then those notebooks would be collected, forming an independent book. This method was called imla or amali. Among the predecessors, muhaddithun, fuqaha', and literary scholars all adopted this method and dictated their respective sciences. Now neither those scholars remain nor that knowledge, so this method of imla has become a thing of the past. In the terminology of the Shafi'is, it is called ta'liqah. (3) Or a single student of Imam Muhammad narrates these issues, such as the specific issues narrated by Ibn Sama'ah (58) and Mu'alla ibn Mansur (80).
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage explains the category of ghayr zahir al-riwayah (non-apparent narrations) in the Hanafi madhhab. The author, from a rasm al-mufti work, defines these as narrations that were not transmitted through the widely-known chains of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani's six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah). Instead, they come from other sources: either from the books of other leading students of Abu Hanifa like Imam Hasan ibn Ziyad or Imam Abu Yusuf's dictations (Amali), or from single student transmissions like those of Ibn Sama'ah. The author also provides a beneficial note on the method of imla, explaining how scholarly dictation worked in early Islam, and notes that the Shafi'i school calls this ta'liqah. This classification is crucial for a mufti because rulings from ghayr zahir al-riwayah carry less weight than those from zahir al-riwayah, and a mufti must be aware of the hierarchy of sources.

Key Terms
غیر ظاہر الروایہ (ghayr zahir al-riwayah): Narrations not transmitted through the six well-known books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah) but from other students or single chains.
امالی (amali): Dictations by a scholar that his students wrote down and compiled into a book.

D) The Muwatta of Imam Malik

Key Takeaway
A mufti must prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah and only use ghayr zahir when necessary and with caution.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
12 min
Distinction Between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah: Ibn Kamal Pasha vs. Allama Shami
Dispute about whether Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah are distinct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the relationship between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah and apply Allama Shami's position to determine which narrations qualify as Zahir al-Riwayah for fatwa.

Core Idea
Riwayat al-Usul is a subset of Zahir al-Riwayah; a Nawadir narration qualifies only if also found in Usul.

This passage tackles a key distinction in Hanafi ifta: the precise relationship between Riwayat al-Usul (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and Zahir al-Riwayah (the prominent narrations). Ibn Kamal Pasha argues they are distinct, citing a case where a narration from Nawadir is called Zahir al-Riwayah. Allama Shami refutes this, showing the narration could also be in Usul. We will unpack this dispute and its implications for a mufti's hierarchy of sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What exactly is being disputed? The question is whether Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah are identical or have a general-specific relationship, and whether a narration found only in Nawadir (non-Usul) can be considered Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Ibn Kamal Pasha's argument
Ibn Kamal points to the Hajj issue: in Sarkhasi's Mabsut, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad (not in Usul books) is called Zahir al-Riwayah. He concludes that Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah, proving a distinction between the two terms.
He interprets 'Zahir al-Riwayah' literally as any prominent narration, even if outside Usul.
3
Allama Shami's response
Shami argues that the narration in question is also found in the books of Usul, as Imam Muhammad transmitted multiple versions. The label 'Zahir al-Riwayah' in that context simply means it is from Usul. Therefore, the case does not prove that a Nawadir-only narration can be Zahir al-Riwayah.
Shami's method: he does not deny the possibility but shows the example fails to prove the general rule.
4
Determine the relationship
Shami's position implies that Riwayat al-Usul is a specific subset of Zahir al-Riwayah. The term Zahir al-Riwayah is broader: it primarily refers to the six books but occasionally includes Nawadir only if the same narration is also in Usul.
This is the general-specific (amm wa khass) relationship: 'Zahir al-Riwayah' is amm, 'Riwayat al-Usul' is khass.
5
Apply to mufti's practice
For a mufti, this means that when seeking a ruling, the primary source is the six books of Usul (Riwayat al-Usul). A narration from Nawadir alone does not have the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah unless it is corroborated by the Usul books. This hierarchy affects which opinions are preferred in fatwa.
Also note the importance of checking whether a Nawadir narration is also in Usul.

Start of Rasm al-Mufti. It is called and Shams al-A'imma al-Hawani and others besides him, their Mabsut are in reality commentaries on Imam Muhammad's Mabsut. These commentators have written the commentary text mixed with the text of Imam Muhammad's Mabsut. The commentators of Jami' al-Saghir have adopted the same method. For example, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Qadi Khan etc. Thus it is said: 'Qadi Khan mentioned this in Jami' al-Saghir, and he means the commentary of Jami' al-Saghir.' (The content from the heading 'Tabaqat al-Masa'il' up to here was taken by Allama Shami from two books: from Allama Birri's Sharh al-Ashbah and from Shaykh Ismail al-Nabulsi's Sharh al-Durr.) No difference between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn Kamal Pasha (with response). After the above, it should be known that Allama Ibn Kamal Pasha differentiated between Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah. In the commentary of Hidayah, regarding the issue of obligation of Hajj on a woman, what he wrote is summarized as follows: In the Mabsut of Siraj al-A'imma (or maybe Rukhs?): 'Zahir al-Riwayah is that Hajj becomes obligatory on a woman when she has, besides her own maintenance, the maintenance of her mahram.' And in Muhit and Dhakhira it is stated: 'The narration of Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifa is that when a woman has her own and her mahram's maintenance, then performing Hajj is obligatory on her, and the narrations from Imam Muhammad are different.' Then Ibn Kamal Pasha writes: 'From here it became apparent that the author of the margin meant by Zahir al-Riwayah the narration of Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifa; thus the difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul became clear. Because 'Usul' refers to al-Mabsut, Jami' al-Saghir, Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Siyar al-Kabir, and these books do not contain the narration of Hasan. These are all narrations of Imam Muhammad. Also it became known that a narration of Nawadir can sometimes be Zahir al-Riwayah, and Nawadir narrations refer to narrations besides those of the books of Usul.' Then at the end Ibn Kamal Pasha writes emphatically: 'Keep this in mind, because this aspect has remained hidden from the commentators of Hidayah, and some commentators of Hidayah have clearly stated that there is no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul. They think that a narration of Nawadir cannot be Zahir al-Riwayah.' (End of Ibn Kamal Pasha's statement.) Clarification: The gist of Ibn Kamal Pasha's opinion is that Riwayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah have a relationship of general and specific absolute. Riwayat al-Usul is specific and Zahir al-Riwayah is general. Because Riwayat al-Usul is said of the issues of Imam Muhammad's six books, and Zahir al-Riwayah is commonly said of the narrations of the six books, but sometimes the narrations of Nawadir are also called Zahir al-Riwayah. Response: I (Allama Shami) say: It will not be hidden from you that the statement of Muhit and Dhakhira 'This is a narration of Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifa' does not necessarily imply that it is against the narration of Usul. Because it is possible that Hasan narrated it from Imam Abu Hanifa in other books, and Imam Muhammad also narrated it in the books of Usul, and the reason for mentioning Hasan's narration is only that there is no inconsistency in it, because they themselves have clarified that Imam Muhammad's narrations are different. So the author of the margin saying that it is Zahir al-Riwayah means that Imam Muhammad mentioned it in the books of Usul, because among the different narrations of Imam Muhammad in Usul from Imam Azam, this is one of them. Therefore, concluding that a narration of Nawadir can sometimes be Zahir al-Riwayah is not correct. Yes, it can be concluded that the narrations of Nawadir that are also mentioned in the books of Usul, like this one.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly dispute about the precise relationship between two technical terms in Hanafi usul al-iftā: Riwayat al-Usul (the narrations found in the six core books of Imam Muhammad) and Zahir al-Riwayah (the apparent/prominent narrations). The passage begins with background on how commentators interwove their explanations with Imam Muhammad's texts. It then presents Ibn Kamal Pasha's argument that there is a difference: he claims that a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad (from Imam Abu Hanifa) is called Zahir al-Riwayah but is not from the Usul books, thus Nawadir (non-Usul) can be Zahir al-Riwayah. Allama Shami responds, rejecting this conclusion. Shami argues that the mere fact that Muhit and Dhakhira attribute a ruling to Hasan's narration does not mean it is not also in the Usul; it could be both. The author of the margin (Sarkhasi) calling it Zahir al-Riwayah simply means it is in the Usul books. Therefore, a Nawadir narration can only be called Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also found in the Usul books; but the category of Nawadir as such is not Zahir al-Riwayah. The lesson for the mufti is precision: 'Riwayat al-Usul' is specific (the six books), while 'Zahir al-Riwayah' is broader (generally Usul but occasionally includes Nawadir if also in Usul). Shami's position is that the terms are not entirely distinct; rather, Riwayat al-Usul is a subset of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent/prominent narrations that are relied upon for fatwa; generally from the six books of Imam Muhammad, but sometimes includes narrations from Nawadir if also present in Usul.
روایت الاصول (Riwayat al-Usul): The narrations found specifically in Imam Muhammad's six core books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare narrations transmitted from Hanafi imams but not included in the six books of Usul; sometimes called 'riwayat al-nawadir'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allama Shami's response in the passage, what condition allows a narration from Nawadir to be considered Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) It must be from Imam Muhammad's transmission.
B) It must also be found in the books of Usul.
C) It must be cited by Sarkhasi in his Mabsut.
D) It must be from Hasan ibn Ziyad.

Key Takeaway
Riwayat al-Usul is a subset of Zahir al-Riwayah; a Nawadir narration is only Zahir al-Riwayah if corroborated by the Usul books.

Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir: When Does a Rare Transmission Become Authoritative?
Ibn 'Abidin refines Ibn Kamal Pasha's view on Nawadir and Zahir al-Riwayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relationship between Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, and apply Ibn 'Abidin's refinement to determine the authority level of a Naradir transmission found in both Nawadir and the six core books.

Core Idea
A Nawadir ruling is only Zahir al-Riwayah if also in Imam Muhammad's six books.

In Hanafi fatwa methodology, the authority of a ruling depends on its transmission history. Ibn Kamal Pasha argued that Nawadir can sometimes be considered Zahir al-Riwayah. In this passage, Ibn 'Abidin refines that claim: only Nawadir that also appear in the six core books of Imam Muhammad qualify as Zahir al-Riwayah. This distinction ensures a clear hierarchy for fatwa-giving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refined
Recognize Ibn Kamal Pasha's argument that Nawadir can be Zahir al-Riwayah because Zahir al-Riwayah is more general than Rawayat al-Usul.
Ibn Kamal Pasha's exact words are given in the source.
2
Analyze the evidence from al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah
Al-Sarkhasi calls a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad 'Zahir al-Riwayah'. Examine what this implies about the ruling's presence in the Usul.
3
Apply Ibn 'Abidin's critical distinction
Understand that al-Sarkhasi's usage only means the ruling is also in the books of Usul, not that every Nawadir becomes Zahir al-Riwayah.
Ibn 'Abidin shows the flaw in generalizing from a single case.
4
Derive the rule
Formulate the rule: Nawadir are considered Zahir al-Riwayah if and only if the same ruling is found in one of Imam Muhammad's six core books.
Otherwise they remain Nawadir.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is the authority weight assigned to a ruling for fatwa. This determines which ruling a mufti prioritizes.

ان کتابوں میں حسن کی روایت نہیں ہے۔ یہ سب کتابیں امام محمد کی روایتیں ہیں۔ نیز یہ بات بھی معلوم ہوگئی کہ نوادر کی روایت بھی کبھی ظاہر الروایہ ہو سکتی ہے اور نوادر کی روایت سے مراد اصول کے علاوہ باقی کتابوں کی روایتیں ہیں۔" پھر آخر میں ابن کمال پاشا تا کید کرتے ہوئے لکھتے ہیں کہ : اس بات کو یا درکھیں ۔ کیونکہ یہ پہلو ہدایہ کے شارحین سے مخفی رہ گیا ہے اور ہدایہ کے بعض شارحین نے تو صراحت کر دی ہے کہ ظاہر الروایہ اور روایت الاصول میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ ان کا خیال ہے کہ نوادر کی روایت ظاہر الروایہ نہیں ہو سکتی ۔‘ ( ابن کمال پاشا کی عبارت پوری ہوئی )
وضاحت
ابن کمال پاشا کی رائے کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ روایت الاصول اور ظاہر الروایہ میں عام خاص مطلق کی نسبت ہے۔ روایت الاصول خاص ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ عام۔ کیونکہ روایت الاصول امام محمد کی چھ کتابوں کے مسائل ہی کو کہا جاتا ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ عام طور پر تو کتب ستہ کی روایات کو کہا جاتا ہے۔ مگر کبھی نوادر کی روایات کو بھی ظاہر الروایہ کہ دیا جاتا ہے۔
جواب:
میں ( علامہ شامی ) کہتا ہوں کہ آپ سے یہ بات مخفی نہیں ہوگی کہ محیط اور ذخیرہ کا یہ قول کہ " یہ حسن کی امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے۔ " اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ وہ اصول کی روایت کے خلاف ہوں ۔ کیونکہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کو حسن بھی امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کرتے ہوں اور امام محمد نے بھی اس کو کتب اصول میں روایت کیا ہو اور حسن کی روایت ذکر کرنے کی وجہ صرف یہ ہو کہ اس میں اضطراب نہیں ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے خود اس کی صراحت کی ہے کہ امام محمد کی روایتیں مختلف ہیں۔ پس سرخی کا یہ کہنا کہ وہ ظاہر الروایہ ہے اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ امام محمد نے اس کو کتب اصول میں ذکر کیا ہے کیونکہ امام محمد نے اصول میں امام اعظم کی جو مختلف روایتیں ذکر کی ہیں، ان میں سے ایک یہ بھی ہے۔ اس لیے یہ نتیجہ نکالنا کہ نوادر کی روایت بھی کبھی ظاہر الروایہ ہوسکتی ہے صحیح نہیں ہے۔ ہاں یہ نتیجہ نکالا جا سکتا ہے کہ نوادر کی جو روایتیں کتب اصول میں بھی مذکور ہیں۔ جیسے یہ مسئلہ... وہ ظاہر الروایہ ہوسکتی ہیں۔ کیونکہ کسی مسئلہ کے نوادر میں مذکور ہونے سے یہ ہرگز لازم نہیں آتا کہ وہ کتب اصول میں نہ ہو۔ ابن کمال پاشا کی بات تو صرف اس صورت میں درست ہو سکتی ہے جب یہ ثابت ہو جائے کہ یہ مسئلہ ظاہر الروایہ کی کتابوں میں کہیں مذکور نہیں جب کہ محیط اور ذخیرہ کی عبارتیں اس پر دلالت نہیں کرتیں اور اندریں صورت ہدایہ کے شارحین پر جن کا کلام ہماری باتوں کی تائید کرتا ہے۔ غفلت کا الزام لگانا بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم ۔
There is no narration of Hasan in these books. All these books are narrations of Imam Muhammad. Also, it became known that the narration of Nawadir can sometimes be Zahir al-Riwayah, and by 'narration of Nawadir' is meant the narrations of books other than the Usul.' Then at the end, Ibn Kamal Pasha writes emphatically: 'Remember this point, because this aspect remained hidden from the commentators of Hidayah, and some commentators of Hidayah have explicitly stated that there is no difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Rawayat al-Usul. They think that the narration of Nawadir cannot be Zahir al-Riwayah.' (Ibn Kamal Pasha's statement ends.) Clarification: The gist of Ibn Kamal Pasha's opinion is that between Rawayat al-Usul and Zahir al-Riwayah there is a relationship of absolute generality and specificity. Rawayat al-Usul is specific, and Zahir al-Riwayah is general. Because Rawayat al-Usul refers only to the issues of Imam Muhammad's six books, while Zahir al-Riwayah generally refers to the narrations of the six books, but sometimes the narrations of Nawadir are also called Zahir al-Riwayah. Response: I (Allama Shami) say that it will not be hidden from you that the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah, 'This is a narration of Hasan from Imam Abu Hanifah,' does not necessitate that it contradicts the narration of Usul. Because it is possible that Hasan also narrates it from Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad also narrated it in the books of Usul, and the reason for mentioning Hasan's narration is only that it has no disturbance, because they themselves have explicitly stated that Imam Muhammad's narrations are varied. So al-Sarkhasi's saying that it is Zahir al-Riwayah means that Imam Muhammad mentioned it in the books of Usul, because among the various narrations from Imam A'zam that Imam Muhammad mentioned in Usul, this is one. Therefore, concluding that the narration of Nawadir can sometimes be Zahir al-Riwayah is not correct. Yes, it can be concluded that those narrations of Nawadir that are also mentioned in the books of Usul, like this issue... they can be Zahir al-Riwayah. Because a issue being mentioned in Nawadir does not necessarily imply that it is not in the books of Usul. Ibn Kamal Pasha's statement can only be correct if it is proven that this issue is not mentioned anywhere in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, whereas the statements of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah do not indicate that, and in this case it is also incorrect to accuse the commentators of Hidayah, whose words support our statements, of negligence. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a rasm rule concerning the hierarchy of Hanafi narrations. Ibn Kamal Pasha had argued that Rawayat al-Usul (narrations of the six books of Imam Muhammad) is specific, while Zahir al-Riwayah is general, and that Nawadir (rare transmissions) can sometimes be called Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn 'Abidin (Allama Shami) responds by carefully analyzing the statement of al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah. He explains that when al-Sarkhasi says a ruling reported by Hasan ibn Ziyad is 'Zahir al-Riwayah,' it means that Imam Muhammad also narrated that same ruling in his books of Usul, not that it is Nawadir masquerading as Zahir al-Riwayah. The true principle is: a ruling's classification as Zahir al-Riwayah depends on its inclusion in Imam Muhammad's six core books, not on its absence from them. Nawadir transmissions that are also found in the books of Usul are indeed Zahir al-Riwayah, but this does not mean that all Nawadir are Zahir al-Riwayah. Ibn 'Abidin thus defends the Hidayah commentators from Ibn Kamal Pasha's charge that they overlooked this subtlety. The passage is essential for understanding the authority weight of different layers of Hanafi texts: Zahir al-Riwayah (highest), Nawadir (lower), and later fatawa.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): Transmissions that are well-known and relied upon, primarily from Imam Muhammad's six books, but sometimes also used for narrations that appear in those books regardless of their original status.
رواية الاصول (Rawayat al-Usul): The narrations found in Imam Muhammad's six core books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare or less common transmissions, such as those from Hasan ibn Ziyad, not included in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Abidin, when can a Nawadir transmission be considered Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) Always, because Nawadir and Zahir al-Riwayah are synonymous.
B) Never, because Nawadir are inherently less reliable.
C) Only if that same ruling is also narrated in one of Imam Muhammad's six core books of Usul.
D) Only if Ibn Kamal Pasha explicitly declares it to be Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, a Nawadir transmission is only considered Zahir al-Riwayah if it is also found in Imam Muhammad's six core books.

Hierarchy of the Six Books: Authority and Precedence
Explains the chronological and authoritative ranking of the six books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy rule that later authorship takes precedence over earlier among the six Zahir al-Riwayah books.

Core Idea
When the six books conflict, the later authored book prevails — al-Siyar al-Kabir is the most relied upon.

This passage establishes a critical principle for Hanafi fatwa: the chronological order of authorship among the six canonical books determines their weight. Understanding this hierarchy ensures correct tarjih when contradictory narrations appear. The author also clarifies the correct pronunciation of 'al-siyar' to avoid common errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books and their order
List the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah in the order they were authored: al-Mabsut (first), then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and finally al-Siyar al-Kabir. Note that al-Mabsut is called 'al-Asl' (the foundation).
The exact order of al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Ziyadat may vary, but the key is that al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last.
2
State the qawida of later precedence
The maxim is: 'The relied-upon in the madhhab is the later authorship (al-mu'tamad fi al-madhhab akhir al-tasanif).' This means that if two books conflict, the one written later takes precedence.
This is because the later author had more time to review and refine earlier rulings.
3
Apply the rule to specific pairs
Apply the rule: al-Mabsut vs al-Jami' al-Saghir → al-Jami' al-Saghir wins. Al-Jami' al-Saghir vs al-Siyar al-Kabir → al-Siyar al-Kabir wins. Thus al-Siyar al-Kabir is the most authoritative among the six.
This hierarchy is only for rulings within the same level of transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah).
4
Recognize the exception for ijma
If a ruling from an earlier book is supported by consensus (ijma), the later book cannot override it. Ijma is a stronger proof than individual authorship order.
This exception is based on the qawida 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk).
5
Correct the pronunciation of 'al-siyar'
The word is pronounced 'siyar' (with kasra on seen and fath on ya), not 'sir' (dammi seen, sukun ya). 'Siyar' is the plural of 'sira', meaning mode of conduct, especially military expeditions.
Common mispronunciation can lead to confusion with unrelated words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سير کے معنی: سير سيرة کی جمع ہے جس کے لغوی معنی ہیں" کاموں کا انداز اور اصطلاح میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا جنگوں میں جو طریقہ تھا وہ سیرت کہلاتا ہے۔ ہدایہ ( ج ۲ ص ۲۵۳) میں ایسا ہی ہے ۔ اور مغرب ( ج ا ص ۴۲۷ ) میں ہے کہ: عرف عام میں السیر الکبیر کہا جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ سیر غیر ذوی العقول کی جمع ہے۔ پس صفت کبیرة آنی چاہیے۔ مگر لوگ مذکر صفت لاتے ہیں ۔ کیونکہ السیر مضاف کے قائم مقام ہے اور وہ کتاب ہے۔ اور تقدیر عبارت کتاب السیر الکبیر ہے ۔ جیسے عرف عام میں صلوٰۃ الظہر کہا جاتا ہے۔ جس کی تقدیر عبارت صلوۃ وقت الظہر ہے ۔ الظہر کو مضاف کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اور سیر الکبیر (مرکب اضافی غلط ہے جامع الصغیر اور جامع الکبیر غلط ہیں ۔“ ) مذکورہ بالا گفتگو سے واضح ہوا کہ السیر الکبیر میں لفظ سیر سین کے کسرہ اور یاء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ ہے اور وہ سیرۃ کی جمع ہے سیرسین کے زبر اور یاء کے سکون کے ساتھ نہیں ہے جو مفر و لفظ ہے پس بعض نا واقف لوگ جو السير الكبير کہتے ہیں وہ غلط ہے۔
وَاشْتَهَرَ الْمَبْسُوط بالأصل وَذَا لِسَبقِهِ البَيَّةَ تَصُنيفا كذا ١٨- الْجَامِعُ الْجَامِعُ الصَّغِيرُ بَعْدَهُ، فَمَا فِيهِ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ، لذا تَقَدَّمَا - وَاخِرُ السِّنَّةِ تَصْنِيفًا وَرَدْ السيرُ الْكَبِيرُ فَهُوَ الْمُعْتَمَدُ ترجمہ: (۱۷) اور مبسوط اصل ( جڑ بنیاد) کے نام سے مشہور ہوئی ہے اور یہ بات۔ اس کی تصنیف کے چھ میں مقدم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے (پس گویا وہ باقی کتابوں کی بنیاد ہے ) اسی طرح ۔ (۱۸) مبسوط کے بعد جامع صغیر ( باقی کتابوں سے مقدم ) ہے۔ لہذا جو بات جامع صغیر میں ہے۔ وہ اسی وجہ سے مبسوط سے مقدم ہے یعنی چونکہ جامع صغیر کی تصنیف بعد میں ہے اس لیے وہ بمنزلہ تاریخ ہے اور بوقت تعارض اس کے اقوال اصل کے اقوال سے مقدم ہوں گے۔ (۱۹) اور منقول ہے کہ چھ میں آخری تصنیف ۔ سیر کبیر ہے پس وہی معتمد علیہ ہے۔
تشریح: ذا اسم اشارہ کو نہ اصلاً مشار الیہ ۔ سبق مصدر مضاف الى الفاعل السته مفعول به تصنيفاً تمیز ہے جو نسبت کے ابہام کو دور کرنے کے لیے ہے۔ کذا کا تعلق آئندہ شعر سے ہے۔ مصرعہ رابع کی سلیس عبارت اس طرح ہے۔ فلہذا مافی الجامع الصغير تقدم على الاصل مصرعہ خامس میں تصدیفا بھی تمیز ہے۔ اصول اور غیر اصول کی روایتیں: پہلے یہ بات بیان کی جا چکی ہے کہ ظاہر الروایۃ کی کتابیں اصول کہلاتی ہیں ۔ ہدایہ باب استیم میں ہے دعن ابی حنیفہ والی یوسف فی غیر روایتہ الاصول الخ اس کی شرح میں ہدایہ کے شارحین لکھتے ہیں کہ: روایت 11 اصول سے مراد جامع صغیر، جامع کبیر زیادات اور مبسوط کی روایتیں ہیں اور روایت غیر اصول سے مراد نوادر امالی رقیات کیسانیات اور ہارونیات کی روایتیں ہیں ۔ ( عنایہ ج ا ص ۱۲۰) اور فقہا، بارہا کہتے ہیں کہ ذکرہ محمد فی الاصل اور شارحین اس کی تفسیر مبسوط سے کرتے ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ لفظ اصل جب مفرد ہو تو اس سے مبسوط مراد ہوتی ہے۔ اصول کی سب کتابوں میں سے مبسوط ہی اس نام کے ساتھ مشہور ہے۔ بحر رائق باب صلوۃ العیدین میں غایہ البیان (۴) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ: اصل کو اصل اس لیے کہا جاتا ہے کہ وہ سب سے پہلے لکھی گئی ہے۔ پھر جامع
Meaning of 'sir': 'Sir' is plural of 'sira', which lexically means 'mode of actions'. In terminology, the method of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in wars is called 'sira'. In Hidayah (vol. 2, p. 253) it is similar. And in Mughrib (vol. 1, p. 427) it says: In common usage, 'al-siyar al-kabir' is said, although 'siyar' is the plural of non-intelligent beings, so the adjective should be feminine (kabira), but people bring the masculine adjective because 'al-siyar' stands in place of the possessed noun and that is 'kitab', and the implied phrase is 'kitab al-siyar al-kabir', like in common usage 'salat al-zuhr' is said, whose implied phrase is 'salat waqt al-zuhr', 'al-zuhr' being substituted for the possessed noun. (And 'al-siyar al-kabir' as a possessive compound is wrong; 'al-jami' al-saghir' and 'al-jami' al-kabir' are wrong.) From the above discussion it is clear that in 'al-siyar al-kabir', the word 'siyar' is with kasra on the seen and fatha on the ya, and it is the plural of 'sira'; it is not 'sir' with damm on the seen and sukun on the ya, which is the singular word. So some ignorant people who say 'al-sir al-kabir' are wrong.
And al-Mabsut became famous as 'al-Asl', and that is because of its precedence over the six in authorship, likewise. (18) After al-Mabsut is al-Jami' al-Saghir, so what is in it takes precedence over al-Asl, therefore it is advanced. (19) And the last of the six in authorship is al-Siyar al-Kabir, so it is the relied-upon.
Tashrih: 'Dha' is a demonstrative pronoun, 'islan' is the referent. 'Sabq' is a verbal noun annexed to the agent. 'Al-sittah' is the object, 'tasnifan' is a distinction that removes ambiguity of relationship. 'Kadha' relates to the next verse. The smooth expression of the fourth hemistich is: So for this reason what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir takes precedence over al-Asl. In the fifth hemistich, 'tasnifan' is also a distinction. Riwayat al-usul and riwayat ghayr al-usul: It was previously stated that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are called 'usul'. In Hidayah, Bab al-Istim it says: 'from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in their narration other than al-usul' etc. In its commentary, the commentators of Hidayah write: 'By riwayat al-usul is meant the narrations of al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut; and by riwayat ghayr al-usul is meant the narrations of al-Nawadir, al-Amali, al-Raqiyat, al-Kaysaniyat, and al-Haruniyat.' (Inayah, vol. 1, p. 120). And jurists often say: 'Muhammad mentioned it in al-Asl' and commentators interpret it as al-Mabsut. It became known that when the word 'Asl' is used in the singular, it means al-Mabsut. Among all the books of usul, al-Mabsut is famous with this name. In Bahr al-Raiq, Bab Salat al-Eidayn, from Ghayat al-Bayan (4) it is narrated: 'Al-Asl is called al-Asl because it was written first, then al-Jami'.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the hierarchy of the six authoritative books (Zahir al-Riwayah) in the Hanafi madhhab. It explains the chronological order of authorship and the resulting precedence when conflicting narrations occur. Al-Mabsut is known as 'al-Asl' (the foundation) because it was written first. However, because al-Jami' al-Saghir was authored later, its rulings take precedence over those of al-Mabsut in case of conflict. Finally, al-Siyar al-Kabir (the book on military expeditions) was the last written among the six, so it is the most authoritative and is considered 'al-mu'tamad' (the relied-upon). The author also clarifies the pronunciation of 'siyar' with kasra and fatha, warning against the erroneous pronunciation 'al-sir al-kabir'.

Key Terms
الاصل (al-asl): Refers specifically to al-Mabsut by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the first written book among the six
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The six books authored by Imam Muhammad that are transmitted with high reliability
السير الكبير (al-siyar al-kabir): The large book on maghazi and siyar by Imam Muhammad, last of the six

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hierarchy of Hanafi authoritative books, which book is considered the most relied-upon (al-mu'tamad)?
A) Al-Mabsut (al-Asl)
B) Al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) Al-Siyar al-Kabir
D) Al-Jami' al-Kabir

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, chronological recency among the six Zahir al-Riwayah books determines authority: the later book, especially al-Siyar al-Kabir, is the relied-upon reference.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
