Hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah: The Principle of Chronological Precedence
Explaining the chronological precedence rule for the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the chronological order of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and apply the rule that later compositions take precedence over earlier ones in case of conflict.

Core Idea
Later compositions in Zahir al-Riwayah override earlier ones; thus al-Jami' al-Saghir supersedes al-Mabsut.

This passage from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti establishes a crucial methodological rule for Hanafi muftis: when conflicting narrations exist within the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah, the later-authored work carries greater authority. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for resolving apparent contradictions in the madhhab's primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books and their chronological order
List the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah as mentioned: al-Mabsut (first), then al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Siyar al-Kabir (last). Recognize that al-Siyar al-Kabir is the final composition.
The passage uses a verse (not quoted in full) that indicates this order.
2
Understand the precedence principle
The key rule: 'The later composition takes precedence over the earlier.' Because al-Jami' al-Saghir was written after al-Mabsut, its rulings override those of al-Mabsut in case of contradiction.
The analogy is made to a 'date' (tarikh) indicating later time.
3
Apply the principle to al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir
If a ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir conflicts with one in al-Mabsut, the ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir is preferred. The passage states 'whatever is in al-Jami' al-Saghir is for that reason given precedence over al-Mabsut.'
This is a direct application of the chronological rule.
4
Recognize the status of al-Siyar al-Kabir
Since al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last of the six, it is the most authoritative. The passage notes that it is 'the relied upon' (mu'tamad 'alayh).
This implies that among all six, it has the highest rank.
5
Distinguish 'asl' and 'usul'
The word 'asl' when used alone refers specifically to al-Mabsut. The plural 'usul' encompasses the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. Non-usul narrations (ghayr usul) come from other sources like Nawadir.
This terminological precision is crucial for reading Hanafi texts.

جامع صغیر کی وجہ تصنیف:

کی۔ آپ نے اس کو بہت پسند فرمایا۔ جامع صغیر کا تعارف:
جامع صغیر ایک با برکت کتاب ہے۔ اس میں بزدوی رحمہ اللہ (۲۱) کے بیان کے مطابق ایک ہزار پانچ سو بتیس (۱۵۳۲) مسائل میں اور بعض علماء نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ باوجو د جلالت شان کے ہمیشہ سفر و حضر میں یہ کتاب ساتھ رکھتے تھے اور علی رازی رحمہ اللہ (۷۳) فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ جو شخص اس کتاب کو سمجھ لے وہ احناف میں فہیم ترین آدمی ہے۔ اور احناف جب تک اس کتاب میں امتحان نہیں لیتے تھے کسی کو عہدہ قضا پر فائز نہیں کرتے تھے ۔ اور غایہ البیان (۴) میں فخر الاسلام بزدوی (۲۱) سے نقل کیا ہے کہ جب امام ابو یوسف کے سامنے جامع صغیر پیش کی گئی تو آپ نے اس کو بہت پسند فرمایا اور ارشاد فر مایا کہ: ابو عبدالله ( یعنی امام محمد ) نے میرے بیان کئے ہوئے مسائل خوب محفوظ کئے ہیں یا امام محمد رحمہ اللہ نے فرمایا کہ : " مجھے یہ مسائل اچھی طرح یہ میں البتہ ان کو سہو ہو گیا ہے۔ یہ کل چھ مسائل ہیں ان کو البحر الرائق باب الوتر والنوافل ج ۲ ص ۶۱ میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔
یہاں رسم المفتی میں ترکہ ہے۔ کشف الظنون ج اص 241 میں بحوالہ سرخسی یہ الفاظ ہیں۔ الا انہ اخطافی ثلاث مسائل ( مگر ان سے تین مسائل میں چوک ہو گئی ہے)
In Rasm al-Mufti, because it is given precedence among the six (so it is the foundation of the remaining books). Similarly, after al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir is given precedence over the remaining books. Hence whatever is in al-Jami' al-Saghir is for that reason given precedence over al-Mabsut, meaning because the composition of al-Jami' al-Saghir is later, so it is like a date, and at the time of contradiction its statements take precedence over the statements of the original (al-Mabsut). And it is narrated that the last composition among the six is al-Siyar al-Kabir, so that is the relied upon. Explanation: This demonstrative pronoun 'dha' is not originally the thing pointed to. 'Sabaq' is a verbal noun in the genitive construction with the agent. 'al-Sittah' is the object, 'tasnifan' is a tamiz to remove ambiguity of relation. 'Kadha' is related to the coming verse. The clear expression of the fourth couplet is like this: 'Therefore what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir takes precedence over the original.' In the fifth couplet, 'tasdikan' is also tamiz. Narrations of usul and non-usul: Previously it was stated that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are called usul. In Hidayah Bab al-Istim, it says 'from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in non-usul narrations...' In its commentary, the commentators of Hidayah write: 'The narrations of usul refer to the narrations of al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut, and the narrations of non-usul refer to the narrations of Nawadir, Amali, Ruqayat, Kisaniyat, and Haruniyat.' (Inayah, vol. 1 p. 120) And the fuqaha frequently say 'Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl' and the commentators interpret it as al-Mabsut. So it is known that the word 'asl' when used alone means al-Mabsut. Among all the books of usul, only al-Mabsut is famous by that name. In Bahr al-Raiq, Bab Salat al-Eidain, he quoted from Ghayat al-Bayan (4) that: 'Al-Asl is called asl because it was written first. Then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat were written.' Also in Bahr al-Raiq it is that: 'Imam Muhammad wrote al-Jami' al-Saghir after al-Asl, therefore whatever issue is in al-Jami' al-Saghir will be the relied upon.' (Bahr, vol. 1 p. 158) The reason for writing al-Jami' al-Saghir: The occasion for writing al-Jami' al-Saghir was that when Imam Muhammad finished writing al-Mabsut, Imam Abu Yusuf requested him to compile a book in which he should mention the statements of Imam A'zam on his (Abu Yusuf's) authority, and should not use his kunya but write the name Ya'qub. Imam Muhammad complied and prepared the book and presented it to Imam Abu Yusuf. He appreciated it greatly. Introduction to al-Jami' al-Saghir: Al-Jami' al-Saghir is a blessed book. According to Bazdawi, it contains one thousand five hundred thirty-two (1532) issues. Some scholars have mentioned that Imam Abu Yusuf, despite his great rank, always carried this book with him in travel and residence. And Ali al-Razi used to say: 'Whoever understands this book is the most understanding among the Hanafis.' And the Hanafis would not appoint anyone to the position of qadi without examining him on this book. And in Ghayat al-Bayan, it is quoted from Fakhr al-Islam Bazdawi that when al-Jami' al-Saghir was presented to Imam Abu Yusuf, he liked it very much and said: 'Abu Abdullah (i.e. Imam Muhammad) has preserved well the issues I narrated.' Or Imam Muhammad said: 'I have these issues well... but I have made a slip in them. There are six such issues, mentioned in Bahr al-Raiq Bab al-Witr wa al-Nawafil, vol. 2 p. 61.' Here in Rasm al-Mufti it is left. In Kashf al-Zunun, vol. 1 p. 241, quoting from Sarakhsi, there are these words: 'Except that I made a mistake in three issues' (i.e. he made a slip in three issues).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Rasm al-Mufti discusses the hierarchy of the six foundational books of the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah). The key principle is that among Imam Muhammad's works, the later composition takes precedence over the earlier in case of conflict. Al-Mabsut (also called 'al-Asl') is the earliest, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat. Al-Siyar al-Kabir is the last of the six. Therefore, al-Jami' al-Saghir's rulings override those of al-Mabsut. The passage also clarifies terminology: 'usul' refers to the six books, while 'ghayr usul' refers to other narrations like Nawadir. When 'al-Asl' is used alone, it specifically means al-Mabsut. The text further highlights the importance of al-Jami' al-Saghir, noting that Hanafi scholars had to master it before becoming judges, and that Imam Abu Yusuf carried it constantly. The author also notes a discrepancy: some sources say Imam Muhammad made three mistakes, others say six. This passage is a methodological rule for muftis: when conflicting narrations exist, prioritize the later authored book.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which are the most authoritative sources within the Hanafi school.
جامع صغیر (al-Jami' al-Saghir): The second book written by Imam Muhammad after al-Mabsut, containing 1532 issues; it takes precedence over al-Mabsut in case of conflict.
اصل (al-Asl): When used alone, it refers specifically to al-Mabsut, the first of the six books. In plural (usul), it refers to the six books collectively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The authoritative hierarchy among the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah is determined by chronological order of composition; later books override earlier ones, with al-Siyar al-Kabir being the most relied upon.

The Occasion for Writing Al-Jami' al-Saghir
Historical account of book composition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the historical reason for the composition of Al-Jami' al-Saghir and identify its chain of transmission from Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Al-Jami' al-Saghir was written at Imam Abu Yusuf's request to preserve Abu Hanifa's rulings through his direct transmission.

This lesson explores the specific occasion that led Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani to compile one of the most important Hanafi fatwa sources. Understanding why and for whom the book was written reveals its authoritative status in the madhhab and its reliance in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figures
Note the two main scholars involved: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the author) and Imam Abu Yusuf (the requester and transmitter). Also recall that both are direct students of Abu Hanifa.
Imam Abu Yusuf was the chief judge of his time, and his transmission is highly valued.
2
Analyze the request
Understand the specific request: Imam Abu Yusuf wanted a book containing Abu Hanifa's sayings narrated on his (Abu Yusuf's) authority, with his name Ya'qub used instead of the kunyah 'Abu Yusuf'.
This emphasizes personal transmission (riwayah) and the importance of naming.
3
Trace the composition process
Imam Muhammad had just finished al-Mabsut when he received the request. He complied by writing Al-Jami' al-Saghir and presented it to Imam Abu Yusuf, who approved it.
The book was produced after al-Mabsut, indicating it is a supplementary or focused compilation.
4
Assess the significance of the chain
The chain is: Abu Hanifa → Abu Yusuf → Muhammad al-Shaybani. This is a 'zahir al-riwayah' chain, making the book a primary source for fatwa.
Later Hanafi methodology gives preference to such direct transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جامع صغیر کی وجہ تصنیف:
جامع صغیر لکھنے کی تقریب یہ بنی تھی کہ جب امام محمد مبسوط کی تصنیف سے فارغ ہوئے تو امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ نے خواہش کی کہ وہ ایک ایسی کتاب مرتب کریں جس میں ان کی سند سے امام اعظم کے اقوال ذکر کیے جائیں اور ان کی کنیت استعمال نہ کی جائے بلکہ نام یعقوب لکھا جائے۔ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ نے تعمیل حکم کی اور کتاب تیار کر کے امام ابو یوسف کی خدمت میں پیش کی۔ آپ نے اس کو بہت پسند فرمایا۔

جامع صغیر کا تعارف:
جامع صغیر ایک با برکت کتاب ہے۔ اس میں بزدوی رحمہ اللہ کے بیان کے مطابق ایک ہزار پانچ سو بتیس (۱۵۳۲) مسائل ہیں اور بعض علماء نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ باوجود جلالت شان کے ہمیشہ سفر و حضر میں یہ کتاب ساتھ رکھتے تھے اور علی رازی رحمہ اللہ فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ جو شخص اس کتاب کو سمجھ لے وہ احناف میں فہیم ترین آدمی ہے۔ اور احناف جب تک اس کتاب میں امتحان نہیں لیتے تھے کسی کو عہدہ قضا پر فائز نہیں کرتے تھے۔
Reason for composition of Al-Jami' al-Saghir:
The occasion for writing Al-Jami' al-Saghir was that when Imam Muhammad finished writing al-Mabsut, Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) desired that he compile a book in which the sayings of Imam A'zam are mentioned on his authority, and his kunyah should not be used, but rather the name Ya'qub should be written. Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) complied with the order and prepared the book and presented it to Imam Abu Yusuf. He liked it very much.

Introduction of Al-Jami' al-Saghir:
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is a blessed book. According to the statement of Bazdawi (may Allah have mercy on him), it contains one thousand five hundred and thirty-two (1532) issues. And some scholars have mentioned that Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), despite his high status, always kept this book with him in travel and at home. And Ali al-Razi (may Allah have mercy on him) used to say that whoever understands this book is the most insightful person among the Hanafis. And the Hanafis would not appoint anyone to the position of judge until they examined him on this book.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule regarding the status of Al-Jami' al-Saghir in Hanafi fatwa methodology. It explains the reason for its composition: at the request of Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad compiled a work relying solely on Abu Yusuf's transmission from Abu Hanifa, using the name Ya'qub instead of the kunyah. The book contains 1532 issues according to Bazdawi. It was so revered that Abu Yusuf carried it constantly, and it was used as a test for judges. This establishes Al-Jami' al-Saghir as a primary source for fatwa, belonging to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
جامع صغیر (Al-Jami' al-Saghir): A foundational Hanafi fiqh work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing 1532 issues transmitted from Imam Abu Yusuf
امام ابو یوسف (Imam Abu Yusuf): A chief Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Hanifa, whose transmission is the basis of this book
امام محمد (Imam Muhammad): Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the author of Al-Jami' al-Saghir and student of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Imam Abu Yusuf
C) Imam Muhammad himself
D) Al-Bazdawi

Key Takeaway
Al-Jami' al-Saghir was deliberately compiled on the authority of Imam Abu Yusuf to ensure a strong, direct chain for Hanafi fatwa.

The Authority and Role of Al-Jami' al-Saghir in Hanafi Fatwa
Description of the book's virtues and institutional role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Al-Jami' al-Saghir is considered a blessed book and describe its role in the appointment of Hanafi judges.

Core Idea
Al-Jami' al-Saghir was so revered that Imam Abu Yusuf carried it always, and mastery of it was a prerequisite for judgeship.

Having understood the composition of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, we now explore its elevated status within the Hanafi school. The passage highlights two proofs of its authority: the personal conduct of Imam Abu Yusuf and its use as an examination standard for judges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the blessings attributed to the book
The text calls it 'blessed' (baraka). Note the specific actions of Imam Abu Yusuf and the statement of Ali al-Razi.
Baraka implies that studying and using the book brings benefit.
2
Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's practice
Despite his high rank, he kept the book with him at all times—in travel and at home. This shows his reliance on it for legal reference.
This was not typical for every book; it indicates special importance.
3
Examine Ali al-Razi's statement
He said whoever understands this book is the most insightful (afham) among Hanafis. This elevates comprehension of the book to a high level of expertise.
'Fahim' means deep understanding, not just memorization.
4
Understand the role in judicial appointment
Hanafis would not appoint a judge until they tested him on Al-Jami' al-Saghir. This establishes it as a standard for competence.
This practice demonstrates the book's centrality in applied fiqh.

جامع صغیر کی وجہ تصنیف:
جامع صغیر لکھنے کی تقریب یہ بنی تھی کہ جب امام محمد مبسوط کی تصنیف سے فارغ ہوئے تو امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ نے خواہش کی کہ وہ ایک ایسی کتاب مرتب کریں جس میں ان کی سند سے امام اعظم کے اقوال ذکر کیے جائیں اور ان کی کنیت استعمال نہ کی جائے بلکہ نام یعقوب لکھا جائے۔ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ نے تعمیل حکم کی اور کتاب تیار کر کے امام ابو یوسف کی خدمت میں پیش کی۔ آپ نے اس کو بہت پسند فرمایا۔

جامع صغیر کا تعارف:
جامع صغیر ایک با برکت کتاب ہے۔ اس میں بزدوی رحمہ اللہ کے بیان کے مطابق ایک ہزار پانچ سو بتیس (۱۵۳۲) مسائل ہیں اور بعض علماء نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ باوجود جلالت شان کے ہمیشہ سفر و حضر میں یہ کتاب ساتھ رکھتے تھے اور علی رازی رحمہ اللہ فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ جو شخص اس کتاب کو سمجھ لے وہ احناف میں فہیم ترین آدمی ہے۔ اور احناف جب تک اس کتاب میں امتحان نہیں لیتے تھے کسی کو عہدہ قضا پر فائز نہیں کرتے تھے۔
Reason for composition of Al-Jami' al-Saghir:
The occasion for writing Al-Jami' al-Saghir was that when Imam Muhammad finished writing al-Mabsut, Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) desired that he compile a book in which the sayings of Imam A'zam are mentioned on his authority, and his kunyah should not be used, but rather the name Ya'qub should be written. Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) complied with the order and prepared the book and presented it to Imam Abu Yusuf. He liked it very much.

Introduction of Al-Jami' al-Saghir:
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is a blessed book. According to the statement of Bazdawi (may Allah have mercy on him), it contains one thousand five hundred and thirty-two (1532) issues. And some scholars have mentioned that Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), despite his high status, always kept this book with him in travel and at home. And Ali al-Razi (may Allah have mercy on him) used to say that whoever understands this book is the most insightful person among the Hanafis. And the Hanafis would not appoint anyone to the position of judge until they examined him on this book.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule regarding the status of Al-Jami' al-Saghir in Hanafi fatwa methodology. It explains the reason for its composition: at the request of Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad compiled a work relying solely on Abu Yusuf's transmission from Abu Hanifa, using the name Ya'qub instead of the kunyah. The book contains 1532 issues according to Bazdawi. It was so revered that Abu Yusuf carried it constantly, and it was used as a test for judges. This establishes Al-Jami' al-Saghir as a primary source for fatwa, belonging to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
بزدوی (al-Bazdawi): A prominent Hanafi scholar whose statement is used to confirm the number of issues in Al-Jami' al-Saghir
علی رازی (Ali al-Razi): A later Hanafi jurist who praised the book and declared its comprehension as a mark of insight
قضاء (qada): The position of judge; appointment required examination on Al-Jami' al-Saghir

The Hierarchical Distinction Between Saghir and Kabir Books
Clarifies the distinction between books named Saghir and Kabir in Hanafi literature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Saghir and Kabir books in the Hanafi madhhab and explain how this distinction affects the weight of legal rulings in fatwa.

Core Idea
Saghir books reflect agreement with Abu Yusuf; Kabir books are Imam Muhammad's independent transmission from Abu Hanifa.

In Hanafi usul al-ifta, the classification of source texts is crucial for determining the reliability of legal opinions. This lesson clarifies the difference between books labeled 'Saghir' and 'Kabir'—a distinction that affects the chain of transmission and the authority of rulings derived from them. Mastering this rasm rule ensures that a mufti cites the most authoritative sources in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book category
Examine the book's title: if it includes 'Saghir' (e.g., Al-Jami' al-Saghir) or 'Kabir' (e.g., Al-Jami' al-Kabir). This is the first indicator of its transmission chain.
2
Trace the transmission chain
For Saghir books, the ruling was transmitted from Imam Muhammad to Imam Abu Yusuf and then to Abu Hanifa. For Kabir books, Imam Muhammad transmitted directly from Abu Hanifa without Abu Yusuf's review.
Saghir books are also called 'muttafaq' (agreed) books.
3
Determine the agreement status
Saghir books represent the agreement of both Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, providing a stronger consensus. Kabir books contain Imam Muhammad's own understanding, which may differ.
This consensus is why Saghir books are given preference in case of conflict.
4
Assess the fatwa weight
When a ruling appears in both a Saghir and a Kabir book, the mufta bihi (operative opinion) is from the Saghir book due to its higher authority. If only a Kabir book exists, it remains valid but with less weight.
Always verify the book classification before citing in a fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صغیر و کبیر میں فرق:
بحر بحث تشہد ( ج ا ص ۳۳۱) میں ہے کہ جن کتابوں کے نام میں لفظ صغیر ہے وہ امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نسیم اللہ کی متفقہ کتابیں ہیں اور جن کتابوں کے نام میں لفظ کبیر ہے وہ امام ابو یوسفی کو نہیں دکھلائی ہیں۔ اور محقق ابن امیر حاج حلبی (۷۴) نے مدینہ المصلی کی شرح حالیہ الحجاب میں تسمیع کی بحث میں لکھا ہے کہ: امام محمد نے اپنی اکثر کتابیں امام ابو یوسف کے سامنے پڑھی ہیں۔ مگر جن کتابوں کے نام میں لفظ کبیر ہے وہ امام محمد کی اپنی تصنیفات ہیں جیسے کتاب المضاربة الكبير كتاب المزارعة الكبير كتاب الماذون الكبير،
فائدہ
الجامع الکبیر اور السیر الکبیر اھ
علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے رد المحتار ج اص ۳۷ میں لکھا ہے کہ صغیر نامی کتا بیں امام محمد کی امام ابو یوسف سے روایتیں ہیں اور کبیر نامی کتابیں امام محمد کی براہ راست امام اعظم سے روایتیں ہیں۔
Difference between Saghir and Kabir:
In Bahr al-Ra'iq, the discussion on Tashahhud (vol. 1, p. 331) it is stated that the books whose names contain the word 'Saghir' are the mutually agreed books of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). And those books whose names contain the word 'Kabir' were not shown to Imam Abu Yusuf. And the researcher Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi (may Allah have mercy on him) wrote in the commentary of Madyan al-Musalla in the discussion of Tasmi' that: Imam Muhammad recited most of his books before Imam Abu Yusuf. However, the books whose names contain the word 'Kabir' are his own compositions, such as Kitab al-Mudarabah al-Kabir, Kitab al-Muzara'ah al-Kabir, Kitab al-Ma'dhun al-Kabir.
Benefit:
Al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Siyar al-Kabir, etc.
Allamah Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) wrote in Radd al-Muhtar (vol. 1, p. 37) that the books named 'Saghir' are Imam Muhammad's narrations from Imam Abu Yusuf, and the books named 'Kabir' are Imam Muhammad's direct narrations from Imam A'zam.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage provides a rasm rule regarding the classification of Hanafi source texts. It distinguishes between 'Saghir' and 'Kabir' books: Saghir books (like Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Siyar al-Saghir) are those that Imam Muhammad wrote in consultation with Imam Abu Yusuf and represent their agreed positions. Kabir books (like Al-Jami' al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Kabir) were not shown to Abu Yusuf; they are Imam Muhammad's independent compilations directly from Abu Hanifa. Allamah Shami adds that Saghir books are transmitted via Abu Yusuf, while Kabir books are directly from Abu Hanifa. This hierarchy affects fatwa: Saghir books carry the weight of two imams' agreement.

Key Terms
صغیر (Saghir): Refers to books agreed upon between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf, transmitted from Abu Hanifa
کبیر (Kabir): Refers to books written by Imam Muhammad alone, based on direct transmission from Abu Hanifa, not shown to Abu Yusuf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Saghir books are agreed upon with Abu Yusuf; Kabir books are Imam Muhammad's own
C) Kabir books are written by Imam Abu Yusuf
D) Saghir books are only about worship

Key Takeaway
The distinction between Saghir and Kabir books is a critical rasm rule that determines the authority of sources in Hanafi fatwa.

The Rule of Consensus by Silence in Imam Muhammad's Works
Rasm rule: silence on ikhtilaf indicates consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authority of rulings in Imam Muhammad's works where no ikhtilaf is mentioned and apply the rule that they represent the consensus of the three imams.

Core Idea
Silence on disagreement in Imam Muhammad's books signals the agreed opinion of the three Hanafi imams.

One of the most practical tools for a Hanafi mufti is knowing which rulings carry the highest authority. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's Zahir al-Riwayah works are central to the school, but how do we know when a ruling is the definitive position? This lesson introduces a key rasm rule articulated by Ibn al-Humam: when Imam Muhammad states a ruling without noting any disagreement, it indicates the consensus of the three founding imams. This rule streamlines fatwa by identifying rulings that require no further tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the rule
The rule is attributed to Ibn al-Humam as quoted by his student Allamah Qasim. Understand that the authority comes from the Zahir al-Riwayah works of Imam Muhammad.
2
Understand what silence implies
When Imam Muhammad mentions a ruling in his books and does not note any ikhtilaf (disagreement) among the three imams, it means he considers the ruling agreed upon.
This is a matter of usul: the default is consensus unless disagreement is recorded.
3
Apply the rule for fatwa
As a mufti, when you encounter such a ruling, you can rely on it as the mufta bihi (operative) position without needing to check for conflicting opinions among the three.
This rule simplifies tarjih; you can skip the step of weighing opinions.
4
Recognize the exception
Note that this rule applies only to the pattern in Imam Muhammad's books. It does not mean that no disagreement exists elsewhere, but within the Zahir al-Riwayah canon, silence indicates consensus.
Later works may still record disagreement; but for fatwa, this rule is decisive for the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متفق علیہ مسائل:
محقق ابن الہمام (۳۹) کے شاگرد علامہ قاسم (۱۰) کے فتوی میں علامہ ابن الہام کا یہ قول ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ جن مسائل میں امام محمد رحمہ اللہ اپنی کتابوں میں اختلاف ذکر نہیں کرتے وہ ائمہ ثلاثہ کی متفق علیہ رائے ہوتی ہے۔
Agreed upon issues:
In the fatwa of Allamah Qasim (10), the student of Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam (39), this statement of Allamah Ibn al-Humam is mentioned: That in issues where Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) does not mention any disagreement in his books, that is the agreed opinion of the three Imams.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a key rasm rule for Hanafi fatwa: when Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, in his Zahir al-Riwayah works, states a ruling without noting any ikhtilaf (disagreement), it indicates that the ruling is agreed upon by the three founding imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad himself. Such rulings carry the highest authority. If disagreement is present, the later preference between the imams' positions may be needed. This rule simplifies the mufti's task in many cases.

Key Terms
ائمہ ثلاثہ (A'immah Thalathah): The three foundational Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani
متفق علیہ (Muttafaq 'Alayh): Issues on which the three imams agree, indicated by silence on ikhtilaf in Imam Muhammad's books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ruling is weak
B) The ruling is agreed upon by the three imams
C) The ruling is from Abu Hanifa alone
D) The ruling is from Imam Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Silence on disagreement in Imam Muhammad's Zahir al-Riwayah works indicates the ruling is the agreed opinion of the three imams and carries the highest authority for fatwa.

The Supreme Authority of Al-Mabsut in Hanafi Fatwa
Rasm rule establishing textual hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm rule that Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate source for fatwa and that no contrary opinion may be followed.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut is the sun; no contrary opinion is given precedence.

In the Hanafi tradition, muftis must navigate a hierarchy of authoritative texts. This passage from Rasm al-Mufti establishes that Al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is the most trusted commentary, superseding all others. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for sound fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Read the key sentence: 'Mu'tamad al-taql… lays yu'mal bi-khilafihi wa laysa 'anhu yu'dal.' Recognize that this means Al-Mabsut is the relied-upon source and no contrary opinion is acted upon.
The phrase 'mu'tamad al-taqlīd' is critical.
2
Understand the relationship between Al-Kafi and Al-Mabsut
Note that Al-Kafi compiles the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. Al-Mabsut is its strongest commentary. The authority of Al-Mabsut derives from being the commentary on the foundation.
Al-Kafi is the source text; Al-Mabsut is the authoritative explication.
3
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Consider: A mufti encounters a ruling in a later work that contradicts Al-Mabsut. According to this rule, the mufti must set aside the later work and follow Al-Mabsut.
This is an absolute rule – no deviation is allowed.
4
Recognize the biographical context
Appreciate that al-Sarakhsi wrote approximately half of Al-Mabsut in prison. This underscores the work's depth and the scholarly sacrifice behind it.
The author's imprisonment did not diminish his scholarly output.

Source Text

شروع رسم السلطتي
-
کیا ہو تو پھر اسی پر عمل واجب ہے چاہے وہ امام زفر رحمہ اللہ (۷۸) ہی کا قول کیوں نہ ہو۔"
وَيَجْمَعُ السِّتْ كِتَابُ الْكَافِى لِلْحَاكِمِ الشَّهِيدِ، فَهُوَ الْكَافِى أقْوَى شُرُوجِهِ الَّذِى كَالشَّمْس مَبْسُوطُ شَمْسِ الْأُمَّةِ السَّرَخْسِي -٢٣ مُعْتَمَدُ التَقُولُ لَيْسَ يُعْمَلُ بخُلُفِه وَلَيْسَ عَنْهُ يُعْدَلُ
ترجمہ: (۲۰) اور اصول ستہ کو کتاب الکافی جمع کرتی ہے۔ جو حاکم شہید کی ہے پس وہی کافی ہے۔ (۲۱) اس کی نہایت عمدہ شرح جو سورج کی طرح ہے۔ شمس الائمہ سرخسی کی مبسوط ہے۔ (۲۳) وہ نقل مذہب میں قابل اعتماد ہے نہیں عمل کیا جائے گا۔ اس کے خلاف قول پر
اور نہ اس سے روگردانی کی جائے گی۔
تشریح
چوتھے مصرع میں ضرورت شعری کی وجہ سے شمس الامہ باندھا گیا ہے اصل لقب شمس ائمہ ( اکابر علماء کے سرتاج) ہے۔ معتمد (اسم مفعول ) نائب فاعل کی طرف مضاف ہے اعتمد بھروسہ کرنا۔ خلف بمعنی خلاف ہے۔ عدل عنہ : ہٹ جانا رو گردانی کرنا۔
حاکم شہید کی کافی :
فتح القدير وغیرہ کتابوں میں لکھا ہے کہ کتاب الکافی میں امام محمد کی وہ سب باتیں جمع کر دی گئی ہیں جو اصول ستہ میں ہیں، جو ظاہر روایت کی کتابیں ہیں ۔ اور علامہ ابراہیم بیری رحمہ اللہ کی شرح اشباہ (۳۱) میں ہے کہ: یہ بات جان لیں کہ مسائل الاصول کی کتابوں میں سے حاکم شہید رحمہ اللہ کی کتاب الکافی ہے اور وہ نقل مذہب میں قابل اعتماد کتا ہے۔ مشائخ کی ایک جماعت نے اس کی شرحیں لکھی ہیں، جن میں شمس الائمہ سرخسی رحمہ اللہ بھی ہیں، ان کی شرح مبسوط سرخی" کے نام سے مشہور ہے۔"
مبسوط سرحسی کا مرتبہ
شیخ اسماعیل نابلسی (۷۲) لکھتے ہیں کہ علامہ طرسوسئی (۵۰) نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو بات مبسوط سرخسی کے خلاف ہو اس پر عمل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ صرف اسی کی طرف میلان اسی کے

آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟
۴۷
شرح رسم المفتی
مطابق فتوئی اور اس پر اعتماد ضروری ہے۔ اور علامہ تقی الدین بن عبد القادر تمیمی نے الطبقات السنیة فی تراجم الحنفیہ (۶۰) میں مبسوط سرخی کی تعریف میں بہت سے اشعار لکھے ہیں۔ ان میں سے کسی کے یہ دو شعر ہیں:
عَلَيْكَ بِمَبْسُوطِ السَّرَخُسِي فَإِنَّهُ هُوَ الْبَحْرُ وَالدُّرُّ الْفَرِيدُ مَسَائِلُهُ -١ -٢ وَلَا تَعْتَمِدُ إِلَّا عَلَيْهِ فَإِنَّهُ يُجَابُ بِاعْطَاءِ الرَغَائب سَائِلُهُ
ترجمہ: (1) مبسوط سرخسی کو مضبوط پکڑ کیوں کہ وہ ہی سمندر ہے اور اس کے مسائل ہی یکتا
موتی ہیں۔
(۲) اور صرف اسی پر بھروسہ کر کیونکہ وہ ۔ جواب دیا جاتا ہے رنبتیں دینے کے ذریعہ اس
کا سائل یعنی اسی سے ہر سائل کا مقصد پورا ہوتا ہے۔
اور علامہ شیخ محمد بہتہ اللہ علی اشباہ کی شرح (۳۱) میں لکھتے ہیں کہ : " مبسوط امام كبير محمد بن احمد بن ابي سهل سرخسی رحمہ اللہ (۲۰) کی تصنیف ہے۔ آپ کا شمار اکابر علماء میں ہے۔ آپ علم کلام کے ماہر علم فقہ کے شناور اور علم اصول فقہ کے زبر دست عالم تھے۔ شمس الائمہ حلوائی (19) کی خدمت میں عرصہ زبردست دراز تک رہے ہیں اور ان سے پڑھ کر فاضل ہوئے ہیں تا آنکہ وہ اپنے زمانہ میں علم النظر والاستدلال میں سب سے فائق ہو گئے تھے اور تصنیفات شروع کر دی تھیں۔ مبسوط کی تقریباً پندرہ جلدیں یعنی نصف کتاب اوز جند کے جیل خانہ میں املاء کرائی ہیں ۔ آپ کو جیل ایک ایسی بات کی وجہ سے جانا پڑا تھا جو آپ نے خیر خواہی کے جذبہ سے کہی تھی ۔ آپ کی وفات ۳۹۰ھ میں ہوئی ہے۔" فقہ حنفی کی مبسوطیں : فقہ حنفی میں بہت سی مبسوطیں لکھی گئی ہیں۔ مثلا امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ کی مبہ، طا امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کی مبسوط جو الاصل کہلاتی ہے۔ جرجانی (۵۳) کی خواہر زاده (۷۱) کی سر ، الائمہ ۔ حلوانی (۱۹) کی ابو الیسر بزدوی (۲۱) کی ان کے بھائی علی بزدوی (۲۱) کی ۔ سیدنا - الد بن سمرقندی کی اور ابواللیث نصر بن محمد (۵۱) کی مبسوطیں اور جہاں مبسوط مطابق بولی جائے تو علامہ
امام سرخسی کے والد کا صحیح نام احمد ہے رسم المفتی میں محمد ہے جو صحیح نہیں ہے۔
"Beginning of Rasm al-Mufti - 
If so, then acting upon it is obligatory, even if it is the saying of Imam Zufr (78)."
"And the six are gathered by the book Al-Kafi of Al-Hakim al-Shahid, so it is sufficient. Its strongest commentary, which is like the sun, is Al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi - 23. It is reliable in transmitting the madhhab; one does not act contrary to it, nor does one deviate from it."
Translation: (20) And Al-Kafi gathers the six principles. It is by Al-Hakim al-Shahid, so it is sufficient. (21) Its most excellent commentary, which is like the sun, is Al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. (23) It is reliable in transmitting the madhhab; one will not act upon an opinion contrary to it, nor will one turn away from it.
Explanation: In the fourth line, due to poetic necessity, 'Shams al-Umma' is used; the original title is Shams al-A'imma (the crown of great scholars). 'Mu'tamad' (passive participle) is added to the agent; i'tamada means to trust. 'Khulf' means contrary. 'Adala 'anhu' means to depart, to turn away.
Al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid:
In Fath al-Qadir and other books, it is written that Al-Kafi contains all the statements of Imam Muhammad that are in the six books, which are the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. And in the commentary of Ashbah by Allama Ibrahim al-Bayri (31), it is stated: Know that among the books of usul, Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim al-Shahid is the reliable book in transmitting the madhhab. A group of mashayikh wrote commentaries on it, among them Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi; his commentary is known as Al-Mabsut."
Status of Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi:
Shaykh Isma'il al-Nabulsi (72) writes that Allama al-Tarsusi (50) said: Whatever is contrary to Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi will not be acted upon. Only inclination towards it and reliance upon it is necessary.
And Allama Taqi al-Din ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Tamimi wrote many poems in praise of Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi in Al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya fi Tarajim al-Hanafiyya (60). Among them are these two lines:
"Upon you is Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, for indeed it is the ocean and its pearls are unique issues. And rely only upon it, for its seeker is answered by granting desires."
Translation: (1) Hold fast to Al-Mabsut al-Sarakhsi, for it is the ocean and its issues are unique pearls. (2) And rely only upon it, because the one who asks it is answered by granting of desires.
And Allama Shaykh Muhammad Bahita writes in his commentary on Al-Ashbah (31): "Al-Mabsut is the work of the great Imam Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Sahl al-Sarakhsi (20). He is counted among the greatest scholars. He was expert in kalam, skilled in fiqh, and a powerful scholar of usul al-fiqh. He stayed for a long time in the service of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwai (19) and became a scholar under him, until he became the most superior in his time in the science of nazar and istidlal and began composing works. He dictated approximately fifteen volumes of Al-Mabsut, half of the book, in the prison of Uzjand. He had to go to prison because of something he said out of goodwill. He passed away in 390 AH."
Mabsuts of Hanafi fiqh: Many Mabsuts have been written in Hanafi fiqh, e.g., Mabsut of Imam Abu Yusuf, Mabsut of Imam Muhammad called Al-Asl, of Jurjani, of Khaherzadeh, of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwai, of Abul Yusr al-Bazdawi, of his brother Ali al-Bazdawi, of Sayyid al-Din al-Samarqandi, of Abul Layth Nasr ibn Muhammad. And wherever 'Mabsut' is said absolutely, it refers to Allama Imam al-Sarakhsi's. The correct name of Imam al-Sarakhsi's father is Ahmad; in Rasm al-Mufti it is Muhammad, which is incorrect.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule from the work 'Rasm al-Mufti' discussing the hierarchy of authoritative sources in the Hanafi madhhab for fatwa. It establishes that the most reliable and indispensable reference is Al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. The earlier book Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid compiled the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah (the core works of Imam Muhammad), but its most authoritative commentary is Al-Mabsut. The rule states that any opinion contrary to what is in Al-Mabsut is not to be acted upon, and one must not deviate from it. This is a key principle for muftis: when issuing fatwas, they should rely on Al-Mabsut as the ultimate authority. The passage also provides a biography of al-Sarakhsi, highlighting his scholarly stature and the circumstances of writing Al-Mabsut. Additionally, it lists other Mabsuts in the madhhab but clarifies that the unqualified term 'Al-Mabsut' refers to al-Sarakhsi's work. The author notes a correction: al-Sarakhsi's father's name is Ahmad, not Muhammad as written in some copies of Rasm al-Mufti.

Key Terms
الْكَافِى (al-Kāfī): The book by al-Hakim al-Shahid that compiles the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah (Imam Muhammad's works).
مَبْسُوطُ السَّرَخْسِي (Mabsūṭ al-Sarakhsī): The extensive commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi on Al-Kafi; considered the most authoritative source for fatwa.
مُعْتَمَدُ التَقُول (Mu‘tamad al-Taqlīd): Reliable in transmitting the madhhab; specifically refers to Al-Mabsut as the trusted source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rasm rule in this passage, which book is considered the most authoritative reference for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid
B) Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi
C) Al-Asl by Imam Muhammad
D) Al-Mabsut by Abu Yusuf

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate authority for Hanafi fatwa; no contrary opinion is given weight.

The Authority of al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi in Hanafi Fatwa
Praise and biography of al-Mabsut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and explain why it is considered a primary source.

Core Idea
Al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi is the ocean of Hanafi fiqh; a mufti must rely on it as a foundational source.

This passage establishes the towering authority of Imam Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut in Hanafi ifta. Through poetic praise and a brief biography, the text shows why this work is indispensable for issuing sound fatwas. As a mufti, understanding the rank of this source is crucial for navigating the Hanafi textual hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source being extolled
The passage praises al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi through two couplets and a biographical sketch. Note that the work is described as 'the sea' and its issues as 'unique pearls'.
The couplets emphasize comprehensiveness and uniqueness.
2
Analyze the authority claim
The couplets instruct: 'do not rely except on it'. Consider what this implies for mufti practice—al-Mabsut is presented as the ultimate reference for Hanafi rulings.
This is a strong endorsement, but must be contextualized within later developments.
3
Examine the biography of the author
Imam Sarakhsi was a senior scholar expert in kalam, fiqh, and usul. He studied under Shams al-Aimmah al-Halwani and dictated half of al-Mabsut from prison. His death was in 390 AH.
The prison circumstances reflect his dedication and the work's credibility.
4
Connect to fatwa hierarchy
Relate the passage to the hierarchy of Hanafi sources: al-Mabsut belongs to the Zahir al-Riwayah level. Later works like al-Hidayah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar rely on it, but it remains a primary source for detailed reasoning.

Source Text

مطابق فتوئی اور اس پر اعتماد ضروری ہے۔ اور علامہ تقی الدین بن عبد القادر تمیمی نے الطبقات السنیة فی تراجم الحنفیہ (۶۰) میں مبسوط سرخی کی تعریف میں بہت سے اشعار لکھے ہیں۔ ان میں سے کسی کے یہ دو شعر ہیں:
عَلَيْكَ بِمَبْسُوطِ السَّرَخُسِي فَإِنَّهُ هُوَ الْبَحْرُ وَالدُّرُّ الْفَرِيدُ مَسَائِلُهُ -١ -٢ وَلَا تَعْتَمِدُ إِلَّا عَلَيْهِ فَإِنَّهُ يُجَابُ بِاعْطَاءِ الرَغَائب سَائِلُهُ ترجمہ: (1) مبسوط سرخسی کو مضبوط پکڑ کیوں کہ وہ ہی سمندر ہے اور اس کے مسائل ہی یکتا موتی ہیں۔ (۲) اور صرف اسی پر بھروسہ کر کیونکہ وہ ۔ جواب دیا جاتا ہے رنبتیں دینے کے ذریعہ اس کا سائل یعنی اسی سے ہر سائل کا مقصد پورا ہوتا ہے۔
اور علامہ شیخ محمد بہتہ اللہ علی اشباہ کی شرح (۳۱) میں لکھتے ہیں کہ : " مبسوط امام كبير محمد بن احمد بن ابي سهل سرخسی رحمہ اللہ (۲۰) کی تصنیف ہے۔ آپ کا شمار اکابر علماء میں ہے۔ آپ علم کلام کے ماہر علم فقہ کے شناور اور علم اصول فقہ کے زبر دست عالم تھے۔ شمس الائمہ حلوائی (19) کی خدمت میں عرصہ زبردست دراز تک رہے ہیں اور ان سے پڑھ کر فاضل ہوئے ہیں تا آنکہ وہ اپنے زمانہ میں علم النظر والاستدلال میں سب سے فائق ہو گئے تھے اور تصنیفات شروع کر دی تھیں۔ مبسوط کی تقریباً پندرہ جلدیں یعنی نصف کتاب اوز جند کے جیل خانہ میں املاء کرائی ہیں ۔ آپ کو جیل ایک ایسی بات کی وجہ سے جانا پڑا تھا جو آپ نے خیر خواہی کے جذبہ سے کہی تھی ۔ آپ کی وفات ۳۹۰ھ میں ہوئی ہے۔"
It is necessary to follow the mufta bihi and rely on it. And Allamah Taqi al-Din ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Tamimi in al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya wrote many poems in praise of al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi. Among them, someone's these two couplets: (1) Upon you is al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi, for verily it is the sea and the unique pearls are its issues. (2) And do not rely except on it, for verily its questioner is answered by giving desires. Translation: (1) Hold firmly to Mabsut Sarkhasi because it is the sea and its issues are unique pearls. (2) And trust only in it because the answerer gives through giving desires, i.e., from it every questioner's purpose is fulfilled. And Allamah Shaykh Muhammad Bahata Allah in his commentary on al-Ashbah writes: 'Al-Mabsut is the composition of the great Imam Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abi Sahl al-Sarkhasi (may Allah have mercy on him). He is counted among the senior scholars. He was expert in kalam, knowledgeable in fiqh, and a great scholar of usul al-fiqh. He stayed in the service of Shams al-Aimmah al-Halwani for a very long time and studied under him until he became the foremost in his time in the science of consideration and inference, and he began composing. He dictated approximately fifteen volumes of al-Mabsut, i.e., half of the book, in the prison of Uzjand. He was imprisoned because of a statement he made out of goodwill. His death was in 390 AH.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage establishes the authority of al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi as a central Hanafi text for issuing fatwas. The author, Imam Sarakhsi, was a towering figure who dictated a major portion of this work from prison. The two couplets emphasize that the mufti should rely on this text. The biography from the commentary on al-Ashbah outlines his scholarly credentials and the circumstances of his composition.

Key Terms
مبسوط (mabsut): A comprehensive fiqh text that expands upon a mukhtasar. Here specifically al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi.
شمس الائمہ (Shams al-A'immah): Title meaning 'Sun of the Imams', used for several Hanafi scholars including al-Halwani and al-Sarkhasi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut al-Sarkhasi is a foundational text for Hanafi fatwa, authored by Imam Sarakhsi who dictated half of it in prison.

Distinguishing the Correct Text: Al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut on al-Mukhtasar
Resolving a scholarly confusion about which text al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut explains

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct subject of al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut by distinguishing between two works sharing the label 'mukhtasar'.

Core Idea
Al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut comments on al-Mukhtasar, not al-Kafi; misidentification distorts fatwa extraction.

In Hanafi scholarship, knowing which text a commentary explains is crucial for correctly tracing rulings. A common mistake is assuming that al-Sarakhsi's famous Mabsut comments on al-Kafi, because al-Kafi is itself a summary (mukhtasar). However, Ibn Abidin clarifies that Mabsut actually expounds a different Mukhtasar by Hakim al-Shahid. This lesson walks through the evidence and reasoning to resolve the confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Confusion
Recognize that Khayr al-Din al-Ramli assumed al-Mabsut explains al-Kafi because both are called 'mukhtasar'. Understand why this assumption is problematic.
The label 'mukhtasar' is generic; many Hanafi works bear it.
2
Examine the Primary Evidence
Read Sarakhsi's own statement: 'I deemed it appropriate to write a commentary on al-Mukhtasar.' This does not specify which Mukhtasar, but the burden of proof lies on equating it with al-Kafi.
Sarakhsi's phrase is a direct quote from his introduction.
3
Analyze the Opposing Argument
Al-Ramli argued that al-Kafi is also a mukhtasar and that Mabsut often quotes it. However, this only proves al-Kafi is a mukhtasar, not that Mabsut is its commentary.
Frequent quotation does not imply the work is the base text.
4
Apply the Corrective Evidence
Ibn Abidin cites Ghayat al-Bayan, where quotations from al-Kafi are introduced as 'al-Hakim al-Shahid said in his Mukhtasar which he named al-Kafi.' This shows al-Kafi itself calls its author's work a mukhtasar, but Sarakhsi's reference is to a different work by the same author.
The phrasing in Ghayat al-Bayan confirms that al-Kafi is one of several mukhtasars by Hakim al-Shahid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں (علامہ شامی) کہتا ہوں کہ حاکم شہید کی تصنیفات میں مختصر السنن؟ اور الإشارات؟ وغیرہ بھی ہیں اور سرخسی کا یہ قول کہ : " پھر میں نے مختصر کی شرح کرنا مناسب خیال کیا " اس پر دلالت نہیں کرتا کہ سرخسی کی مبسوط کافی کی نہیں بلکہ مختصر کی شرح ہے جیسا کہ اشباہ کے حاشیہ میں علامہ خیر الدین رملی (۲۸) کو وہم ہوا ہے۔ کیونکہ کافی بھی مختصر ہے پہلے یہ بات آ چکی ہے کہ اس میں ظاہر روایت کی کتابوں کی تلخیص کی گئی ہے۔ اور غایۃ البیان (۴) میں بکثرت کافی کے اقتباسات اس جملہ سے شروع ہوئے ہیں۔ قال الحاكم الشہید فی مختصرہ اسمی بالکافی اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کافی کو بھی مختصر کہتے ہیں واللہ اعلم ۔
I (Allamah Shami) say: Among the compositions of Hakim Shahid are al-Mukhtasar al-Sunan and al-Isharat, etc. And Sarakhsi's statement, 'Then I deemed it appropriate to write a commentary on al-Mukhtasar,' does not indicate that Sarakhsi's Mabsut is a commentary on al-Kafi, but rather on al-Mukhtasar, as was mistakenly thought by Allamah Khayr al-Din al-Ramli in his gloss on al-Ashbah. Because al-Kafi is also a mukhtasar; it has been mentioned before that it summarizes the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. And in Ghayat al-Bayan, many quotations from al-Kafi begin with the phrase 'al-Hakim al-Shahid said in his Mukhtasar which he named al-Kafi.' From this it is known that al-Kafi is also called a mukhtasar. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by Ibn Abidin (Shami) correcting a misunderstanding. Khayr al-Din al-Ramli assumed that al-Sarakhsi's Mabsut was a commentary on al-Kafi because al-Kafi is a mukhtasar. However, Ibn Abidin argues that Sarakhsi's Mabsut is a commentary on the Mukhtasar of Hakim Shahid (possibly his other work, not al-Kafi). The key point is that both al-Kafi and other works can be called 'mukhtasar', so the term alone is ambiguous. The evidence from Ghayat al-Bayan shows that al-Kafi is also called a mukhtasar, but Sarakhsi's reference is to a different mukhtasar.

Key Terms
مختصر (mukhtasar): A concise fiqh text. Here it refers to the work that al-Sarakhsi commented on, not necessarily al-Kafi.
مبسوط (mabsut): An extensive commentary. Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is a major Hanafi reference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, what evidence shows that al-Mabsut is not a commentary on al-Kafi?
A) Al-Kafi is not a reliable text
B) Al-Kafi itself is called a mukhtasar in Ghayat al-Bayan, not the subject of al-Mabsut
C) Al-Sarakhsi never mentions al-Kafi
D) Al-Mabsut only quotes al-Mukhtasar

Key Takeaway
Al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut is a commentary on al-Mukhtasar by Hakim al-Shahid, not on al-Kafi; correctly identifying the base text is essential for accurate fatwa citation.

The Authority of Abu Hanifah's Transmissions in the Hanafi School
Rasm rule: Authority hierarchy in the Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of authority in the Hanafi school and apply it to determine which ruling a mufti should issue.

Core Idea
Only Imam Abu Hanifah's transmitted narrations are the ultimate authority; the Sahibayn's rulings are selections from those.

This short verse from a classical rasm al-mufti text lays out the foundational principle of authority in the Hanafi school. As a mufti, you must understand that the school's rulings are built on the transmissions of Abu Hanifah, and the opinions of his senior disciples are not independent but rather selections from his corpus. This hierarchy is essential for issuing correct fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim
Read the Arabic verse and note the central assertion: 'فلم يكن لغيره جواب' – there is no answer for anyone else. This establishes that only Abu Hanifah's transmitted positions are authoritative.
The word 'غيره' refers to anyone outside the chain of Abu Hanifah and his companions.
2
Parse the roles
Identify the two groups: the 'روایات منیفة' (distinguished narrations from Abu Hanifah) and the 'رفاق' (companions, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifah selected some narrations; the companions select from the remaining.
The companions are not originators of rulings but selectors from the Imam's transmissions.
3
Understand the hierarchy
The verse implies a clear order: first the narrations chosen by Abu Hanifah himself, then those selected by the Sahibayn. Later scholars cannot produce a 'جواب' (answer) that contradicts these.
This is the basis for the principle that a mufti must follow the strongest riwayah from Abu Hanifah.
4
Apply to a hypothetical
Consider a case where Abu Hanifah rules a sale valid, but Abu Yusuf rules it invalid. According to this verse, the mufti must adopt Abu Hanifah's ruling, because Abu Yusuf's view is a selection from the Imam's narrations, not an independent ruling.
An exception may arise if custom changes and the Sahibayn's view becomes preferred, as per 'العادة محكمة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم بان عن أبي حنيفة جاء ت روايات عدت مُنِيفةً اختار منها بعضها والْبَاقِي يَخْتارُ مِنْهُ سَائِرُ الرفاق -۲۵ فلم يكن لغيره جواب كما عَلَيْهِ أَقْسَمَ الأصْحَاب
And know that from Abu Hanifah have come numerous distinguished narrations. He chose some of them, and the rest of the companions choose from them. So there is no answer for anyone else, as the companions have sworn upon it.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a foundational rasm rule from a versified text (likely by Ibn al-Sa'ati or similar). It states that in the Hanafi school, the positions of Imam Abu Hanifah are the primary authority. Although his companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) also gave rulings, these are essentially selections from Abu Hanifah's transmitted narrations. Therefore, no one else's verdict (i.e., from later scholars) can override the Imam's ruling. The companions' oaths emphasize this hierarchy. This rule is crucial for muftis: they must base their fatwas on the strongest narrations from Abu Hanifah, or if none, then from the Sahibayn, and only then from later authorities.

Key Terms
روایات منیفة (riwayat munifah): Distinguished narrations transmitted from Abu Hanifah
رفاق (rifaq): Companions (of Abu Hanifah), specifically Abu Yusuf and Muhammad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this principle, what is the status of a ruling by Abu Yusuf if Abu Hanifah has a different ruling on the same issue?
A) It takes precedence over Abu Hanifah's ruling
B) It is considered a mere selection from Abu Hanifah's narrations
C) It is of equal authority to Abu Hanifah's ruling
D) It is only valid if it contradicts Abu Hanifah's ruling

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the final authority is the transmitted narrations of Imam Abu Hanifah; the opinions of his companions are authoritative only as selections from those narrations.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
15 min
Rules for Preferring Conflicting Rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa
Establishing a hierarchy for tarjih among Imam Abu Hanifa's narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a hierarchy of tarjih for conflicting narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa and identify the mufta bihi using the rules of rasm al-mufti.

Core Idea
A mujtahid cannot have contradictory opinions; later opinions and supporting evidence determine the operative ruling.

This passage establishes the foundational methodology for preferring one narration over another when multiple conflicting rulings are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. It presents a clear hierarchy: first the later opinion, then supporting evidence, then ijtihad fi al-madhhab, and finally heart testimony. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any mufti or student of Hanafi fiqh to correctly determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core maxim
Find the usul principle that a mujtahid cannot have contradictory opinions on the same issue. This is the foundation for all tarjih rules.
This is stated explicitly in the commentary: 'مسئلہ میں مجتہد کے دو قول بر بنائے تعارض نہیں ہو سکتے'.
2
Apply the first tarjih rule: later opinion
If the dates of the narrations are known, the later opinion supersedes the earlier. This is the strongest form of tarjih.
The earlier opinion is considered as if it never existed (ruju').
3
Apply the second tarjih rule: supporting evidence
If dates are unknown, look for any indication from the Imam that strengthens one narration, such as additional qualifications or contextual evidence.
The text says: 'اگر کوئی ایسی بات امام سے منقول ہے جو اس کو قوی کرتی ہو'.
4
Apply the third tarjih rule: ijtihad fi al-madhhab
If no supporting evidence exists, a muqallid who has reached the level of ijtihad within the madhhab may prefer based on previous tarjih or personal conviction (shahadat al-qalb).
This is allowed only for those who have deep understanding of Hanafi principles.
5
Determine the fallback for common people and students
A common person follows a superior mufti; a student of fiqh follows the later scholars (mutakhkhirin) and acts on the more cautious opinion.
The passage emphasizes following the later scholars as a safer path.

میں اکثر علماء سے جو منقول ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مسئلہ میں مجتہد کے دو قول بر بنائے تعارض نہیں ہو سکتے۔ پھر اگر دوقولوں میں سے آخری قول معلوم ہے تو اس کو رجوع قرار دینا متعین ہوگا ورنہ بعد کے مجتہد پر بشہادت قلب ایک قول کو ترجیح دینا واجب ہو گا، جیسا کہ احناف کی بعض مشہور کتابوں میں ہے اور بعض میں ہے کہ اگر اقوال کی تاریخ معلوم نہ ہو تو اگر دو قولوں میں سے ایک کے ساتھ کوئی ایسی بات امام سے منقول ہے جو اس کو قوی کرتی ہو۔۔ تو وہی قول امام کے نزدیک صحیح ہے ۔ ورنہ اگر کوئی ایسا مقلد موجود ہے جو اجتہاد فی المذہب کے درجہ کو پہنچا ہوا ہے تو وہ گزشتہ ترجیحات کے ذریعہ ترجیح دے گا اگر کوئی مریج موجود ہو ورنہ دل کی گواہی سے جس قول پر چاہے عمل کرے اور اگر کوئی عام آدمی ہے تو وہ علم میں برتر اور تقویٰ میں بہتر مفتی کے فتوی کی پیروی کرے اور اگر فقہ کا طالب علم ہے تو وہ متاخرین کی پیروی کرے اور اس قول پر عمل کرے جو اس کے نزدیک زیادہ درست اور زیادہ مبنی بر احتیاط ہے۔ محقق ابن ہمام کی تحریر میں ایسا ہی ہے۔ وضاحت علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے مذکورہ بالا پورا مضمون علامہ ابن الہمام رحمہ اللہ کی مشہور کتاب سے اور اس کے شارح علامہ ابن امیر حاج طلبی رحمہ اللہ کی التقرير و التحبير ( ج ۳ ص ۳۳۳) سے نقل کیا ہے۔ اس کی وضاحت یہ ہے کہ اتنی بات تو ظاہر ہے کہ کسی مجتہد کے بیک وقت کسی مسئلہ میں دو یا زیادہ متعارض اقوال نہیں ہو سکتے، عقلاء کے کلام میں تعارض پسندیدہ بات نہیں ہے پس اگر کسی مسئلہ میں مجتہد کے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں تو ان پر ترجیح ضروری ہے تا کہ تعارض رفع ہو جائے اور وجوہ ترجیح درج ذیل ہیں۔ (۱) اگر مختلف اقوال میں سے کسی قول کے بارے میں معلوم ہو جائے کہ وہ امام کا بعد کا قول ہے تو وہی مرجوع الیہ قول ہو گا اور سابق قول یا اقوال کا لعدم سمجھے جائیں گے۔ (۲) اور اگر آخری قول معلوم نہ ہو سکے تو دیکھا جائے کہ کسی قول کے ساتھ کوئی ترجیحی امام العصر علامہ کشمیری قدس سرہ نے فیض الباری - ج ۱ ص ۳۵۷ میں بیان فرمایا ہے کہ ایک امام کے مختلف اقوال میں ترجیح سے بہتر تطبیق ہے اور اخیر میں لکھا ہے کہ: 'میرے نزدیک امام صاحب کی روایات میں بھی حتی الامکان تطبیق دینے کی کوشش کرنی چاہیے الا یہ کہ کسی دلیل سے دوسری صورت رایج قرار پائے ۔' یہ ایک مفید بحث ہے شائقین اسے ضرور ملاحظہ فرمائیں ۔
And know that from Abu Hanifa have come many narrations (riwayat). He selected some of them, and the rest are chosen from among them by the other companions. So no other has a response (opinion), as the companions swore. Translation: (23) And know that from Imam Abu Hanifa have come narrations that have become prominent. (24) Some of them were selected by Imam A'zam, and the rest are selected by the remaining companions. (25) Thus in Hanafi fiqh, there is no saying of anyone other than Imam A'zam, as the students of Imam have sworn. Explanation: 'Ghadā' (defective verb) meaning 'became'; 'Munīfah' (active participle) meaning 'elevated, prominent'. 'Ghadanī' is the attribute of narrations. 'Ikhtāra' meaning 'selected, chose'. 'Rifāq' is the plural of 'Rafqah' meaning group of companions. Different sayings of a mujtahid and the rule of preference: Know that what is transmitted in many books of usul al-fiqh from most scholars is that a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory sayings in one issue. Then if the later saying among the two is known, then it is determined to be the final saying. Otherwise, it becomes obligatory for the later mujtahid to prefer one saying by the testimony of the heart, as is in some famous Hanafi books and in others: if the dates of the sayings are not known, then if there is something transmitted from the Imam with one of the two sayings that strengthens it, then that saying is correct according to the Imam. Otherwise, if there is a muqallid who has reached the level of ijtihad within the madhhab, he will give preference through previous preferences; if there is a person capable of preference, otherwise he may act on whichever saying he wishes by the testimony of the heart. If a common person, then he follows the fatwa of a mufti who is superior in knowledge and better in piety. If a student of fiqh, then he follows the later scholars and acts on the saying that is more correct and more precautionary in his view. This is as in the writing of Ibn al-Humam. Explanation: Allama Shami has transmitted the whole discussion from Ibn al-Humam's famous book and its commentator Ibn Amir Haj's al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir (vol. 3, p. 333). The clarification: it is apparent that a mujtahid cannot have two or more contradictory sayings simultaneously; contradiction is not liked in the speech of rational people. So if different sayings of a mujtahid are narrated, preference (tarjih) is necessary to remove contradiction. The grounds of preference are: (1) if it is known that one saying is the later one, it is the referred-to saying and the previous saying is considered non-existent; (2) if the later saying cannot be known, then see if there is any preferential sign... Imam al-Asr Allama Kashmiri said in Fays al-Bari (vol. 1, p. 357) that applying reconciliation (tatbiq) is better than preference among different sayings of one Imam, and he wrote: 'In my view, one should strive as much as possible to reconcile the narrations of Imam, unless some evidence establishes another way as prevalent.' This is a useful discussion; those interested should consult it.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti ruling on how to handle multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. It begins by stating that Imam Abu Hanifa had many narrations (riwayat), some of which he selected as his own opinion, and the rest his companions selected. The students of Imam emphasized that no one else's opinion counts in the madhhab. The core rule is that a mujtahid cannot have two contradictory opinions on the same issue. Therefore, when conflicting rulings are attributed, tarjih (preference) is required. The hierarchy of tarjih is explained: (1) If the later opinion is known, it is final. (2) If not, look for supporting evidence from the Imam. (3) If a muqallid capable of ijtihad fi al-madhhab exists, he may prefer based on existing tarjih or heart testimony. Common people follow a superior mufti; students follow later scholars and the more cautious opinion. The passage also notes that Imam Kashmiri preferred tatbiq (reconciliation) over tarjih when possible. This teaches the systematic methodology for determining the mufta bihi (operative) opinion in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preferring one of two conflicting opinions based on evidence or rules of preference.
رجوع (rujūʿ): The act of a mujtahid retracting his earlier opinion and adopting a later one.
اجتہاد فی المذہب (ijtihād fī al-madhhab): The ability to derive rulings within the Hanafi school based on its principles.
تطبیق (ṭaṭbīq): Reconciliation of apparently conflicting narrations to avoid contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first step in preferring one of two conflicting opinions attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Follow the opinion of the majority of companions.
B) Determine which is the later opinion.
C) Apply the most precautionary opinion.
D) Follow the opinion of the student of the Imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi methodology for tarjih prioritizes chronological sequence, then supporting evidence, then ijtihad within the madhhab, and finally reliance on later scholars or caution.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Tarjih Among Conflicting Sayings of a Mujtahid
Rules for preferring one of multiple conflicting sayings of an Imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the methods of tarjih for conflicting sayings of an Imam and apply the appropriate method based on the status of the person seeking the ruling.

Core Idea
A mujtahid cannot hold contradictory sayings; later sayings or those with preponderant indications take precedence.

When different sayings are attributed to a single Imam, contradiction must be resolved. The Hanafi school provides a hierarchy of methods—chronological, indication-based, and subjective—depending on the level of the mufti.

Guided Path
1
Affirm the impossibility of real contradiction
Understand that a mujtahid cannot simultaneously hold two contradictory views. If two saying conflict, one must be later or there must be a method to prefer one.
This is a foundational premise.
2
Check chronological order
If the later saying is known, it constitutes ruju' (withdrawal) and supersedes earlier sayings.
The later saying is considered the final position.
3
Look for preponderating indications
If chronology is unknown, search for indications from the Imam himself, such as comments about a ruling being more suitable for the people or times.
Such indications make the saying the correct one according to the Imam.
4
Apply the hierarchy of persons
If no indication exists, the method depends on who is performing tarjih: a mujtahid fi al-madhhab uses usul methods or shahadat al-qalb; a mere faqih follows the mutakhirrin; a common Muslim follows the most knowledgeable mufti.
This ensures consistency across different levels of practitioners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسئلہ میں مجتہد کے دو قول بر بنائے تعارض نہیں ہو سکتے۔ پھر اگر دوقولوں میں سے آخری قول معلوم ہے تو اس کو رجوع قرار دینا متعین ہوگا ورنہ بعد کے مجتہد پر بشہادت قلب ایک قول کو ترجیح دینا واجب ہو گا، جیسا کہ احناف کی بعض مشہور کتابوں میں ہے اور بعض میں ہے کہ اگر اقوال کی تاریخ معلوم نہ ہو تو اگر دو قولوں میں سے ایک کے ساتھ کوئی ایسی بات امام سے منقول ہے جو اس کو قوی کرتی ہو۔۔ تو وہی قول امام کے نزدیک صحیح ہے ۔ ورنہ اگر کوئی ایسا مقلد موجود ہے جو اجتہاد فی المذہب کے درجہ کو پہنچا ہوا ہے تو وہ گزشتہ ترجیحات کے ذریعہ ترجیح دے گا اگر کوئی مریج موجود ہو ورنہ دل کی گواہی سے جس قول پر چاہے عمل کرے اور اگر کوئی عام آدمی ہے تو وہ علم میں برتر اور تقویٰ میں بہتر مفتی کے فتوی کی پیروی کرے اور اگر فقہ کا طالب علم ہے تو وہ متاخرین کی پیروی کرے اور اس قول پر عمل کرے جو اس کے نزدیک زیادہ درست اور زیادہ مبنی بر احتیاط ہے۔ محقق ابن ہمام کی تحریر میں ایسا ہی ہے۔

وضاحت

علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے مذکورہ بالا پورا مضمون علامہ ابن الہمام رحمہ اللہ کی مشہور کتاب سے اور اس کے شارح علامہ ابن امیر حاج طلبی رحمہ اللہ کی التقرير و التحبير ( ج ۳ ص ۳۳۳) سے نقل کیا ہے۔ اس کی وضاحت یہ ہے کہ اتنی بات تو ظاہر ہے کہ کسی مجتہد کے بیک وقت کسی مسئلہ میں دو یا زیادہ متعارض اقوال نہیں ہو سکتے، عقلاء کے کلام میں تعارض پسندیدہ بات نہیں ہے پس اگر کسی مسئلہ میں مجتہد کے مختلف اقوال مروی ہوں تو ان پر ترجیح ضروری ہے تا کہ تعارض رفع ہو جائے اور وجوہ ترجیح درج ذیل ہیں۔ (۱) اگر مختلف اقوال میں سے کسی قول کے بارے میں معلوم ہو جائے کہ وہ امام کا بعد کا قول ہے تو وہی مرجوع الیہ قول ہو گا اور سابق قول یا اقوال کا لعدم سمجھے جائیں گے۔ (۲) اور اگر آخری قول معلوم نہ ہو سکے تو دیکھا جائے کہ کسی قول کے ساتھ کوئی ترجیحی اشارہ موجود ہے یا نہیں؟ مثلا کسی قول کو خود امام نے ارفق للناس اوفق بالزمان یا اشبه بالصوار کہا ہو تو اسی قول کو اختیار کیا جائے گا اور وہی امام کا صحیح قول سمجھا جائے گا۔

امام العصر علامہ کشمیری قدس سرہ نے فیض الباری - ج ۱ ص ۳۵۷ میں بیان فرمایا ہے کہ ایک امام کے مختلف اقوال میں ترجیح سے بہتر تطبیق ہے اور اخیر میں لکھا ہے کہ: "میرے نزدیک امام صاحب کی روایات میں بھی حتی الامکان تطبیق دینے کی کوشش کرنی چاہیے الا یہ کہ کسی دلیل سے دوسری صورت رایج قرار پائے ۔ یہ ایک مفید بحث ہے شائقین اسے ضرور ملاحظہ فرمائیں ۔

(۳) اور اگر کسی قول کے ساتھ ترجیحی اشارہ موجود نہ ہو تو صاحب معاملہ یعنی جن لوگوں کو فتوی دینے کے لیے یا عمل کرنے کے لیے کسی ایک قول کو ترجیح دینے کی ضرورت ہے وہ تین قسم کے حضرات ہو سکتے ہیں۔ (۱) مجتہد فی المذهب (۲) محض فقيه (مفتیان زمانه ) (۳) اور عام مسلمان۔ تینوں کے احکام درج ذیل ہیں:

(الف) مجتہد فی المذہب اصول فقہ میں تعارض ادلہ کی بحث میں جو وجوہ ترجیح بیان کئے گئے ہیں ان میں سے کسی وجہ کے ذریعہ کسی ایک قول کو ترجیح دے گا اور اگر کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہ ہو تو اپنے دل کی گواہی سے جس قول کو رائج سمجھے اس پر عمل کرے اور اس پر فتوی دے۔ (ب) اور محض فقیہ (اور عصر حاضر کے سب مفتی اسی درجہ میں ہیں الا ماشاء اللہ ) متاخرین کی ترجیحات کی پیروی کرے یعنی متاخرین نے جس قول پر فتویٰ دیا ہے اس کو راجح سمجھے اور اس پر فتوی دے۔ ( ج ) اور عام مسلمان اپنے زمانہ کے اعلم واتقی مفتی کے فتوی کی پیروی کریں۔ وہ جس قول پر فتوی دے اس پر عمل کریں۔
In an issue, two sayings of a mujtahid cannot be based on contradiction. Then, if the later of the two sayings is known, then considering it as a withdrawal (ruju') is definite; otherwise, it is obligatory for the later mujtahid to prefer one saying by testimony of the heart, as is found in some famous Hanafi books. And in some books it is that if the date of the sayings is not known, then if with one of the two sayings there is something transmitted from the Imam that strengthens it, then that saying is correct according to the Imam. Otherwise, if there is a muqallid who has reached the level of ijtihad fi al-madhhab, then he will give preference through previous preferences if there is a preponderating factor; otherwise, by the testimony of the heart, he may act on whichever saying he wishes. And if it is a common person, then he should follow the fatwa of a mufti who is superior in knowledge and better in piety. And if it is a student of fiqh, then he should follow the later scholars (mutakhirrin) and act on the saying that is more correct and more precautionary in his view. That is what is found in the writing of Muhaddith Ibn al-Humam.

Clarification

Allama al-Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) has transmitted the entire above passage from the famous book of Allama Ibn al-Humam and from its commentator Allama Ibn Amir Haj Halabi's al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir (vol. 3, p. 333). The clarification is that it is obvious that a mujtahid cannot have two or more contradictory sayings on an issue at one time; contradiction is not liked in the speech of intelligent people. So if different sayings of a mujtahid are narrated on an issue, then preference (tarjih) is necessary to remove contradiction. The methods of preference are as follows: (1) If it becomes known regarding one of the different sayings that it is the later saying of the Imam, then that is the referred-to saying (marju' ilayh), and the previous saying or sayings will be considered as non-existent. (2) And if the later saying cannot be known, then it is seen whether there is any preponderating indication with any saying. For example, if the Imam himself has said about a saying that it is more convenient for the people, more in accordance with the time, or more similar to what is correct, then that same saying will be adopted, and that will be considered the correct saying of the Imam.

The Imam of the age, Allama Kashmiri (may his secret be sanctified) stated in Fays al-Bari (vol. 1, p. 357) that tatbiq (reconciliation) is better than tarjih among the different sayings of one Imam. And at the end he wrote: "In my view, one should try to reconcile the narrations of Imam Abu Hanifa as much as possible, unless a proof makes another course prevalent." This is a beneficial discussion; those interested should definitely consult it.

(3) And if there is no preponderating indication with any saying, then the person concerned — that is, the people who need to prefer one saying for giving a fatwa or for acting — can be of three types: (i) a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, (ii) a mere faqih (the muftis of the time), and (iii) a common Muslim. Their rulings are as follows:

(a) The mujtahid fi al-madhhab will prefer one saying through some method of preference from those which are mentioned in the discussion of conflicting evidences in usul al-fiqh. And if no method of preference exists, then by the testimony of his heart, he will act on whichever saying he deems prevalent and give fatwa accordingly. (b) And the mere faqih (and all muftis of the present age are in this category, except as Allah wills) should follow the preferences of the later scholars (mutakhirrin); that is, he should consider the saying on which the later scholars have given fatwa as preponderant and give fatwa accordingly. (c) And the common Muslim should follow the fatwa of the mufti of his time who is most knowledgeable and most pious; he should act on whatever saying the mufti gives fatwa on.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule explaining how to handle conflicting sayings attributed to a single mujtahid Imam. The author begins by asserting the fundamental principle: a mujtahid cannot hold two contradictory positions simultaneously; thus, if two sayings appear contradictory, one must be the later view (ruju') or a preference must be made. The text then presents multiple methods of tarjih, starting with chronological order: if the later saying is known, it supersedes earlier ones. If the order is unknown, one looks for implicit indications from the Imam himself, such as statements that a particular ruling is more appropriate for the people or for the times. The passage then introduces a nuance from the Hanafi tradition: some books say that if no indication exists, a mujtahid fi al-madhhab—a scholar capable of ijtihad within the school—should use the established methods of tarjih from usul al-fiqh; if none apply, he may rely on his own heart's conviction. For a mere faqih (which includes most contemporary muftis), the rule is to follow the preferences of the later Hanafi authorities (mutakhirrin) who have already weighed the evidence. The common Muslim must simply follow the most knowledgeable and pious mufti of his time. Important: the passage ends with a quote from Allama Kashmiri suggesting that tatbiq (reconciliation) is preferable to tarjih when possible, indicating that seeking harmony between conflicting narrations is more commendable than simply choosing one over the other. This is a key methodological point in Hanafi ifta.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one of two conflicting sayings or evidences based on preponderance
رجوع (ruju'): Withdrawal by a mujtahid from an earlier opinion to a later one
شہادت قلب (shahadat al-qalb): Conviction or testimony of the heart, used when no objective tarjih is available
متاخرین (mutakhirrin): Later Hanafi scholars whose preferences are authoritative for mere fuqaha
مجتہد فی المذہب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar capable of ijtihad within the Hanafi school, able to derive rulings from evidence within the school's framework
محض فقیہ (mujarrad faqih): A jurist who is not a mujtahid fi al-madhhab, knowledgeable in fiqh but not to the level of ijtihad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a 'mere faqih' (محض فقیہ) do when faced with conflicting sayings of an Imam?
A) Perform ijtihad and choose based on his own reasoning
B) Follow the fatwa of the later scholars (mutakhirrin)
C) Ask the public which saying they prefer
D) Ignore the conflict and give a fatwa based on his personal desire

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy for resolving conflicting sayings, ensuring that fatwas are based on the strongest evidence and are consistent with the school's established preferences.
