Distinguishing Ikhtilaf al-Aqwal from Ikhtilaf al-Riwayat
Distinction between conflicting sayings from the Imam and conflicting narrations from transmitters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a conflicting report about a Hanafi ruling is an ikhtilaf al-aqwal or ikhtilaf al-riwayat, and apply the appropriate resolution method as a mufti.

Core Idea
A conflict from the Imam is aqwal; a conflict from narrators is riwayat — origin dictates resolution.

Not every contradiction in the Hanafi school originates from Imam Abu Hanifa himself. Sometimes, transmitters (narrators) inadvertently create conflicts through memory lapses or differences in narration. This lesson draws a sharp line between genuine differences of opinion from the Imam (ikhtilaf al-aqwal) and transmission errors (ikhtilaf al-riwayat). Understanding this distinction is essential for a mufti to correctly navigate the madhhab's rich legacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of conflict
Read the passage and note that two categories are defined: ikhtilaf al-aqwal and ikhtilaf al-riwayat. Understand that the first originates from the Imam himself, the second from transmitters.
The passage uses the terms 'منقول عنہ' (the one from whom transmitted) and 'ناقل' (the transmitter).
2
Trace the origin of each conflict
Connect each type to its source: ikhtilaf al-aqwal is attributed to the mujtahid (Imam); ikhtilaf al-riwayat is attributed to the narrators. The passage explicitly states that sayings come from the Imam, whereas narration conflicts come from the transmitters.
This origin determines the next step a mufti must take.
3
Apply the distinction to the example given
Consider the example of Imam Abu Hanifa's rulings on women visiting graves. If the Imam himself gave both permissions and prohibitions at different times, that is a genuine ikhtilaf al-aqwal. If, however, the conflict arises from two different transmitters reporting opposite views, it is ikhtilaf al-riwayat.
The same set of reports can be classified differently depending on the origin.
4
Determine the proper resolution pathway
For ikhtilaf al-aqwal, a mufti applies tarjih (preference) or tatbiq (reconciliation). For ikhtilaf al-riwayat, the mufti investigates the reliability of the transmitters and the textual strength of each riwaya.
Mistaking one for the other leads to erroneous fatwas.
5
Explore implications for ifta practice
Reflect on real-world scenarios where a mufti receives conflicting fatwas from the madhhab. The first step is always to classify the conflict correctly before choosing which ruling to issue.
This distinction is a foundational tool in the mufti's methodology (rasm al-mufti).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلاف اقوال و اختلاف روایات میں فرق:

اور یہ بات جان لیں کہ دور داتیوں کا اختلاف دو قولوں کے اختلاف کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے کیوں کہ دو قول تو مجتہد کی صراحت کی وجہ سے ہوتے ہیں اور دو روایتوں کے اختلاف کا معاملہ اس سے مختلف ہے۔ الغرض دو قولوں کا اختلاف تو منقول عنہ کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے ناقل کی طرف سے نہیں ہوتا اور دوروایتوں کا معاملہ اس کے برعکس ہے (وہ ناقلین کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے امام کی طرف سے نہیں ہوتا ) یہ بات محقق ابن امیر حاج حلبی (۷۴) نے التحریر کی شرح التقرير و التحبير ج ۳، ص۳۳۴ میں بیان فرمائی ہے۔

وضاحت

ایک مثال لیجئے۔ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ نے ایک وقت میں عورتوں کو قبرستان جانے کی اجازت دی اور دوسرے وقت میں ممانعت فرمائی تو یہ اقوال کا اختلاف ہے جو منقول عنہ کی
Difference between ikhtilaf al-aqwal (conflict of sayings) and ikhtilaf al-riwayat (conflict of narrations):

And know this that the conflict of two narrations is not of the same category as conflict of two sayings, because two sayings occur due to the explicit statement of the mujtahid, while the matter of conflict of two narrations is different from that. In short, conflict of two sayings is from the side of the one from whom it is transmitted (al-manqul 'anhu), not from the side of the transmitter (naqil), while the matter of two narrations is the opposite (they occur from the transmitters, not from the Imam). This point has been stated by the investigator Ibn Amir Haj Halabi (74) in his commentary on al-Tahrir, al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir, vol. 3, p. 334.

Clarification

Take an example: Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) at one time permitted women to visit graveyards, and at another time prohibited it. This is a conflict of sayings, which is from the one from whom it is transmitted...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage draws a critical distinction in Hanafi ifta methodology between two types of apparent contradictions: ikhtilaf al-aqwal and ikhtilaf al-riwayat. Ikhtilaf al-aqwal refers to genuinely contradictory opinions attributed to the Imam himself, such as him changing his ruling over time. These are resolved by tarjih or tatbiq as discussed earlier. Ikhtilaf al-riwayat, on the other hand, refers to contradictory reports about the Imam's position that arise from mistakes or differences among transmitters (narrators). The example given is that Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly both permitted and prohibited women visiting graveyards; this could be a genuine change of opinion (aqwal) or a misattribution (riwayat). The passage stresses that the nature of the conflict determines how it is handled. The text as provided ends mid-sentence, but the key point is clear: the origin of the difference is crucial for the mufti to know whether to apply tarjih or to investigate the reliability of narrations.

Key Terms
منقول عنہ (al-manqul 'anhu): The person from whom something is transmitted, i.e., the Imam
ناقل (naqil): The transmitter who reports the Imam's saying
اختلاف اقوال (ikhtilaf al-aqwal): Conflict of sayings attributed to the Imam himself
اختلاف روایات (ikhtilaf al-riwayat): Conflict of narrations arising from transmitters

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the origin of ikhtilaf al-riwayat (conflict of narrations)?
A) The Imam's change of opinion over time
B) The transmitters (narrators) themselves
C) The common people's misunderstanding
D) The mufti's own reasoning

Key Takeaway
The origin of a conflict — whether from the Imam or from transmitters — determines how a mufti resolves it.

The Hierarchy of Tarjih and Distinction Between Aqwal and Riwayat
Explains tarjih hierarchy for fatwa and the distinction between aqwal and riwayat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi tarjih hierarchy by identifying which authority (mujtahid fi'l-madhhab, mahdh faqih, or common Muslim) should prefer a given opinion, and distinguish ikhtilaf al-aqwal from ikhtilaf al-riwayat when analyzing conflicting rulings.

Core Idea
Who does tarjih? The mujtahid fi'l-madhhab uses usul; the faqih follows mutakhkhirin; the commoner follows a mufti.

This passage from 'Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den' lays out the foundational rules for preferring one opinion over another within the Hanafi school—a core skill for anyone issuing fatwa. It first categorizes the people who need to choose between conflicting narrations, then clarifies a subtle but critical distinction between differences in the Imam's own statements (aqwal) and differences in what has been transmitted (riwayat). Mastering this hierarchy is essential for accurate fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels of tarjih practitioners
The passage divides those who need to choose a ruling into three: mujtahid fi'l-madhhab, mahdh faqih, and common Muslim. Understand the role and responsibility of each.
2
Understand the tarjih criteria for each level
For the mujtahid fi'l-madhhab, he uses usul al-fiqh reasons of preference; for the faqih, he follows the later jurists' preferences; for the commoner, he follows the most learned mufti.
3
Distinguish ikhtilaf al-aqwal from ikhtilaf al-riwayat
Recognize that aqwal originate from the Imam himself (e.g., a change of ruling over time), while riwayat differ due to narrators' errors or incomplete knowledge.
4
Apply the distinction to the four causes of ikhtilaf al-riwayat
The passage lists hearing mistakes and retraction unknown to some narrators as two causes; understand that these cause two transmissions, not a genuine difference in the Imam's position.

اختلاف اقوال و اختلاف روایات میں فرق:

وضاحت
ایک مثال لیجئے۔ امام اعظم رحمہ اللہ نے ایک وقت میں عورتوں کو قبرستان جانے کی اجازت دی اور دوسرے وقت میں ممانعت فرمائی تو یہ اقوال کا اختلاف ہے جو منقول عنہ کی
طرف سے ہے اور اگر امام صاحب نے تو کسی مسئلہ میں کوئی ایک متعین بات فرمائی ہو مگر ناقلین میں اختلاف ہو گیا ہو کہ کہ امام صاحب نے کیا فرمایا تھا؟ تو یہ روایتوں کا اختلاف ہے۔ پس جو فرق علامہ ابن امیر حاج نے بیان کیا ہے وہ نہایت واضح اور بد یہی ہے ۔ مگر مشکل اس وقت پیش آتی ہے جب ایک کی جگہ دوسرے کو استعمال کیا جائے ۔ یعنی قول کی جگہ روایت کو اور اس کے برعکس۔ کیونکہ ان اصطلاحات کے استعمال میں توسع ہے۔ آگے کی ساری الجھن اسی وجہ سے پیدا ہوئی ہے کہ اقوال اور روایات کی اصطلاحیں ہمیشہ حقیقی معنی میں استعمال نہیں
کی جاتیں۔ اختلاف روایات کے چار اسباب: لیکن ابن امیر حاج نے مذکورہ فرق بیان کرنے کے بعد امام ابو بکر بلیغی کی الدرر سے
نقل کیا ہے کہ امام اعظم سے روایتوں کے اختلاف کی چند وجوہ ہو سکتی ہیں ۔ (۱) بات سننے میں غلطی ہونا۔ مثلاً جب امام صاحب سے کسی معاملہ میں پوچھا گیا تو آپ نے نفی میں جواب دیا اور فرمایا کہ: " جائز نہیں مگر راوی پر بات مشتبہ ہو گئی۔ چنانچہ اس نے جیسا سنا ویسا نقل کر دیا۔ اور دوسرے راوی نے صحیح بات سنی اور وہی نقل کی تو مسئلہ میں دو روایتیں
ہوگئیں ) : (۲) امام صاحب کی ایک رائے تھی جس سے بعد میں آپ نے رجوع کر لیا اور جو رادی امام صاحب کے پاس آتا جاتا تھا اس کے علم میں وہ رجوع آیا اور اس نے آخری رائے نقل کی اور دوسرا راوتی جس کا آنا جانا کم تھا یہ آخری رائے اس کے علم میں نہ آسکی تو اس نے وہی پہلی رائے نقل کی تو مسئلہ میں دور ھوا ستیں پیدا ہو گئیں۔
لیکن استدراک کے لیے ہے۔ علامہ شامی رحمہ اللہ نے یہاں سے جو اعتراض شروع کیا ہے اس کی وضاحت آگے آئے گی۔ امام ابوبکر بلیغی کا تذکرہ مجھے کہیں نہیں ملا نیز التقریر و تحریر میں بلیغی کی کتاب کا نام "الغرز" ہے " الدرر" نہیں۔ خیال یہ ہے کہ یہ سب تصیفات میں صحیح نام عبد الرحمن بن ابی بکر العینی ہے جن کا لقب زین الدین شہرت ابن العینی سے ہے من ولادت ۸۳۷ ھ اور سن وفات ۸۹۳ ھ ہے ۔ انہوں نے علامہ قونوی (۲۵) کی درر البحار کی شرح لکھی ہے جس کے بارے میں حاجی خلیفہ نے لکھا ہے کہ احسن فيه و اجاد (کشف الظنون ج ا ص ۷۴۶ ) مذکورہ عبارت غالباً اسی شرح کی ہے واللہ اعلم ۔
You, how to give fatwa? 52. Rasm al-Mufti. Is there an indication present or not? For example, if the Imam himself said about a certain saying that it is more convenient for the people, more suitable for the time, or more resembling the [?], then that saying will be adopted and considered the Imam's correct saying. T (3) And if there is no preferential indication with any saying, then the people of the matter—i.e., those who need to prefer one saying for giving fatwa or for practice—can be three types of persons: (1) Mujtahid fi'l-madhhab, (2) mere faqih (muftis of the time), (3) and the common Muslim. Their rulings are as follows: (a) The mujtahid fi'l-madhhab will prefer one saying by means of one of the reasons of preference mentioned in the discussion of conflicting evidences in usul al-fiqh; and if no reason of preference exists, he will act on the saying he considers prevalent based on the testimony of his heart and give fatwa accordingly. (b) The mere faqih (and all muftis of the present age are in this rank, except as Allah wills) should follow the preferences of the later jurists—i.e., consider the saying on which the later jurists gave fatwa as preponderant and give fatwa accordingly. (c) The common Muslim should follow the fatwa of the most learned and most pious mufti of his time; he should act on whichever saying that mufti gives fatwa. Difference between ikhtilaf al-aqwal and ikhtilaf al-riwayat: And know that the difference of two transmissions is not of the category of difference of two statements, because two statements occur due to the explicit [ruling] of the mujtahid, whereas the difference of two transmissions is different. In short, the difference of two statements comes from the person from whom it is transmitted (manqul 'anhu), not from the transmitter; and the case of two transmissions is opposite (they come from the transmitters, not from the Imam). This was stated by the scholar Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi (74) in al-Tahrir's commentary al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir, vol. 3, p. 334. Explanation: Take an example: Imam A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) at one time permitted women to visit graves and at another time forbade it—this is a difference of statements, which comes from the one from whom it is transmitted. And if the Imam stated one specific thing on a matter, but the transmitters differed as to what the Imam said, then this is a difference of transmissions. So the difference that 'Allama Ibn Amir Haj mentioned is very clear and obvious. But difficulty arises when one is used in place of the other—i.e., using 'transmission' in place of 'statement' and vice versa, because these terms are used loosely. All the confusion ahead arises from this: that the terminologies of aqwal and riwayat are not always used in their real meanings. Four causes of ikhtilaf al-riwayat: After mentioning the above difference, Ibn Amir Haj quoted from Imam Abu Bakr al-Balighi's al-Durar that there can be several causes for the difference of transmissions from Imam A'zam: (1) Error in hearing. For example, when the Imam was asked about a matter, he answered in the negative and said 'not permissible', but the narrator became confused, so he transmitted as he heard, and another narrator heard correctly and transmitted that—so two transmissions arose. (2) The Imam had one opinion from which he later retracted. A narrator who frequently visited the Imam knew of the retraction and transmitted the final opinion, while another narrator who visited less did not know of the final opinion and transmitted the earlier one—so two transmissions arose. But this is for correction. 'Allama Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) began an objection from here, the explanation of which will come later. I did not find any mention of Imam Abu Bakr al-Balighi; also in al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir the name of al-Balighi's book is al-Ghurur, not al-Durar. It is thought that the correct name in all these books is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr al-'Ayni, whose nickname is Zayn al-Din, famous as Ibn al-'Ayni; his birth was 837 AH and death 893 AH. He wrote a commentary on 'Allama Qunawi's (25) Durar al-Bihar, about which Hajji Khalifa wrote that he excelled in it (Kashf al-Zunun, vol. 1, p. 746). The mentioned passage is probably from that commentary, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from 'Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den' is a rasm al-mufti text detailing the methodology of tarjih (preference) within the Hanafi school. It first discusses a scenario where the Imam himself has indicated a preference (e.g., saying a certain opinion is more suitable for the time), in which case that opinion is to be taken as the correct one. Then it addresses the case when no such indication exists, and divides those who need to choose an opinion into three categories. The mujtahid fi'l-madhhab is capable of applying usul al-fiqh principles of tarjih to weigh conflicting evidences. The mere faqih (which includes most contemporary muftis) must follow the tarjih of the later Hanafi jurists (mutakhkhirin), who have already determined which opinions are to be given fatwa on. The common Muslim should follow the most learned and pious mufti of his time. The author then clarifies a critical distinction between ikhtilaf al-aqwal (difference in the Imam's own statements over time) and ikhtilaf al-riwayat (difference in the reports transmitted from the Imam). This distinction is often blurred due to loose usage of terms, causing confusion. Finally, four causes of conflict in transmission are listed: (1) hearing mistakes by the narrators, (2) retraction by the Imam unknown to some narrators, and two others implied. The passage ends with a textual note correcting the name of a referenced book, demonstrating the precision required in scholarly citation.

Key Terms
مجتہد فی المذهب (mujtahid fi'l-madhhab): A jurist within the Hanafi school who can independently weigh evidences and prefer among opinions using usul al-fiqh principles.
محض فقیہ (mahdh faqih): A jurist who does not have the capacity to weigh evidences directly but must follow the tarjih of the later Hanafi jurists.
اختلاف اقوال (ikhtilaf al-aqwal): Difference in the statements or rulings of the Imam himself, often due to changing circumstances or later retraction.
اختلاف روایات (ikhtilaf al-riwayat): Difference in the transmitted versions of what the Imam said, often due to errors or incomplete information on the part of narrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mere faqih (mahdh faqih) do when there is no explicit tarjih indication from the Imam?
A) Perform his own ijtihad using usul al-fiqh.
B) Follow the preferences of the later Hanafi jurists.
C) Ask a common Muslim to decide.
D) Choose based on his personal opinion.

Key Takeaway
The key to sound Hanafi fatwa is knowing who you are: a mujtahid fi'l-madhhab can weigh evidence, but a faqih must follow the later jurists, and a commoner follows a qualified mufti. Always distinguish between genuine differences in the Imam's rulings and mere transmission variations.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Distinction Between Aqwal and Riwayat
Explaining the distinction between aqwal and riwayat and the four causes of ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a qawl and a riwaya in the Hanafi tradition and identify the four causes of difference in narrations, applying the tarjih mechanism to resolve conflicting reports.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fatwa methodology, a qawl is the Imam’s direct statement, while a riwaya is a transmitted version—precision in these terms is essential for correct tarjih.

This passage tackles a fundamental distinction in Hanafi iftaa: the difference between the Imam’s own words (aqwal) and the transmitted versions (riwayat). Understanding this distinction is crucial because later scholars often use the terms loosely, leading to confusion. The author presents four causes for differing riwayat and engages with a critical objection by Allamah Shami.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key distinction
Define qawl and riwaya as given in the text: qawl is a direct statement from Imam Abu Hanifa, while riwaya is a transmitted version that may contain errors or variations.
Note that the terms are often used loosely, causing confusion.
2
List the four causes of difference
Extract the four causes from al-Baliqi: (1) hearing error, (2) Imam's retraction unknown to some, (3) rulings based on qiyas vs istihsan, (4) rulings from perspective of qada vs taqwa.
These causes explain why multiple narrations exist for a single issue.
3
Analyze Shami's objection
Allamah Shami argues that the first two causes are invalid because the difference originates from the Imam himself, making aqwal and riwayat the same category. He suggests confining causes to the last two.
Shami's concern is about the epistemological validity of distinguishing qawl and riwaya.
4
Apply Ibn Amir Haj's defense
Ibn Amir Haj clarifies that al-Baliqi meant at least one cause applies, not all four in every case. The first two causes can be valid when narrators are different authors.
This resolves the apparent contradiction and preserves the usefulness of all four causes.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that all four causes are possible in appropriate contexts. A mufti must assess the context to determine which cause applies.
This guides the mufti in resolving conflicting reports from the Imam.

شروع رسم الملتقى
(۳) امام صاحب نے ایک بات قیاس کی رو سے فرمائی اور دوسری استحسان کی رو سے ایک راوی نے پہلی بات سنی اور اس کو روایت کیا اور دوسرے نے دوسری بات سنی اور اس کو روایت کیا جس کی وجہ سے مختلف اقوال پیدا ہو گئے۔ (۴) کسی مسئلہ میں حکم دو جہتوں سے ہوا ایک قضا کی جہت سے اور دوسرا احتیاط ( تقوئی ) کی جہت سے اور ہر راوی اسی طرح حکم نقل کرتا ہے جس طرح اس نے سنا ہے (پس اقوال میں اختلاف پیدا ہو جاتا ہے ) ( ابن امیر حاج کی بات پوری ہوئی )

اقوال و روایات میں فرق پر اعتراض: میں ( علامہ شامی ) کہتا ہوں کہ وجہ اول کو چھوڑ کر باقی وجود میں دو روایتوں میں اختلاف منقول عنہ کی طرف سے بھی ہو گا۔ کیونکہ ان میں اختلاف امام سے مروی دوقولوں میں اختلاف کی بنیاد پر سے لیس دانوں (یعنی قول اور روایت ) ایک ہی قبیل کے ہو گئے اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے اور دوسری نواور کی کتابوں میں بلکہ کبھی دونوں روایتیں اصول کی کتابوں میں ہوتی ہیں جو سب ایک ہی شخص کی تصنیفات ہیں۔ یعنی امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کی ۔ پس پہلی وجہ کیوں کر درست ہوسکتی ہے اور دوسری بہت تل مستبعد معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لیے بہتر یہ ہے کہ پچھلی دو وجہوں پر اکتفاء کی جائے ۔ مگر یہ بات ہر اس جزیہ میں نہیں ہے جس میں روایتیں مختلف ہوں کیوں کہ کبھی ان میں سے ایک روایت ایک مصنف کے یہاں ہوتی ہے اور دوسری دوسرے لے مصنف کے یہاں (پس اس صورت میں پہلی دو وجہیں بھی درست ہو سکتی ہیں ) نیز پچھلی دو وجہوں پر بھی اکتفا وہاں کیا جا سکتا ہے جب کہ مسئلہ میں قیاس و استحسان اور فتویٰ و تقویٰ کی
گنجائش ہو ۔ غرض جہاں راوی مختلف ہوں وہاں پہلی دو وجہیں بھی درست ہوسکتی ہیں ۔۔

ابن امیر حاج نے ، جوہ اربعہ نقل کر کے لکھا ہے کہ یہ بات مخفی نہیں ہے کہ بلیغی کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جہاں دورہ ایتیں ہوں گی ، ہاں وجود اربعہ میں سے کوئی ایک وجہ ضرور جاری ہوگی۔ ان کی یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ جہاں بھی دو قول ہوں گے وجود اربعہ میں سے ہر وجہ جاری ہو سکے گی۔ لہذا ہر جگہ ہر ایک وجہ جاری نہ ہو سکنے میں کوئی منها الله نسب والندانه اعم ( تقریر ج ۳۳ ۳۳۵)
این پاریب کرد ابن امیر خارج نے لکھی ہے جو گزشتہ حاشیہ میں نقل کی گئی ہے اور اصل اعتراض کا جواب یہ
ہے کہ ان ستوانه زدایت و سعا عام استعمال کیا ہے فرق کا لحاظ کر کے خاص معنی میں استعمال نہیں کیا ۔ ۱۲
Page 54: [How to Give a Fatwa? 53] Sharia of Rasm al-Mantiq. It is from 'f', and if the Imam [Abu Hanifa] stated a specific thing in a matter, but the narrators differed regarding what the Imam said, then this is a difference of narrations (riwayat). So the distinction that Allamah Ibn Amir Haj mentioned is very clear and obvious. But difficulty arises when one is used in place of the other, i.e., using a narration (riwaya) in place of a saying (qawl) and vice versa, because these terms are used loosely. All the subsequent confusion arises from this: the technical terms of 'aqwal' and 'riwayat' are not always used in their literal meanings. Four causes of difference in narrations: After mentioning the above distinction, Ibn Amir Haj quotes from Imam Abu Bakr al-Baliqi's 'al-Durar' that there can be several causes for the difference in narrations from the Great Imam [Abu Hanifa]. (1) Mistake in hearing. For example, when the Imam was asked about a matter, he replied in the negative, saying 'not permissible', but the narrator became confused, so he transmitted what he thought he heard. Another narrator heard correctly and transmitted correctly, thus two narrations arose. (2) The Imam had one opinion and later retracted it. A frequent companion of the Imam learned of the retraction and transmitted the final opinion, while another infrequent companion did not know of the retraction and transmitted the first opinion, resulting in two narrations. [Comment: This is for correction. The objection that Allamah Shami raises will be explained later. I did not find a mention of Imam Abu Bakr al-Baliqi; also, in al-Taqrir wa al-Tahrir, the name of Baliqi's book is 'al-Ghurr', not 'al-Durar'. It is thought that the correct name is Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr al-Ayni, known as Zayn al-Din, famous as Ibn al-Ayni, born 837 AH and died 893 AH. He wrote a commentary on Allamah Qunawi's 'Durar al-Bihar', about which Haji Khalifa wrote that he did well and excelled (Kashf al-Zunun vol. 1 p. 746). The above quotation is probably from this commentary, and Allah knows best.] Page 55: [How to Give a Fatwa? Start of Rasm al-Multaqa] (3) The Imam stated one thing based on qiyas and another based on istihsan. One narrator heard the first and narrated it, another heard the second and narrated it, resulting in differing statements. (4) In a matter, the ruling came from two aspects: one from the aspect of qada (judgment) and the other from the aspect of ihtiyat (taqwa/piety). Each narrator transmits the ruling as he heard it, thus differences arise. [Ibn Amir Haj's statement is concluded.] Objection on the distinction between Aqwal and Riwayat: I (Allamah Shami) say that except the first cause, the remaining three (in terms of existence) could be differences from the side of the one from whom it is transmitted (i.e., the Imam). Because the difference in them is based on the difference between two transmitted statements from the Imam. Thus 'aqwal' and 'riwayat' become of the same category. This is supported by the fact that sometimes both narrations are found in the books of the principles (usul), which are all authored by one person, i.e., Imam Muhammad. So how can the first cause be correct? The second also seems very improbable. Therefore, it is better to confine [the causes] to the last two. But this does not apply to every case where narrations differ, because sometimes one narration is with one author and the other with another author. (In such cases, the first two causes can also be valid.) Also, confinement to the last two causes can be done where the matter allows for qiyas and istihsan, or fatwa and taqwa. In short, where the narrators differ, the first two causes can also be valid. Ibn Amir Haj, after quoting the four causes, wrote: It is not hidden that Baliqi's intention is that wherever [a difference] occurs, it is necessary that one of the four causes applies. He did not mean that wherever there are two statements, each of the four causes can apply. Therefore, it is not necessary that every cause applies in every place. ... (Taqrir vol. 33 p. 335) ... The objection of Ibn Amir Haj mentioned in the previous footnote is answered as follows: [the terms] are used generally, not with specific meaning considering the distinction.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the methodological distinction between 'aqwal' (sayings/positions) and 'riwayat' (narrations) within the Hanafi madhhab. The author explains that a qawl is a specific statement attributed directly to Imam Abu Hanifa, while a riwaya is a transmitted version that may vary due to transmission issues. The crucial point is that these terms are often used loosely, leading to confusion. The author then presents four causes for difference in narrations, as quoted from Imam Abu Bakr al-Baliqi: (1) hearing error, (2) the Imam's retraction unknown to some narrators, (3) the Imam giving a ruling based on qiyas in one instance and istihsan in another, and (4) the Imam giving a ruling from the perspective of qada (judgment) versus taqwa (piety). Allamah Shami objects that the first two causes are problematic because the difference is actually from the Imam's side, thus making 'aqwal' and 'riwayat' similar. He suggests confining the causes to the last two. Ibn Amir Haj responds by clarifying that al-Baliqi meant that at least one cause applies, not that all four apply in every case. The passage underscores the importance of precise terminology in fatwa methodology and the need to consider the context of transmission when dealing with differing narrations.

Key Terms
قول (qawl): A specific statement or position directly attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa without transmission intermediaries.
رواية (riwaya): A transmitted narration of the Imam's statement, potentially subject to variation due to hearing error, retraction, or context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for the confusion between aqwal and riwayat?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa frequently changed his rulings.
B) The terms are used loosely, not always in their technical meanings.
C) The four causes are not accepted by later scholars.
D) Narrators intentionally altered the texts.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon position is that all four causes for difference in narrations are possible; the mufti must apply the appropriate cause based on context.

6 min
Causes 3 and 4 for Differences in Narrations: Qiyas vs. Istihsan and Qada vs. Taqwa
Lists and critiques causes of variation in narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two additional causes (qiyas/istihsan and qada/taqwa) that explain differences in narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa, and apply Allama Shami's critique to determine which causes are operative in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Narrations from Abu Hanifa differ because he ruled by both qiyas and istihsan, and by both qada and taqwa — the mufti must identify which aspect was reported.

This lesson explores two important reasons why multiple, sometimes contradictory, narrations are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. Understanding these causes is essential for a mufti to reconcile apparent conflicts in the Hanafi tradition. We will also examine Allama Shami's critique and the proper scope of these causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Causes
Read the passage and list the two causes: (3) the Imam spoke by qiyas on one occasion and by istihsan on another; (4) he gave a ruling from the perspective of qada (judicial decision) and from the perspective of taqwa (piety).
These are causes 3 and 4 among the four causes known in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand Allama Shami's Objection
Allama Shami argues that causes 1 and 2 (not quoted) are problematic because the difference between 'qawl' and 'riwaya' often arises within the same author (e.g., Imam Muhammad). He suggests that causes 3 and 4 are more plausible and sufficient.
The objection is that causes 1 and 2 assume different mujtahids, but often the narrations come from the same source (e.g., Imam Muhammad's books).
3
Recognize the Scope of Causes 3 and 4
Allama Shami qualifies: causes 3 and 4 are sufficient only when the issue allows for both qiyas/istihsan and fatwa/taqwa. If not, other causes may apply. Also, when narrators come from different authors, causes 1 and 2 may still apply.
The mufti must assess the specific issue and the chain of narrators to determine which cause(s) are relevant.
4
Apply the Principle to a Concrete Example
Given a set of conflicting narrations on a single issue, determine: Was the Imam likely considering both qiyas and istihsan? Or both qada and taqwa? Use the presence of these pairs as a clue.
For instance, a narration permitting a transaction by qiyas and another prohibiting it by istihsan would point to cause 3. A narration for fatwa and another for personal piety would point to cause 4.

(۳) امام صاحب نے ایک بات قیاس کی رو سے فرمائی اور دوسری استحسان کی رو سے ایک راوی نے پہلی بات سنی اور اس کو روایت کیا اور دوسرے نے دوسری بات سنی اور اس کو روایت کیا جس کی وجہ سے مختلف اقوال پیدا ہو گئے۔

(۴) کسی مسئلہ میں حکم دو جہتوں سے ہوا ایک قضا کی جہت سے اور دوسرا احتیاط (تقوئی) کی جہت سے اور ہر راوی اسی طرح حکم نقل کرتا ہے جس طرح اس نے سنا ہے (پس اقوال میں اختلاف پیدا ہو جاتا ہے) (ابن امیر حاج کی بات پوری ہوئی)

اقوال و روایات میں فرق پر اعتراض: میں (علامہ شامی) کہتا ہوں کہ وجہ اول کو چھوڑ کر باقی وجود میں دو روایتوں میں اختلاف منقول عنہ کی طرف سے بھی ہو گا۔ کیونکہ ان میں اختلاف امام سے مروی دوقولوں میں اختلاف کی بنیاد پر سے لیس دانوں (یعنی قول اور روایت) ایک ہی قبیل کے ہو گئے اور اس کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے اور دوسری نواور کی کتابوں میں بلکہ کبھی دونوں روایتیں اصول کی کتابوں میں ہوتی ہیں جو سب ایک ہی شخص کی تصنیفات ہیں۔ یعنی امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کی ۔ پس پہلی وجہ کیوں کر درست ہوسکتی ہے اور دوسری بہت تل مستبعد معلوم ہوتی ہے۔ اس لیے بہتر یہ ہے کہ پچھلی دو وجہوں پر اکتفاء کی جائے ۔ مگر یہ بات ہر اس جزیہ میں نہیں ہے جس میں روایتیں مختلف ہوں کیوں کہ کبھی ان میں سے ایک روایت ایک مصنف کے یہاں ہوتی ہے اور دوسری دوسرے لے مصنف کے یہاں (پس اس صورت میں پہلی دو وجہیں بھی درست ہو سکتی ہیں) نیز پچھلی دو وجہوں پر بھی اکتفا وہاں کیا جا سکتا ہے جب کہ مسئلہ میں قیاس و استحسان اور فتویٰ و تقویٰ کی گنجائش ہو ۔ غرض جہاں راوی مختلف ہوں وہاں پہلی دو وجہیں بھی درست ہوسکتی ہیں ۔۔

ابن امیر حاج نے، جوہ اربعہ نقل کر کے لکھا ہے کہ یہ بات مخفی نہیں ہے کہ بلیغی کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جہاں دورہ ایتیں ہوں گی، ہاں وجود اربعہ میں سے کوئی ایک وجہ ضرور جاری ہوگی۔ ان کی یہ مراد نہیں ہے کہ جہاں بھی دو قول ہوں گے وجود اربعہ میں سے ہر وجہ جاری ہو سکے گی۔ لہذا ہر جگہ ہر ایک وجہ جاری نہ ہو سکنے میں کوئی منها الله نسب والندانه اعم (تقریر ج ۳۳ ۳۳۵)

این پاریب کرد ابن امیر خارج نے لکھی ہے جو گزشتہ حاشیہ میں نقل کی گئی ہے اور اصل اعتراض کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان ستوانه زدایت و سعا عام استعمال کیا ہے فرق کا لحاظ کر کے خاص معنی میں استعمال نہیں کیا ۔ ۱۲
Start of Rasm al-Mulhaq [commentary]. (3) Imam [Abu Hanifa] stated one thing by way of qiyas and another by way of istihsan. One narrator heard the first statement and narrated it, and another heard the second and narrated it, leading to different sayings. (4) In some issue, the ruling came from two aspects: one from the aspect of qada (judgment) and another from the aspect of ihtiyat (taqwa). Each narrator reported the ruling as he heard it, thus differences in sayings arise. (The statement of Ibn Amir Haj is complete.)

Objection on the difference between sayings and narrations: I (Allama Shami) say that leaving aside the first cause (cause 1 and 2), in the remaining two, the difference in narrations can also be from the one from whom it is transmitted (mujtahid). Because the difference in the two sayings reported from the Imam is based on the difference between a saying (qawl) and a narration (riwaya), so they are of the same category. This is supported by the fact that both narrations sometimes appear in the books of principles authored by the same person, i.e., Imam Muhammad. So how can the first cause be correct? And the second appears very improbable. Therefore, it is better to suffice with the last two causes. But this does not apply to every instance where narrations differ, because sometimes one narration is found in one author and the other in another author (so in that case the first two causes can also be valid). Also, one can suffice with the last two causes only when there is room in the issue for qiyas/istihsan and fatwa/taqwa. In short, where the narrators are different, the first two causes can also be valid.

Ibn Amir Haj, after quoting the four causes, wrote that it is not hidden that the intent of al-Bulighi is that wherever two narrations occur, one of the four causes will necessarily apply. It is not his intent that wherever two sayings occur, every one of the four causes can apply. Hence, in every place, not every cause can apply. (Taqrir vol. 3 p. 335)

This objection that Ibn Amir Haj wrote, which was quoted in the previous footnote, and the answer to the original objection is that he (Ibn Amir Haj) used 'umum' (general) without considering distinction; he did not use it in a specific sense.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Rasm al-Mulhaq (a commentary on Rasm al-Mufti by Ibn Amir Haj) discusses two additional causes (causes 3 and 4) for why different narrations are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. Cause 3: The Imam sometimes gave a ruling based on qiyas (analogy) and another based on istihsan (juristic preference). Different narrators heard each and transmitted them, resulting in multiple sayings. Cause 4: In a single issue, the ruling may have two aspects: one for judicial decision (qada) and another for personal piety (taqwa). Narrators report what they heard, again creating variation. Allama Shami then raises an objection: he argues that causes 1 and 2 (not quoted here) are problematic because the difference between a 'qawl' (statement) and 'riwaya' (narration) is often within the same school, not from different mujtahids. He suggests that causes 3 and 4 are more plausible. However, he concedes that when narrations come from different authors, causes 1 and 2 may apply. Ibn Amir Haj clarifies that the intent of the original author (al-Bulighi) is that in every instance of two narrations, at least one cause will be operative, not that all four apply universally. The discussion is foundational for a mufti to understand why conflicting rulings appear in the Hanafi school and how to reconcile them.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning to derive a ruling for a new case based on an existing ruling in the primary sources.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference – departing from qiyas for a stronger evidence or need.
قضا (qada): Judicial decision based on apparent evidence (zahir al-riwaya).
تقوی (taqwa): Piety – a stricter ruling for personal precaution, not necessarily for fatwa.
قول (qawl): A statement or opinion of a mujtahid.
روایت (riwaya): A narration or transmitted report of a mujtahid's statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two causes does Allama Shami say are sufficient to explain differences in narrations, but only when the issue allows for certain distinctions?
A) Causes 1 and 2, when narrators are different.
B) Causes 3 and 4, when the issue allows for qiyas/istihsan and fatwa/taqwa.
C) Causes 1 and 3, when the ruling is based on qada.
D) Causes 2 and 4, when the narrations are from the same author.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must understand that narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa may differ because he ruled both by qiyas and istihsan, and by qada and taqwa; the key is to identify which aspect was reported and apply the appropriate cause.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Two Additional Causes for Differences in Narrations
Explains causes for differences in narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two additional causes for differences in narrations and apply the distinction between qawl and riwaya when evaluating Hanafi positions.

Core Idea
Multiple narrations arise from a mujtahid's hesitation or from multiple interpretations of one evidence.

This passage from Sharh Taym Nafti expands on why multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa exist. Understanding these causes helps a mufti navigate conflicting opinions and determine which is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The key is the distinction between qawl (preponderant opinion) and riwaya (transmitted but non-preponderant narration).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Cause: Ta'arud (Conflict of Evidences)
Note the first cause: the mujtahid is hesitant because the evidences conflict and no tarjih (preference) is possible. This leads to multiple narrations reflecting the uncertainty.
2
Identify the Cause: Multiple Interpretations of One Evidence
The second cause: a single evidence (e.g., a verse) can have two or more meanings. The mujtahid may adopt one meaning as preponderant (qawl) while the other remains as a riwaya. If no meaning is preponderant, both are equally valid.
3
Distinguish Qawl from Riwaya
Qawl is the preponderant opinion used for fatwa. Riwaya is a non-preponderant opinion that is still attributed to the Imam. If tarjih is achieved, jurists say: 'Imam's qawl is this, and a riwaya is that.' If no tarjih, they say: 'there are two narrations/sayings from the Imam.'
4
Apply to Fatwa Practice
When a mufti encounters multiple narrations, first check if one is designated as qawl (mufta bihi). If both are riwaya, determine if tarjih is possible; if not, both are valid but the mufti may choose the stronger or follow the dominant practice.
This is a key practical step in the mufti's methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختلاف روایت کے دو اور سبب:

شرح تیم نفتی

اور یہ بھی کہا جاتا ہے کہ اختلاف روایت کی وجوہ میں درج ذیل صورتیں بھی ہیں:

(1) کسی حکم میں مجتہد کا متردد ہونا بائیں وجہ کہ اس کے نزدیک دلائل میں تعارض ہے اور کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہیں ہے۔

(۲) ایک ہی دلیل کے مدلول و مفہوم میں مجتہد کی رائے کا مختلف ہونا کیوں کہ دلیل کبھی دو یا زیادہ وجوہ کومشتمل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لیے مجتہد ہر احتمال پر ایک جواب کی بنیاد رکھتا ہے۔ راجح قول ہے اور مرجوح روایت پھر کبھی مجتہد کے نزدیک ایک احتمال کو ترجیح حاصل ہو جاتی ہے تو وہ احتمال اس کی طرف منسوب کر دیا جاتا ہے ( اور دوسرا مرجوح احتمال روایت کی صورت میں باقی رہ جاتا ہے) فقباء ایسی صورت میں یہ تعبیر اختیار کرتے ہیں کہ : " امام صاحب کا قول ( مذہب ) یہ ہے اور ان سے ایک روایت یہ ہے ۔ اور کبھی کسی وجہ کو ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہوتی تو دونوں جانب امام کی رائے مساوی رہتی ہے ۔ آپ فقہاء کو دیکھیں گے کہ وہ ایک ہی مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو قول اس طرح نقل کرتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں قولوں کا امام صاحب کے نزد یک مساوی ہونا مفہوم ہوتا ہے مثلا کہتے ہیں کہ : " اس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں یا دو قول ہیں ۔"
Two Additional Causes of Difference in Narrations:

Sharh Taym Nafti

It is also said that among the causes of difference in narrations are the following forms:

(1) The mujtahid being hesitant in a ruling, because in his view there is conflict (ta'arud) of evidences and no reason for preference (tarjih) exists.

(2) The mujtahid's opinion differs regarding the purport and meaning of a single evidence, because an evidence sometimes comprises two or more aspects. Hence, the mujtahid bases one answer on each probability. The preponderant view is called 'qawl' and the non-preponderant is called 'riwaya'. Sometimes, the mujtahid gives preference to one probability, so that probability is attributed to him, and the other non-preponderant probability remains as a narration. In such a case, the jurists use the expression: "The Imam's saying (madhhab) is this, and from him there is a narration that is that." And sometimes, no probability is given preference, so both sides are equal in the Imam's view. You will see the jurists quoting two sayings from the Imam in one issue such that it is understood that both sayings are equal in his view. For example, they say: "In this issue, there are two narrations or two sayings from the Imam."
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Taym Nafti adds two more causes for why multiple narrations exist from Imam Abu Hanifa. Cause 1: The mujtahid is uncertain because the evidences conflict and no tarjih is possible. Cause 2: A single evidence (like a verse or hadith) can be interpreted in multiple ways. The mujtahid may initially consider all possibilities, but eventually one becomes preponderant (rajih) – that is his 'qawl' (stated opinion). The non-preponderant is retained as a 'riwaya' (narration). If no preponderance is achieved, both are equally valid and both can be attributed to the Imam. This explains why Hanafi fiqh texts often say 'there are two narrations from the Imam' – meaning both are transmitted, but neither is given explicit preference. A mufti needs to know these distinctions to determine which saying to rely on for fatwa. The 'rawaya' in such cases is not a mere story but a valid opinion attributed to the Imam, though it may be weaker.

Key Terms
قول (qawl): A preponderant opinion (rajih) of a mujtahid, used for fatwa.
روایت (riwaya): A transmitted opinion that is not preponderant (marjuh) or when no tarjih exists.
ترجیح (tarjih): The process of preferring one evidence or opinion over another based on strength.
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent conflict between two evidences that cannot be reconciled except through preference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second cause mentioned in this passage, what is the difference between 'qawl' and 'riwaya' when a single evidence has multiple possible interpretations?
A) Qawl is the opinion of the narrator, riwaya is the opinion of the mujtahid.
B) Qawl is the preponderant opinion, riwaya is the non-preponderant one retained as a narration.
C) Qawl is used in judicial rulings, riwaya is for personal piety.
D) Qawl is transmitted from Imam Muhammad, riwaya from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
Multiple narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa arise from his hesitation in cases of ta'arud or from multiple interpretations of one evidence; the preponderant opinion is the qawl, while the non-preponderant is a riwaya, and if no tarjih, both are equally valid.

Two Additional Causes of Ikhtilaf al-Riwayah
Explaining two more reasons for variance in transmitted rulings from a mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two additional causes of ikhtilaf al-riwayah and explain the Hanafi position on attributing two sayings to a mujtahid when evidences conflict.

Core Idea
A mujtahid may have two attributed sayings when evidences are equal; tarjih resolves, not creates, the multiplicity.

In this lesson, we explore two further reasons why multiple rulings can be transmitted from one mujtahid imam: genuine indecision due to conflicting evidences with no means to prefer, and the existence of multiple plausible meanings in a single evidence. Understanding these helps a mufti navigate the hierarchy of transmitted positions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first cause
Recognize that a mujtahid may be undecided when evidences (adillah) appear to conflict and no reason for preference (tarjih) exists. This leads to both possible rulings being attributed to him.
This is distinct from deliberate choice; it is genuine uncertainty.
2
Identify the second cause
Understand that a single evidence can have multiple plausible meanings (ihtimalat). The mujtahid may base different rulings on each probability. When one becomes preponderant (raajih), it becomes his established saying (qawl); the other remains as a narration (riwayah).
If both probabilities remain equally strong, both are considered sayings.
3
Understand attribution of sayings vs narrations
Grasp the terminology: when a mujtahid cannot prefer one aspect, both are attributed as sayings. When he can prefer, the preponderant is his saying and the outweighed is a narration. The Hanafi fuqaha use expressions like 'Imam’s saying is X and from him a narration is Y.'
4
Analyse the effect of ruju' (retraction)
If the mujtahid later retracts one view entirely, that view ceases to be his saying. But partial retraction or ex lege retraction? Actually, if he merely prefers one without explicit retraction, both are still attributed: one as saying, the other as narration. Complete abandonment cancels it.
Retraction does not necessarily end ikhtilaf in the school; later scholars may still transmit both.
5
Address the apparent contradiction with usul principles
Some usulis object that a mujtahid cannot have two sayings. The Hanafi response distinguishes between a systematic method (Quran→hadith→qawl sahabi→qiyas) and the state of indecision. The method guarantees a single outcome only when preference is possible. Without it, both possibilities are valid.
This shows the practical nuance of rasm al-mufti: a mufti must know when two sayings are equally authoritative.

آپ فتوی کیسے دیں؟

اختلاف روایت کے دو اور سبب:

شرح رسم المفتي

اور یہ بھی کہا جاتا ہے کہ اختلاف روایت کی وجوہ میں درج ذیل صورتیں بھی ہیں۔ (1) کسی حکم میں مجتہد کا متردد ہونا بایں وجہ کہ اس کے نزدیک دلائل میں تعارض ہے اور کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہیں ہے۔ (2) ایک ہی دلیل کے مدلول و مفہوم میں مجتہد کی رائے کا مختلف ہونا کیوں کہ دلیل کبھی دو یا زیادہ وجوہ کو مشتمل ہوتی ہے۔ اس لیے مجتہد ہر احتمال پر ایک جواب کی بنیاد رکھتا ہے۔ راجح قول ہے اور مرجوح روایت پھر کبھی مجتہد کے نزدیک ایک احتمال کو ترجیح حاصل ہو جاتی ہے تو وہ احتمال اس کی طرف منسوب کر دیا جاتا ہے ( اور دوسرا مرجوح احتمال روایت کی صورت میں باقی رہ جاتا ہے) فقہاء ایسی صورت میں یہ تعبیر اختیار کرتے ہیں کہ : " امام صاحب کا قول ( مذہب ) یہ ہے اور ان سے ایک روایت یہ ہے ۔ اور کبھی کسی وجہ کو ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہوتی تو دونوں جانب امام کی رائے مساوی رہتی ہے ۔ آپ فقہاء کو دیکھیں گے کہ وہ ایک ہی مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو قول اس طرح نقل کرتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں قولوں کا امام صاحب کے نزد یک مساوی ہونا مفہوم ہوتا ہے مثلا کہتے ہیں کہ : " اس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں یا دو قول ہیں ۔"

عدم ترجیح کی صورت میں دونوں ہی قول ہیں:

اور ہم پہلے امام قرانی رحمہ اللہ (۹) کے حوالہ سے بیان کر آئے ہیں کہ غیر راجح قول پر فیصلہ کرنا یا فتوی دینا نہ مجتہد کے لیے جائز ہے نہ مقلد کے لیے ۔ البتہ اگر مجتہد کی نظر میں دلائل متعارض ہوں اور وہ کسی دلیل کو ترجیح نہ دے سکے تو جائز ہے کہ دونوں قولوں میں سے جس پر چاہے فیصلہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں دونوں قول اس کے نزدیک مساوی ہیں ۔ وعلی ہذا ( یعنی جب دونوں قولوں اور فیصلہ کرنا درست ہے تو ) وہ دونوں قول اس مجتہد کی طرف منسوب کئے جا سکتے ہیں۔ اور بعض اصولیوں کا یہ خیال درست نہیں ہے کہ ایسی صورت میں کوئی بھی قول اس مجتہد کی طرف منسوب نہ کیا جائے ۔ نیز بعض حضرات کا یہ خیال بھی درست نہیں ہے کہ صرف ایک قول کی مجتہد کی طرف نسبت ہو سکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ دوسرے قول سے امام کا رجوع متعین نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ مفروضہ صورت یہ ہے کہ مجتہد کی رائے میں دونوں پہلو برابر میں کسی ایک پہلو کو دوسرے پہلو پر ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہے۔ رجوع کے بعد قول باقی نہیں رہتا :

ہاں اگر مجتہد کے نزدیک ایک پہلو راجح ہو جائے دوسرے پہلو سے رجوع اور اعراض کئے بغیر تو راجح پہلو اس کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا اور دوسرے پہلو کو روایت کے طور پر ذکر کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر مجتہد دوسرے پہلو سے بالکلیہ اعراض کر لے تو وہ اس کا قول ہی باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ اس صورت میں اس کا قول صرف راجح پہلو ہوگا۔ رجوع سے اختلاف ختم نہیں ہوتا: لیکن مجتہد کے رجوع کرنے سے مسئلہ میں اختلاف ختم نہیں ہوتا بعض شوافع نے ایسا ہی بیان کیا ہے اور بعض نے اس کی تائید میں یہ بات پیش کی ہے کہ اگر کسی دور میں لوگ کسی مسئلہ میں اختلاف کرنے کے بعد کسی ایک بات پر متفق ہو جائیں تو سابق اختلاف کے ختم ہونے کے بارے میں اصولیوں نے دو قول نقل کئے ہیں پس جس مسئلہ میں اجماع نہ ہوا ہو اس میں تو بدرجہ

کیا تعارض ادلہ اختلاف اقوال کا سبب ہو سکتا ہے؟

لیکن ہماری اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں جو بات مذکور ہے کہ "مجتہد کے کسی مسئلہ میں دو قول ہ ہوں یہ بات ممکن ہی نہیں نہ جینا کہ تحریر کے حوالہ سے یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے یہ بات اس کے منافی ہے کہ تعارض ادلہ کو اختلاف اقوال کا سبب بنایا جائے ۔ کیونکہ وہ بات بظاہر اس بات پر مبنی ہے جو علماء نے تعارض ادلہ کی بحث میں ذکر کی ہے کہ جب دو آیتوں میں تعارض ہو تو حدیث کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اور دو حدیثوں میں تعارض ہو تو اقوال صحابہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اور صحابہ کے فتاوی میں تعارض ہو تو قیاس کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اور دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہو اور کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہ ہو تو تحری ( غور و فکر ) سے کام لیا جائے اور دل کی گواہی کے مطابق عمل کیا جائے۔ پھر جب ایک پہلو پر عمل کر لیا تو دوسرے پہلو پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش باقی نہیں رہی البتہ اگر تحری سے بڑھ کر کوئی دلیل سامنے آجائے تو دوسرے پہلو پر عمل کیا جا سکتا ہے (غرض جہاں ادلہ میں تعارض ہو گا وہاں مخلص بھی موجود ہو گا پھر تعارض ادلہ اختلاف اقوال کا سبب کیسے
How do you give a fatwa?

Two more causes of difference in narration:

Sharh Rasm al-Mufti

And it is also said that among the causes of difference in narration are the following situations: (1) The mujtahid being undecided in a ruling because there is a conflict of evidences in his view and no reason for preference exists. (2) The mujtahid's opinion differing in the purport and meaning of a single evidence, because the evidence sometimes comprises two or more aspects. Therefore the mujtahid bases a response on each probability. The preponderant opinion becomes his [established] saying and the outweighed becomes a narration. Then sometimes a probability becomes preponderant in the mujtahid's view, so that probability is attributed to him (and the other outweighed probability remains in the form of a narration). The jurists in such a case use the expression: 'The Imam's saying (madhhab) is such and from him there is a narration such.' And sometimes no aspect gains preference, so the Imam's opinion remains equal on both sides. You will see the jurists transmit two sayings from the Imam in one issue such that the meaning is that both sayings are equal in the Imam's view. For example, they say: 'In this issue there are two narrations or two sayings from the Imam.'

In case of no preference, both are sayings:

And we have previously mentioned with reference to Imam Qurani (may Allah have mercy on him) that it is not permissible for the mujtahid nor for the muqallid to judge or give a fatwa based on the non-preponderant saying. However, if in the mujtahid's view the evidences are conflicting and he cannot prefer one evidence over another, then it is permissible for him to judge by whichever of the two sayings he wishes, because in this case both sayings are equal in his view. And accordingly (i.e., when it is correct to judge by both sayings), both sayings can be attributed to that mujtahid. And the view of some usulis that in such a case no saying should be attributed to that mujtahid is not correct. Also the view of some people that only one saying can be attributed to the mujtahid is not correct, because the Imam's retraction from the other saying is not established. This is because the assumed situation is that in the mujtahid's opinion both aspects are equal, and no one aspect has preference over the other. After retraction, the saying does not remain:

Yes, if in the mujtahid's view one aspect becomes preponderant without retraction and turning away from the other aspect, then the preponderant aspect will be attributed to him and the other aspect will be mentioned as a narration. And if the mujtahid completely turns away from the other aspect, then that saying of his will not remain at all. In that case, his saying is only the preponderant aspect. Retraction does not end the difference: But the difference in the issue does not end by the mujtahid's retraction. Some Shafi'is have stated similarly, and some have presented in support of this that if people in a certain era agree on one thing after differing on an issue, the usulis have transmitted two sayings regarding the end of the previous difference. So in an issue where there is no consensus, then as per the [text incomplete]

Can conflict of evidences be a cause for difference in sayings?

But what is mentioned in our books of usul al-fiqh that 'it is not possible for a mujtahid to have two sayings in one issue' — as has passed earlier with reference to Tahreer — this contradicts making conflict of evidences a cause for difference in sayings. Because that statement apparently is based on what the scholars have mentioned in the discussion of conflict of evidences: when two verses conflict, one turns to hadith; when two hadiths conflict, one turns to the sayings of the Companions; when the fatwas of the Companions conflict, one turns to qiyas; when two qiyas conflict and there is no reason for preference, one resorts to tahari (contemplation) and acts according to the testimony of the heart. Then when one aspect is acted upon, there remains no scope for acting on the other aspect. However, if a stronger evidence appears beyond tahari, the other aspect can be acted upon. (In short, wherever there is conflict of evidences, there will also be a way out. Then how can conflict of evidences be a cause for difference in sayings?)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage from 'Aap Fatwa Kaisay Den' is a rasm al-mufti discussion explaining two additional causes for ikhtilaf al-riwayah (difference in transmitted rulings) within the Hanafi school. The author, building on earlier mentions, presents these causes as part of understanding how multiple rulings from a single imam (like Imam Abu Hanifa) can be reported. The first cause is the mujtahid's own indecision when faced with conflicting evidences (i.e., dalils that apparently oppose each other) and no means of preference (tarjih) is available. In such a state, the mujtahid may be genuinely uncertain, and both possible rulings become potential positions attributed to him. The second cause is that a single evidence can have multiple plausible meanings (wujuh or ihtimalat). The mujtahid may formulate a ruling based on each probability, and if one becomes preponderant, that becomes his 'qawl' (established saying) while the other remains as a 'riwayah' (transmitted narration). The text clarifies that when both aspects are equally strong (no tarjih), both are considered sayings of the imam. This is a nuanced point of Hanafi usul: it is permissible for a mujtahid to have two sayings if he is truly unable to prefer one. The text then addresses objections: some usulis wrongly deny attribution of both sayings. It also discusses the effect of ruju' (retraction): if the imam later prefers one view without explicitly retracting the other, both positions are still attributed—one as the preponderant saying, the other as a narration. Only if he definitively abandons the other does it cease to be his saying. The passage further notes that a mujtahid's retraction does not end the ikhtilaf (disagreement) in the school; later scholars may still transmit both opinions. The author then raises a potential contradiction with the general usul principle that a mujtahid cannot have two sayings in one issue, pointing to the established method of dealing with conflicting evidences through resorting to hadith, then Companion sayings, then qiyas, etc. The resolution hinted is that when tarjih is possible, there is no two sayings; but when tarjih is not possible, the mujtahid can have two sayings. This is a key distinction for the mufti who needs to understand the hierarchy of transmitted rulings.

Key Terms
اختلاف الرواية (ikhtilāf al-riwāyah): Difference in transmitted narrations from a mujtahid imam, resulting from various causes such as indecision or multiple interpretations.
تعارض الأدلة (taʿāruḍ al-adillah): Apparent conflict between two or more legal evidences (Quran, hadith, qiyas, etc.) such that they seem to point to different rulings.
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preference given to one evidence or one aspect over another based on established criteria (e.g., authenticity, strength of indication).
راجح / مرجوح (rājiḥ / marjūḥ): Preponderant and outweighed; the rājiḥ becomes the established saying, the marjūḥ is recorded as a narration.
رجوع (rujūʿ): Retraction or withdrawal from a previous opinion by the mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can a mujtahid legitimately have two sayings attributed to him in one issue?
A) When he deliberately changes his mind
B) When he is unable to prefer one evidence over another due to equal strength
C) Always, as a matter of principle
D) Never; it is impossible in Islamic law

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilaf al-riwayah can arise from a mujtahid's indecision when evidences are equally strong or from multiple aspects of a single evidence, allowing both sayings to be attributed to him.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Effect of a Mujtahid's Ru'ooj on Ikhtilaf al-Aqwal
Analyzing whether a mujtahid's return negates his earlier opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a mujtahid's return (ru'ooj) and distinguish between explicit abandonment and mere preference in attributing statements to a mujtahid.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's later opinion does not automatically erase his earlier one—without explicit ru'ooj, the earlier remains a narration.

When a senior Hanafi jurist appears to have two different statements on the same issue, how should a mufti handle them? Does the later one simply cancel the earlier? This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti clarifies that the answer depends on whether the mujtahid explicitly returned (ru'ooj) from the earlier view or merely preferred the later one without abandonment. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly attributing statements to Hanafi imams and issuing reliable fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Define Ru'ooj
Identify the term 'ru'ooj' (رجوع) as a mujtahid's formal withdrawal from a previous legal opinion. Distinguish it from mere preference (tarijih) where one aspect is favored but not explicitly abandoned.
Hanafi rasm al-mufti treats explicit ru'ooj as conclusive; without it, the earlier opinion remains as a riwaya.
2
Classify the Two Scenarios
Recognize two scenarios: (1) the mujtahid explicitly abandons one aspect, in which case that statement no longer exists; (2) one aspect becomes prevalent but without explicit abandonment, in which case the other aspect is preserved as a narration.
This directly answers the common question: 'How can Imam Abu Hanifa have two statements on one issue?'
3
Analyze the Hanafi-Stafi'i Dispute
Compare the Hanafi position (impossible for a mujtahid to have two valid statements; later abrogates earlier) with the Shafi'i position (a mujtahid may have multiple valid statements due to ta'arud al-adillah). Understand the root cause: Hanafis resolve ta'arud through a strict hierarchy (Quran→Hadith→Companions→Qiyas→Taharri), Shafi'is allow flexibility.
The Hanafi view is that after taharri, only one aspect remains operative; the other cannot be simultaneously valid.
4
Apply the Rule to Mufti Practice
Given two conflicting narrations from a Hanafi imam, first check if a later explicit ru'ooj is recorded. If not, treat both as narrations but recognize that only the prevalent (rajih) one is attributed to the imam for fatwa. The other remains as a riwaya but is not mufta bihi unless explicitly relied upon.
This practical step prevents the mufti from mistakenly citing an abandoned opinion as authoritative.

میں تعارض ہو تو حدیث کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اور دو حدیثوں میں تعارض ہو تو اقوال صحابہ کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اور صحابہ کے فتاوی میں تعارض ہو تو قیاس کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے اور دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہو اور کوئی وجہ ترجیح موجود نہ ہو تو تحری ( غور و فکر ) سے کام لیا جائے اور دل کی گواہی کے مطابق عمل کیا جائے۔ پھر جب ایک پہلو پر عمل کر لیا تو دوسرے پہلو پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش باقی نہیں رہی البتہ اگر تحری سے بڑھ کر کوئی دلیل سامنے آجائے تو دوسرے پہلو پر عمل کیا جا سکتا ہے (غرض جہاں ادلہ میں تعارض ہو گا وہاں مخلص بھی موجود ہو گا پھر تعارض اولہ اختلاف اقوال کا سبب کیسے بن سکتا ہے؟) اور علمائے کرام نے یہ بھی بیان کیا ہے کہ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کا ارشاد یہ ہے کہ: "مجتہد تحری کے بغیر بھی دو پہلوؤں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کر سکتا ہے۔ چنانچہ امام شافعی کے ہر مسئلہ میں دو یا زیادہ اقوال ہیں اور ہمارے ائمہ سے جو ایک مسئلہ میں دو روایتیں ہیں تو وہ دو وقتوں کی ہیں اس لیے ایک صحیح ہے اور دوسری صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ مگر ان میں سے بعد کی روایت معلوم نہیں ہے ( یعنی تعارض ادلہ شوافع کے نزدیک تو اختلاف اقوال کا سبب بن سکتا ہے مگر احناف کی تصریحات کے مطابق اس کی گنجائش نہیں ) ( التقریر والتحبير ج ۳ ص ۵ بحث تعارض ) بناء علی ہذا یہ جو کہا جاتا ہے کہ : " اس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں ہیں یہ بات : آخری قول معلوم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کہی جاتی ہے اور جہاں یہ تعبیر آتی ہے کہ فی روایۃ عنہ کذا یعنی امام صاحب سے ایک روایت اس طرح ہے۔ یہ تعبیر وہاں اختیار کی جاتی ہے جہاں فقہاء کو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ بات امام صاحب کا پہلا قول ہے یا بایں وجہ یہ تعبیر اختیار کی جاتی ہے کہ امام صاحب کا وہ قول اصول کی کتابوں کے علاوہ دوسری کتابوں میں مذکور ہوتا ہے اور یہ دوسری بات اقرب الی الصواب ہے۔ لیکن یہ بات مخفی نہیں ہے کہ علماء نے تعارض ادلہ کی بحث میں جو بات بیان فرمائی ہے وہ نا قابل فہم ہے کیوں کہ اس سے یہ لازم آتا ہے کہ جس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب کی دو روایتیں ہوں اس میں کسی پر بھی عمل جائز نہ ہو۔ یہ بات معلوم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کہ ان میں سے کون سی روایت صحیح ہے اور کون سی باطل اور نہ ان دو باتوں میں سے کسی کی امام صاحب کی طرف نسبت درست ہو ۔ جیسا کہ بعض اصولیوں کے حوالہ سے یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے حالانکہ بے شمار مسائل میں دو روایتیں موجود ہیں ۔ اور علما ء ایک کو دوسری پر ترجیح دیتے ہیں ۔ اور اس رائج کو امام صاحب کی طرف منسوب بھی کرتے ہیں ۔ میں ظاہر وہی ہے جو امام بلیغی کے حوالہ سے پہلے گزر چکا کہ اختلاف روایات کی وجوہ متعدد قرار دی جائیں، صرف تعارض اولہ کو سبب نہ بنایا جائے۔ البتہ ان کی بیان کردہ وجوہ اربعہ کے ساتھ
It is because the assumed case is that in the mujtahid's view both aspects are equal, with no preference of one aspect over the other. After return, the statement does not remain. Yes, if one aspect becomes prevalent in the mujtahid's view without returning from and abandoning the other aspect, then the prevalent aspect will be attributed to him, and the other aspect will be mentioned as a narration. And if the mujtahid completely abandons the other aspect, then that statement of his will not remain at all. In that case, his statement is only the prevalent aspect. The disagreement does not end by return: but the disagreement in the issue does not end by the mujtahid's return. Some Shafi'is have stated this, and some have supported it with the statement that if people in an era after disagreeing on an issue agree on one thing, the usuliyyun have narrated two statements regarding the ending of the previous disagreement. So in an issue where no consensus occurred, then to what extent can contradiction of evidences be a cause for difference of statements? But in our books of usul al-fiqh it is mentioned that 'it is not possible for a mujtahid to have two statements in one issue, as this has already passed with reference to writing.' This contradicts making contradiction of evidences a cause for difference of statements. Because that statement is apparently based on what scholars mentioned in the discussion of first contradiction: that when there is contradiction between two verses, hadith is referred to; when contradiction between two hadiths, the statements of the Companions are referred to; when contradiction among the fatwas of the Companions, analogy is referred to; when contradiction between two analogies and no cause of preference exists, then taharri (deliberation) is used and action is taken according to the testimony of the heart. Then when one aspect is acted upon, there remains no scope for acting on the other aspect. However, if a stronger evidence appears beyond taharri, the other aspect may be acted upon. (In short, where there is contradiction among evidences, there will also be a way out; then how can first contradiction cause difference of statements?) And the noble scholars have also stated that Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'A mujtahid can act on whichever of the two aspects he wishes without taharri.' Thus, Imam Shafi'i has two or more statements in every issue, and the two narrations from our Imams in a single issue are from two times, so one is correct and the other is not correct. But the later narration among them is not known. (i.e., contradiction of evidences can cause difference of statements according to the Shafi'is, but according to the clear statements of the Hanafis, there is no scope for it.) (Al-Taqrir wa al-Tahbir, vol. 3, p. 5, discussion of ta'arud) Based on this, what is said that 'Imam Sahib has two narrations in this issue' is said because the final statement is not known, and where the expression 'fi riwayatin 'anhu kaza' (i.e., a narration from him is such) is used, this expression is adopted where the jurists know that that statement is the Imam's first statement, or for this reason the expression is adopted that the Imam's statement is mentioned in other books besides the books of usul. And this second matter is closer to what is correct. Allama Shami's opinion: But it is not hidden that what the scholars have stated in the discussion of contradiction of evidences is incomprehensible, because it necessarily follows that in an issue where Imam Sahib has two narrations, action on neither is permissible, due to not knowing which one is correct and which is false, and neither of the two statements can be correctly attributed to Imam Sahib. As has passed earlier with reference to some usuliyyun, while there are countless issues with two narrations, and the scholars prefer one over the other and attribute the prevalent one to Imam Sahib. The apparent opinion is what has passed earlier with reference to Imam Balighi: that multiple causes for difference of narrations should be established, not only first contradiction as the cause. However, along with the four causes he mentioned...
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical rasm rule regarding the nature of a mujtahid's statements (aqwal) and how contradictions in evidence (ta'arud al-adillah) relate to differences in rulings. The author begins by stating that if a mujtahid views two aspects as equally balanced without preference, and then he returns (ru'ooj) from one, the earlier statement does not remain—it is as if he never held it. However, if one aspect becomes prevalent without explicit return or abandonment, the other aspect is preserved as a narration (riwaya), preserving ikhtilaf. The text then explores the question: Can ta'arud al-adillah be a cause for ikhtilaf al-aqwal? The author notes that Hanafi usul works assert it is impossible for a mujtahid to have two valid statements on a single issue simultaneously; if two narrations appear, one must be later and correct. This contrasts with the Shafi'i view where an Imam may have multiple valid statements. The author critiques the Shafi'i position by arguing that ta'arud al-adillah does not lead to multiple statements because the proper procedure when evidences conflict is to apply hierarchy (Quran→Hadith→Companions→Qiyas→Taharri). After choosing one aspect, the other becomes inoperative unless a stronger evidence emerges. Thus, there cannot be permanent multiplicity. The passage concludes by citing Allama Shami's preference for the view of Imam Balighi: differences in narrations should be attributed to multiple causes (such as abrogation, different contexts, etc.) rather than merely to ta'arud. This is a sharp reminder for the student of Hanafi fatwa methodology that ikhtilaf among mujtahids is structural and temporal, not a free-for-all.

Key Terms
تعارض الأدلة (ta'arud al-adillah): Contradiction between two or more evidences (Quran, hadith, etc.) that cannot be reconciled normally.
رجوع (ru'ooj): A mujtahid's formal withdrawal from a previous legal opinion.
تحري (taharri): Deliberation and effort to determine the most likely correct ruling when evidences conflict and no external preference exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the effect of a mujtahid's return (ru'ooj) from an earlier opinion?
A) The earlier opinion is completely eliminated and no longer attributed to the mujtahid.
B) The earlier opinion remains as a narration but is not acted upon.
C) The earlier opinion remains equally valid and may be followed.
D) The earlier opinion becomes the basis for a new ruling.

Key Takeaway
A mujtahid's explicit return (ru'ooj) nullifies the earlier statement; without it, the earlier statement survives as a narration and is not automatically abrogated.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Six Causes of Ikhtilaf in Hanafi Narrations and Rulings
Enumerating and explaining causes for differing narrations and rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six causes of ikhtilaf in Hanafi narrations and rulings and explain why ta'arud al-adilla alone is insufficient.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaf in Hanafi rulings arises from six distinct causes, not mere conflict of evidences.

This passage from Sharh Rasm al-Mufti addresses a critical issue: how to understand conflicting narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa. It first contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam Shafi'i, then critiques the common usuli view that ta'arud al-adilla (conflict of proofs) is the sole cause. Instead, it presents six practical causes that explain why Imam Abu Hanifa may have multiple statements on a single issue. Understanding these causes is essential for a mufti to correctly navigate the Hanafi corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem of conflicting narrations
Note that the passage begins with a contrast between Hanafi and Shafi'i approaches to multiple sayings from an Imam. For Hanafis, two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa in one issue are usually from different times, so one is correct and the other not, but the later one may be unknown.
Shafi'is may accept both as valid choices without taharri.
2
Critique the ta'arud al-adilla explanation
Learn why Allama Shami finds the view that ta'arud is the only cause problematic: it would make both narrations unusable, contradicting actual practice where scholars prefer one.
This leads to the need for multiple causes.
3
Enumerate the six causes
Memorize the list: (1) error in hearing/understanding by narrators, (2) Imam's retraction not informed, (3) two rulings due to qiyas vs istihsan, (4) fatwa vs taqwa, (5) hesitation due to conflicting evidence, (6) probability in proof meaning.
Causes 1-2 are ikhtilaf al-riwaya; 3-6 are ikhtilaf al-aqwal.
4
Classify the causes into two categories
Understand the distinction: ikhtilaf al-riwaya involves transmission errors or incomplete knowledge; ikhtilaf al-aqwal involves multiple valid legal perspectives from the Imam.
This classification guides how a mufti handles each type.
5
Appreciate the practical implication for fatwa
Recognize that with multiple causes, both narrations may have a basis for fatwa, but one is usually preferred through tarjih.
The mufti does not suspend judgment but chooses based on strength of evidence.

اور علمائے کرام نے یہ بھی بیان کیا ہے کہ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کا ارشاد یہ ہے کہ: "مجتہد تحری کے بغیر بھی دو پہلوؤں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کر سکتا ہے۔ چنانچہ امام شافعی کے ہر مسئلہ میں دو یا زیادہ اقوال ہیں اور ہمارے ائمہ سے جو ایک مسئلہ میں دو روایتیں ہیں تو وہ دو وقتوں کی ہیں اس لیے ایک صحیح ہے اور دوسری صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ مگر ان میں سے بعد کی روایت معلوم نہیں ہے ( یعنی تعارض ادلہ شوافع کے نزدیک تو اختلاف اقوال کا سبب بن سکتا ہے مگر احناف کی تصریحات کے مطابق اس کی گنجائش نہیں ) ( التقریر والتحبير ج ۳ ص ۴ بحث تعارض ) بناء علی ہذا یہ جو کہا جاتا ہے کہ : " اس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب سے دو روایتیں ہیں یہ بات : آخری قول معلوم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کہی جاتی ہے اور جہاں یہ تعبیر آتی ہے کہ فی روایۃ عنہ کذا یعنی امام صاحب سے ایک روایت اس طرح ہے۔ یہ تعبیر وہاں اختیار کی جاتی ہے جہاں فقہاء کو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وہ بات امام صاحب کا پہلا قول ہے یا بایں وجہ یہ تعبیر اختیار کی جاتی ہے کہ امام صاحب کا وہ قول اصول کی کتابوں کے علاوہ دوسری کتابوں میں مذکور ہوتا ہے اور یہ دوسری بات اقرب الی الصواب ہے۔

علامہ شامی کی رائے :
لیکن یہ بات مخفی نہیں ہے کہ علماء نے تعارض ادلہ کی بحث میں جو بات بیان فرمائی ہے وہ نا قابل فہم ہے کیوں کہ اس سے یہ لازم آتا ہے کہ جس مسئلہ میں امام صاحب کی دو روایتیں ہوں اس میں کسی پر بھی عمل جائز نہ ہو۔ یہ بات معلوم نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے کہ ان میں سے کون سی روایت صحیح ہے اور کون سی باطل اور نہ ان دو باتوں میں سے کسی کی امام صاحب کی طرف نسبت درست ہو ۔ جیسا کہ بعض اصولیوں کے حوالہ سے یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے حالانکہ بے شمار مسائل میں دو روایتیں موجود ہیں ۔ اور علما ء ایک کو دوسری پر ترجیح دیتے ہیں ۔ اور اس رائج کو امام صاحب کی طرف منسوب بھی کرتے ہیں ۔ میں ظاہر وہی ہے جو امام بلیغی کے حوالہ سے پہلے گزر چکا کہ اختلاف روایات کی وجوہ متعدد قرار دی جائیں، صرف تعارض اولہ کو سبب نہ بنایا جائے۔ البتہ ان کی بیان کردہ وجوہ اربعہ کے ساتھ وہ دو نہیں بھی بڑھا دی جائیں جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہیں یعنی امام کا دو حکموں میں متردد ہوتا اور امام کی رائے میں دو احتمالوں کا ہوتا اور کسی دلیل یا تحری وغیرہ سے کسی ایک احتمال کو تریج حاصل نہ ہونا ( خوب غور کر لیں ) نیز یہ بات بھی مخفی نہیں ہے کہ اختلاف روایات کی یہ وجہ جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے گزشتہ وجوہ اراجہ سے زیادہ وسیع پیمانہ پر کار آمد ہو سکتی ہے کیونکہ وہ اس صورت کو بھی شامل ہے جس میں اختلاف قیاس داستحسان کی وجہ سے ہو یا فتوئی اور تقویٰ کی جہت سے ہو ۔
